CHAPTER 6
CITY OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
SECTION:
1-6-1: Appointments, Terms And Bonds
1-6-2: Salaries Of Appointive Officials
1-6-3: City Clerk-Treasurer
1-6-4: City Attorney
1-6-5: City Maintenance Supervisor
1-6-1: APPOINTMENTS, TERMS AND BONDS:
   A.   Officers Appointed: The mayor, with the consent of the city council,
shall appoint a clerk-treasurer, attorney, chief of the fire department, city
maintenance supervisor and other such officers as may be deemed advisable for
the efficient operation of the city. (1963 Code § 1-1001; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Term Of Office; Removal: All appointive officers shall hold office for
the term for which they were appointed and qualified; provided, that any
appointive officer may at any time be removed by the action of the majority of
the city council; provided further, that all employees holding positions by
virtue of appointment only may be removed and discharged at the pleasure of the
appointing power. (1963 Code § 1-1002)
   C.   Bonds Of Officers: The following officers shall give bonds to the city,
with two (2) or more sufficient sureties, in the penal sum as follows, provided
surety bonds may be furnished at the expense of the city in lieu of personal
bonds:
 
City clerk-treasurer:        $20,000.00
City maintenance supervisor: 10,000.00
(1963 Code § 1-1003; amd. 2010 Code)
1-6-2: SALARIES OF APPOINTIVE OFFICIALS:
The salaries or other remuneration of appointive officials shall be fixed by
resolution of the city council, unless their salaries are elsewhere provided
for in this code. (1963 Code § 1-702)
1-6-3: CITY CLERK-TREASURER:
   A.   Appointment: The mayor, with the consent of the city council, shall
appoint a clerk-treasurer who shall hold office for the duration of said
appointment or until such time as said person is removed from office by the
city council.
   B.   Duties: The clerk-treasurer shall have all the duties of the city clerk
and duties of the city treasurer as provided by state law, including but not
limited to Title 50, Idaho Code, as amended. In addition, the clerk-treasurer
shall have the following powers and duties:
      1.   Keep Seal, Ordinances And Records: The clerk-treasurer shall be
custodian of the seal and affix same to documents as provided. The clerk-
treasurer shall also be custodian of all public records, documents, ordinances,
resolutions and orders of the council, and such other papers and documents as
may be delivered into the clerk-treasurer’s custody.
      2.   Attend Council Meetings; Keep Minutes And Records: The clerk-
treasurer shall attend all sessions of the council, keep a correct journal and
shall keep in a separate book a record of ordinances passed by the council and
of the title of such ordinances; and all ordinances not published in book form
shall be carefully indexed alphabetically. The clerk-treasurer shall see that
each ordinance is published as required by law, and shall keep on file the
proof of such publication.
      3.   Funds, Records And Financial Duties:
         a.   Receive And Safely Keep Funds: It shall be the duty of the clerk-
treasurer to receive and safely keep in designated depositories, as required by
law, all monies or funds belonging to the city which may come into his hands;
to disburse the same upon an appropriation by ordinance or resolution of the
city council after audit and allowance by the city council of claims therefor,
and upon warrant of the mayor. Securities belonging to the city, incapable of
deposit in a checking account, shall be kept by the clerk-treasurer in a safety
deposit box in some banking institution designated by the city council. All
bonds or securities delivered to the clerk-treasurer by any designated
depository of city funds as security for such funds shall be deposited with the
county auditor or other public official as may be provided by law.
         b.   Keep Proper Books And Records: The clerk-treasurer shall keep in
a suitable book or books a full and accurate account of municipal money and
funds received by him, showing the date of the receipt thereof, the person from
whom received, on what account, and to what fund the same is credited, with the
date of disbursement, the person to whom disbursed, on what account and against
what fund.
         c.   Issue Duplicate Receipts For Money Received: The clerk-treasurer
shall execute and deliver to every officer or other person paying money or
funds into the treasury a receipt therefor specifying the date of payment, the
amount thereof and upon what fund or account the same is received.
         d.   Report To City Council:
            (1)   The clerk-treasurer shall prepare and present to the council
at its regular meeting each month a full and complete statement of the
financial transactions of the clerk-treasurer’s office during month preceding,
which said statement shall set forth: all receipts for licenses issued; money
received with applications for licenses which are to come before the council;
and all other funds received by him as clerk-treasurer; and said report shall
give a detailed explanation of disbursements redeemed including a statement of
the aggregate of warrants outstanding against each fund at the close of such
month.
            (2)   The clerk-treasurer shall also, at the close of each fiscal
year, present to the council an annual report covering the operations of the
entire year, which report shall contain a description of the bonds issued and
sold during the year, and the term of sale; and shall itemize each and every
expense thereof.
            (3)   The clerk-treasurer shall also make such additional report
and furnish such other data from the records and files of their office as may
be requested by the city council or be required by law.
            4.   Public Records - Designated Custodian: Unless otherwise
provided by resolution of the city council, the clerk-treasurer is hereby
designed as the custodian of all public records in the possession and control
of city for purposes of the Idaho Public Records Act, Chapter 1, Title 74,
Idaho Code, as amended, and the clerk-treasurer shall perform the duties of
said designated custodian respect to requests to inspect or copy public records
in the possession or control of city pursuant to said act.
            5.   Keep Books And Records: The clerk-treasurer shall keep such
books and permanent records of the transactions and business of the clerk-
treasurer’s office as may be necessary to accurately disclose all transactions
and business of said office. The clerk-treasurer shall also countersign all
warrants, and keep a "Warrant Register And Abstract Of Expenditures", showing
the number and amount of warrants issued and the person to whom issued, the
date redeemed, the interest paid, and the several funds against which each of
said warrants is drawn.
            6.   Issue Licenses And Permits: The clerk-treasurer shall
administer the issuance of all city licenses and permits issued by city as
required under this code or applicable ordinance, a duplicate of which shall be
kept on file, but no license or permit shall be issued to any person unless
fees and charges fixed by law shall have first been paid, for which payment the
clerk-treasurer shall issue a receipt in duplicate. The clerk-treasurer shall
endorse upon the receipt and duplicate receipt the number of the license permit
issued, the number of the application for license or permit, and the duplicate
of such receipt so issued shall be kept on file with the duplicate license or
permit.
            7.   Keep Record Of Municipal Bonds: The clerk-treasurer shall keep
records of outstanding bonds of the city, showing the number and amount of
each, for what and to whom said bonds were issued; and when any of said bonds
are purchased or paid or cancelled, said record shall show the fact; and in the
clerk- treasurer’s report at the close of each fiscal year, the clerk-treasurer
shall describe particularly the bonds issued and sold during the year, the
terms of sale, and itemize each and every expense thereof.
            8.   Warrants: The clerk-treasurer shall duly administer the
processing and payments of all city warrants as provided by state law.
            9.   Claims: The clerk-treasurer shall duly present all claims
filed with the city to the city council for consideration as provided by state
law.
            10.   Attest Documents: The clerk-treasurer, when authorized and
directed by the city council, shall attest and place the city seal officially
and in behalf of the city on all contracts, including deeds, bonds, bills,
notes, obligations and other agreements, ordinances, documents and papers to
which the city is a party, and where required, shall prepare certified copies
of the same.
            11.   Deliver Books And Papers To Successor: The clerk-treasurer
shall deliver to the clerk-treasurer’s successor in office all books, monies,
papers and other property pertaining to said office.
            12.   Publish Quarterly Reports Of Receipts And Expenditures: It
shall be the duty of the clerk-treasurer to cause to be published for at least
one insertion in some newspaper of general circulation in the city, between the
first and third Mondays of May, August, November and February of each and every
year a full statement of the receipts and expenditures of the city, giving the
source from which received, to what purpose applied and to whom paid.
            13.   Collect All Monies: The clerk-treasurer shall receive, and
all officers or other persons shall forthwith pay to, the clerk-treasurer,
except as otherwise provided by this code, all monies due the city on any
account whatsoever.
            14.   Monthly Report To Council: The clerk-treasurer shall at the
end of each and every month, and at other times when required by the city
council, render an account, including a showing, under oath, the condition of
the treasury at the date of such account, including in said statement the
balance of money in the treasury with a detailed statement of the specified
amount in each designated depository and of the amount and class of security
held to guarantee such deposit. Such account shall also contain a statement of
receipts and disbursements and of all warrants redeemed and paid by the clerk-
treasurer, which said warrants, with all vouchers held by the clerk-treasurer,
shall be filed with any and all books or papers in the office of the clerk-
treasurer for the purpose of inspection or examination. (Ord. 286, 9-5-1978;
amd. 2010 Code; Ord. 444, 4-2-2024)
1-6-4: CITY ATTORNEY:
   A.   Appointment: The mayor, with the consent of the city council, shall
appoint a city attorney who shall hold office for the duration of his
appointment or until such time as he shall be removed by the city council.
(1963 Code § 1-1201; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Duties: The city attorney shall be the legal advisor to the city and
shall have such other duties as provided for city attorneys under state law,
including but not limited to as provided in Chapter 2, Title 50, Idaho Code, as
amended.
      1.   The city attorney shall be the legal advisor of the council.
      2.   He shall commence, prosecute and defend all suits and actions
necessary to be commenced, prosecuted or defended on behalf of the city, or
that may be ordered by the council.
      3.   When requested, he shall attend meetings of the council and give
them his opinion upon any matters submitted to him. (1963 Code § 1-1202; amd.
Ord. 444, 4-2-2024)
1-6-5: CITY MAINTENANCE SUPERVISOR:
   A.   Appointment: The mayor, with the consent of the city council, may
appoint a city maintenance supervisor who shall hold office for the duration of
his appointment or until such time as he shall be removed by the city council.
(1963 Code § 1-1401; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Duties: The city maintenance supervisor shall have charge of the
superintending of all municipal work as follows:
      1.   Streets And Alleys: He shall supervise the grading, surfacing,
repairs and maintenance of all streets and alleys.
      2.   Sewer: He shall supervise the installation and maintenance of all
sewer lines in the city, except the installation of sewer projects which are
accomplished by contract.
      3.   Water: He shall supervise the installation and maintenance of all
water mains and water services, except the installation of water mains so
accomplished by contract.
      4.   Parks: He shall have charge of the care and maintenance of the
municipal parks.
      5.   Equipment: He shall have charge of and supervise the repair and
upkeep of all municipal works equipment.
      6.   Employment And Supervision: He may employ, with the consent of the
city council, such help as is needed to carry on the work of the city, such
help to be directly under the supervision of his office.
      7.   Other Duties: The supervisor shall be responsible for the
accomplishment of such other work of the city which the city council may from
time to time assign to him.
      8.   Make Report: The supervisor shall present to the city council at its
regular meeting each month a written report of the municipal work accomplished
the preceding month and also, as far as can be foreseen, municipal work planned
for the current month. (1963 Code § 1-1402; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 7
MUNICIPAL FINANCES
SECTION:
1-7-1: Depository
1-7-2: Funds And Accounts
1-7-1: DEPOSITORY:
The city council may by resolution designated one or more depositories for the
deposit and safe keeping of city funds consistent with state law. Unless
otherwise directed by the city council or provided by law, the clerk-treasurer
shall keep monies belonging to or in the care of the city coming into the
clerk-treasurer’s possession or control in the depository(ies) so designated by
the city council. (1963 Code § 1-601; amd. 2010 Code; Ord. 435, 5-2-2023; Ord.
444, 4-2-2024)
1-7-2: FUNDS AND ACCOUNTS:
   A.   Capitalization Of Fixed Assets And Fixed Asset Inventory Maintenance: A
policy has been established by the city for the following purposes:
      1.   Capitalization of fixed assets; and
      2.   A process for maintaining fixed assets inventory.
   B.   Sewer Revenue Account: The city clerk-treasurer is hereby authorized to
open a separate account at the Wells Fargo Bank N.A., Craigmont, Idaho, or its
successor, or at such other depository(ies) directed by the city council, to
deposit all sewer revenues generated by the sewer system.
   C.   The city shall have a minimum of four funds:
      1.   Water fund;
      2.   Wastewater fund;
      3.   Sanitation fund; and
      4.   General fund:
         a.   All other expenses not covered in water, wastewater, or sewer
funds. (Ord. 326, 8-1-1989; amd. 2010 Code; Ord. 435, 5-2-2023; Ord. 444, 4-2-
2024)
CHAPTER 8
MISCELLANEOUS ADMINISTRATIVE PROVISIONS
SECTION:
1-8-1: Corporate Seal
1-8-2: Official Newspaper
1-8-1: CORPORATE SEAL:
   A.   Design: The common, corporate and official seal of the city shall be
circular in form with inner and outer circles. The outer circle shall be one
and one-half inches (11/2") in diameter, and the inner circle shall be one inch
(1") in diameter. It shall bear upon the upper portion of space between the two
(2) circles, the words "City of Craigmont, Idaho". Upon the upper space within
the inner circle, and upon the upper portion thereof, shall be inscribed the
word "Incorporated", and upon the lower portion of the space within the inner
circle shall be the words "June 17, 1920". Upon and across the center of the
space within the inner circle, shall be the word "Seal". (1963 Code § 1-401;
amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Adoption: The seal described in subsection A of this section is hereby
adopted as the official common and corporate seal of the city. (1963 Code § 1-
402)
   C.   Custody Of Seal: The city clerk-treasurer shall be the custodian of the
corporate seal of the city, and shall affix said seal imprint upon all official
city documents, records and licenses. (1963 Code § 1-403)
1-8-2: OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER:
The "Lewis County Herald", a weekly newspaper printed and published in Lewis
County, and a newspaper of general circulation in the city, is hereby
appointed, designated and constituted the official newspaper of the city, and
such writings as are required under and by virtue of the city council to be
given publication in a newspaper shall be published in said newspaper. (1963
Code § 1-501; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 9
CITY HALL RENTAL
SECTION:
1-9-1: Rental Authorized
1-9-2: Rental Fees
1-9-1: RENTAL AUTHORIZED:
The assembly rooms and kitchen of the city hall may be rented to public or
business organizations or individuals upon proper application being made to the
city clerk-treasurer, and the payment of the appropriate rental fees. The city
hall shall be made available for use by such organizations or individuals,
either separately or in conjunction with the use of other rooms, only by
specific authorization of the city council. (Ord. 239, 8-12-1969)
1-9-2: RENTAL FEES:
   A.   Time Of Payment: Rental fees for the use of the city hall shall be paid
in advance and upon the making of the application for rental, when the rental
period desired is one month or less. If a period of rental for longer than one
month is desired, the first month's rental shall be payable in advance, and
each succeeding month's rental shall be due and payable to the clerk-treasurer
on the first day of the month preceding use.
   B.   Payment Of Fees; Waivers; Responsibility For Damages:
      1.   Rental fees shall be set and determined by resolution of the mayor
and city council. The city council may waive any rental fee, or any portion
thereof, for any particular user or use the city hall if the city council
determines that such waiver is in the best interest of the city.
      2.   Any organization or individual using any room in the city hall shall
be responsible for any damages to said room or its contents, and shall be
responsible for cleaning said room immediately after each use.
      3.   The city shall pay all normal utility fees and heating expenses
during the rental period. (Ord. 239, 8-12-1969; amd. Ord. 325, 5-2-1989; 2010
Code; Ord. 444, 4-2-2024)
CHAPTER 10
AREA OF CITY IMPACT
SECTION:
1-10-1: Purpose
1-10-2: Geographic Area Of City Impact
1-10-3: Comprehensive Plan And Zoning Ordinance
1-10-4: Subdivision Ordinance
1-10-5: Council Review And Comment; Approval
1-10-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of establishing an area of city impact is to identify a logical
fringe area adjoining the city. The fringe area includes the unincorporated
area surrounding Craigmont that has a potential for development that could
affect the provision of public services or the quality of life in Craigmont.
(Ord. 289, 12-5-1978)
1-10-2: GEOGRAPHIC AREA OF CITY IMPACT:
The officially adopted geographic area of city impact includes all
unincorporated land within the southern 1/2 of Sections 27, 28, and 29, and SE
1/4 of Section 30, the eastern 1/2 of Section 31, all of Sections 32, 33, and
34 in T.34N., R.1W.; and within the eastern 1/2 of Section 6, all of Sections
3, 4, and 5 in T.33N., R.1W. All parcels of land, or portions thereof, lying
within the area of city impact shall be subject to provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 289, 12-5-1978)
1-10-3: COMPREHENSIVE PLAN AND ZONING ORDINANCE:
The comprehensive plan and the zoning ordinance, and subsequent amendments
thereto, as officially adopted by the board of county commissioners, Lewis
County, Idaho, shall apply to the area of city impact. (Ord. 289, 12-5-1978)
1-10-4: SUBDIVISION ORDINANCE:
Pursuant to Idaho Code sections 50-1306 and 50-1308, the subdivision ordinance,
and subsequent amendments thereto, as officially adopted by the city council,
shall apply to all plats situated within one mile outside the city limits. The
subdivision ordinance, and subsequent amendments thereto, as officially adopted
by the board of county commissioners, shall apply to all other plats situated
within the area of city impact. (Ord. 289, 12-5-1978)
1-10-5: COUNCIL REVIEW AND COMMENT; APPROVAL:
Any request for development, zone change, conditional use permit, or variance
within the area of city impact shall be referred to the city council for review
and comment. The city council shall have forty (40) days to consider the
request and submit a reply to the board of county commissioners. If no reply is
received by the board within the forty (40) day period, the city council
forfeits its right to comment on the request, and processing shall continue
under the board's administration. Both the city council and board shall approve
all subdivision plats within the area of city impact, pursuant to Idaho Code
sections 50-1306 and 50-1308. (Ord. 289, 12-5-1978)
TITLE 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
Planning And Zoning Commission   1
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-1-1: Commission Established; Membership, Duties
2-1-1: COMMISSION ESTABLISHED; MEMBERSHIP, DUTIES:
Those members duly constituted as members of the city council shall exercise
and be charged with all rights, obligations and duties as set forth in Idaho
Code title 67, chapter 65, relating to planning and zoning affecting the city.
Said city council shall exercise all of the powers required and authorized by
Idaho Code section 67-6504, in lieu of the appointment of a planning and zoning
commission. (2010 Code)
TITLE 3
BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS
General Licensing Provisions   1
Liquor, Beer And Wine   2
Liquor By The Drink   2A
Beer   2B
Wine   2C
Peddlers, Solicitors And Transient Merchants   3
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL LICENSING PROVISIONS
SECTION:
3-1-1: Applications
3-1-2: Persons Subject To License
3-1-3: Forms
3-1-4: Signatures
3-1-5: Inspections Or Investigations
3-1-6: Term Of License
3-1-7: Building And Premises
3-1-8: Change Of Location
3-1-9: Nuisances
3-1-10: Posting Of License
3-1-11: Revocation Of License Or Permit; Hearing
3-1-12: Appeal Procedure
3-1-1: APPLICATIONS:
Applications for all licenses and permits required by this code shall be made
in writing to the city clerk-treasurer or his designee, unless otherwise
specifically provided by law. Each application shall state the name of the
applicant, the permit or license desired, the location to be used, if any, the
time covered and the fee to be paid; and each application shall contain such
additional information as may be required by the issuing official. (2010 Code)
3-1-2: PERSONS SUBJECT TO LICENSE:
Whenever in this code a license is required for the maintenance, operation or
conduct of any business or establishment or for doing business or engaging in
any activity or occupation, any person or corporation shall be subject to this
requirement if by himself or through an agent, employee or partner, he holds
himself forth as being engaged in the business or occupation; or solicits
patronage therefor, actively or passively; or performs or attempts to perform
any part of such business or occupation in the city. (2010 Code)
3-1-3: FORMS:
Forms for all licenses and permits, and applications therefor, shall be
prepared and kept on file by the city clerk-treasurer or his designee. (2010
Code)
3-1-4: SIGNATURES:
Each license or permit issued shall bear the signature of the city clerk-
treasurer or his designee in the absence of any provision to the contrary.
(2010 Code)
3-1-5: INSPECTIONS OR INVESTIGATIONS:
Upon the receipt of an application for a license or permit, where laws of the
city necessitate an inspection or investigation before the issuance of such
permit or license, the city clerk- treasurer or his designee shall refer such
application to the proper officer for making such investigation within forty
eight (48) hours of the time of such receipt. The officer charged with the duty
of making the investigation or inspection shall make a report thereon,
favorable or otherwise, within ten (10) days after receiving the application or
a copy thereof. (2010 Code)
3-1-6: TERM OF LICENSE:
All annual licenses shall terminate on December 31, where no provision to the
contrary is made. (2010 Code)
3-1-7: BUILDING AND PREMISES:
No license shall be issued for the conduct of any business and no permit shall
be issued for any thing or act if the premises and building to be used for the
purpose do not fully comply with the requirements of the city. (2010 Code)
3-1-8: CHANGE OF LOCATION:
In the absence of any provision to the contrary, the location of any licensed
business or occupation or of any permitted act may be changed, provided ten
(10) days' notice thereof is given to the city clerk-treasurer or his designee;
and further provided, that the building requirements of this code are complied
with. (2010 Code)
3-1-9: NUISANCES:
No business, licensed or not, shall be conducted or operated as to amount to a
nuisance in fact. (2010 Code)
3-1-10: POSTING OF LICENSE:
It shall be the duty of any person conducting a licensed business in the city
to keep his license posted at all times in a prominent place on the premises
used for such business. (2010 Code)
3-1-11: REVOCATION OF LICENSE OR PERMIT; HEARING:
   A.   City Authority: Any license or permit, for a limited time, may be
revoked by the city council during the life of such license or permit for the
violation by the licensee or permittee of any provision relating to the license
or permit, the subject of the license or permit, or the premises occupied; such
revocation may be in addition to any fine imposed. The city council shall be
authorized to summarily order the cessation of business, the closing of the
premises, and the suspension of any business license or permit for a period not
to exceed fifteen (15) days.
   B.   Hearing: Within ten (10) days after the city officials have so acted,
the mayor shall call a hearing for the purpose of determining whether or not
the license or permit should be revoked.
   C.   Notice Of Hearing: Notice of hearing for revocation of a license or
permit shall be given in writing setting forth specifically the grounds of the
complaint and the time and place of hearing. Such notice shall be sent to the
licensee or permittee by certified mail at his last known address or personally
served at least five (5) days prior to the date of the hearing.
   D.   Hearing Procedure: At the hearing, the licensee or permittee shall be
permitted counsel and shall have the right to submit evidence and cross examine
witnesses. The mayor shall preside over the city council who will render the
decision and recommendation.
   E.   Causes For Revocation: Business licenses and permits issued under the
ordinances of the city, unless otherwise provided, may be revoked by the city
council after notice and hearing as provided in subsections C and D of this
section for any of the following causes:
      1.   Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement contained in the
application for the license or permit.
      2.   Any violation by the licensee or permittee of ordinance provisions
or state law relating to the license or permit, the subject matter of the
license or permit, or the premises occupied.
      3.   Conviction of the licensee or permittee of any felony or of a
misdemeanor involving moral turpitude.
      4.   Failure of the licensee or permittee to pay any fine or penalty
owing to the city.
      5.   Refusal to permit an inspection or investigation or any interference
with a duly authorized city officer or employee while in the performance of his
duties in making such inspections, as provided in this code. (2010 Code)
3-1-12: APPEAL PROCEDURE:
   A.   Right To Appeal: Any applicant aggrieved by the refusal of the city to
issue a license or permit or by the revocation of a license or permit shall
have the right to appeal the city's decision to the city council. Such appeal
shall be requested by submitting a written request to the mayor within five (5)
days of the action of the city which is appealed.
   B.   Council Consideration: The city council shall consider the appeal at
its next regularly scheduled meeting, at which time the applicant shall be
entitled to present his appeal orally or in writing. The city council shall act
on the appeal within seven (7) days of the hearing and shall either uphold the
action of the city or shall direct the issuance of a license or permit which
the city has denied or the reissuance of a license or permit which the city had
revoked. (2010 Code)
CHAPTER 2
LIQUOR, BEER AND WINE
ARTICLE A. LIQUOR BY THE DRINK
SECTION:
3-2A-1: Purpose
3-2A-2: Definitions
3-2A-3: License Issuance; Conditions And Restrictions
3-2A-4: Application For License
3-2A-5: Investigation Of Applicant
3-2A-6: Form Of License
3-2A-7: Transfer Of License; Fee
3-2A-8: License Fee; Term Of License
3-2A-9: Premises And Location Requirements
3-2A-10: Hours Of Sale
3-2A-11: Gambling Prohibited
3-2A-12: Restrictions On Sales By Licensee
3-2A-13: Purchases By Unqualified Persons
3-2A-14: Intoxicated Persons
3-2A-15: Restrictions On Sales And Advertising
3-2A-16: Unlicensed Rooms Unlawful
3-2A-17: License Revocation Or Cancellation
3-2A-18: Certification Of Conviction
3-2A-1: PURPOSE:
The mayor and city council may issue licenses to qualified applicants as herein
provided, whereby the licensee shall be authorized and permitted to sell liquor
by the drink at retail within the city; and, upon the issuance of such license,
the licensee therein named shall be authorized to sell liquor by the drink at
retail in the city in accordance with the provisions of this article and the
terms and provisions of Idaho Code section 23-901 et seq., as amended. (1963
Code § 5-401; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2A-2: DEFINITIONS:
All terms, words and phrases used in this article, and not herein specifically
defined, but defined in Idaho Code section 23-902, as amended, shall be given
the meanings set out in said statute. (1963 Code § 5-424; amd. 2010 Code)
All words and phrases used in this article, the definition of which is not
given in this section, shall be given the ordinary and commonly understood and
accepted meaning.
The following words and phrases used in this article shall be given the
following interpretations:
INTERDICTED PERSON: A person to whom the sale of liquor is prohibited under the
laws of the state of Idaho and this article.
LICENSE: A license issued by the city to a qualified person under which it
shall be lawful for the licensee to sell and dispense liquor by the drink at
retail as provided by this article and as provided by law.
LICENSEE: A person to whom a license is issued under the provisions of this
article.
LIQUOR: All kinds of liquor sold by and in a state liquor store of the state of
Idaho.
PERSON: Every individual, partnership, corporation, organization or association
holding a state retail liquor license, whether conducting the business
singularly or collectively. (1963 Code § 5-402)
3-2A-3: LICENSE ISSUANCE; CONDITIONS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Issuance To State Licensees: The clerk-treasurer, upon the approval of
the city council, is hereby authorized and directed to issue licenses to
qualified applicants to whom licenses to sell retail liquor by the drink shall
have been issued by the director of Idaho state police. (1963 Code § 5-403;
amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Separate Licenses: Every license issued under the provisions of this
article is separate and distinct and no person except the licensee therein
named shall exercise any of the privileges granted thereunder. (1963 Code § 5-
408)
   C.   Applicable To Premises Only: All licenses issued under the provisions
of this article shall be applicable only to the premises in respect to which
they have been issued. (1963 Code § 5-409)
   D.   Disqualified Persons: No license shall be issued to any person, firm,
corporation, association or other group defined as not being qualified to be
licensed under the provisions of Idaho Code section 23-910. (1963 Code § 5-411;
amd. 2010 Code)
3-2A-4: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Each applicant for a license shall file with the city clerk- treasurer an
application, in writing, setting forth the following facts:
   A.   That he is the lawful holder of a license issued by the director of
Idaho state police pursuant to the provisions of Idaho Code section 23-901 et
seq., as amended, and the licensee shall also present a copy of the state
license. (1963 Code § 5-404; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Description of premises for which license is sought and its location,
and the name of the owner of said premises; such description shall set forth as
a fact that there are windows and/or doors to said premises on the street side
thereof, and that such windows and/or doors have clear window glass therein
permitting an unobstructed view of the interior of said premises from the
abutting street, except when the same are covered by blinds or shades.
   C.   The names and addresses of all persons who will have any financial
interest in any business to be carried on in and/or upon the licensed premises,
whether such interest results from open loans, mortgages, conditional sales
contracts, silent partnerships, trusts or any other basis than open trade
accounts incurred in the ordinary course of business, and the amount of such
interest.
   D.   If the premises described in the license application are not owned by
the applicant, the application shall be accompanied by a certificate of the
owner of the premises expressing such owner's consent to the sale of liquor by
the drink on such premises.
   E.   The name and address of the applicant, which shall include all members
of a partnership or association and the officers and members of the governing
board of a corporation. (1963 Code § 5-404)
   F.   If, during the period of any license issued hereunder, any change shall
take place in any of the requirements of subsections A through E of this
section, the licensee shall forthwith make a report of such change to the city
clerk-treasurer. (1963 Code § 5-404; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2A-5: INVESTIGATION OF APPLICANT:
Upon the receipt of an application for a license under this article,
accompanied by the necessary license fee, the city council may make such
investigation of all matters pertaining thereto as it shall deem proper. If the
council shall determine that the contents of the application are true, that
such applicant is qualified to receive a license, that his premises are
suitable for the carrying on of the intended business, and that the
requirements of this article have been met and complied with, a license shall
be issued; otherwise the application shall be denied and the license fee
returned. (1963 Code § 5-405)
3-2A-6: FORM OF LICENSE:
Every license issued under this article shall set forth the name of the person
to whom issued, the location by street and number, or other definite
designation of the premises; if issued to a partnership, the names of the
persons constituting the partnership shall be therein set forth; if issued to a
corporation or association, the names of the principal officers and the
governing board shall be therein set forth. Such license shall be signed by the
licensee. (1963 Code § 5-406)
3-2A-7: TRANSFER OF LICENSE; FEE:
A license issued under the provisions of this article shall be transferable
upon the payment of a transfer fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) to the city clerk-
treasurer. (Ord. 291, 3-6-1979; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2A-8: LICENSE FEE; TERM OF LICENSE:
   A.   Fee: Each licensee to whom a license is issued under the provisions of
this article shall pay to the city in advance an annual license fee of two
hundred twenty five dollars ($225.00). (Ord. 391, 3-8-2005)
   B.   Term: All licenses hereunder shall expire annually upon the date the
corresponding state license expires. The license fee shall be for an entire
year, and shall not be prorated but shall be paid in full at the beginning of
each year. (Ord. 391, 3-8-2005; amd. 2010 Code)
   C.   Refund: No refund shall be allowed for any cancelled, revoked or unused
license. No refund or discount of an annual license fee shall be granted or
allowed for any year. (Ord. 391, 3-8-2005)
3-2A-9: PREMISES AND LOCATION REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Sanitation: All licensed premises shall be maintained in sanitary
condition according to the requirements of Idaho department of health and
welfare licensing requirements, as amended. (1963 Code § 5-412; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Location Restrictions; Exceptions: No license shall be issued for any
premises in any neighborhood which is predominantly residential or within three
hundred feet (300') of any public school, church, or any other place of
worship, measured in a straight line to the nearest entrance of the licensed
premises, except with the approval of the city council; provided, that this
limitation shall not apply to any duly licensed premises that at the time of
licensing did not come within the restricted area, but subsequent to licensing
came therein. (1963 Code § 5-413; amd. 2010 Code)
   C.   Examination Of Premises: Any law enforcement officer shall have the
right at any time to make an examination of the premises of any licensee to
ascertain whether the laws of the state of Idaho and the ordinances of the city
are being complied with, and it shall be unlawful to refuse any such officer
the right of admittance or access to such premises. (1963 Code § 5-421)
3-2A-10: HOURS OF SALE:
No liquor shall be sold, offered for sale, or given away upon any licensed
premises during the following hours:
   A.   Memorial Day, Thanksgiving Day and Christmas Day from one o'clock (1:
00) A.M. to ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. on the following day.
   B.   On any other day between two o'clock (2:00) A.M. to ten o'clock (10:00)
A.M. (Ord. 345, 6-4-1991)
   C.   On any day of a general, primary or municipal election until after the
time when the polls are closed. (1963 Code § 5-415)
3-2A-11: GAMBLING PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any licensee to permit, conduct, play, carry on, open
or cause to be opened any gaming in or upon licensed premises or in or upon any
premises directly connected by door, hallway or other means of access from the
licensed premises, except such forms of gaming as are authorized by the laws of
the state of Idaho and the ordinances of the city. (1963 Code § 5-416)
3-2A-12: RESTRICTIONS ON SALES BY LICENSEE:
No licensee or his or its employees, agents, servants or bartenders shall sell,
deliver or give away, or cause or permit to be sold, delivered or given away
any liquor to:
   A.   Any person under the age of twenty one (21) years.
   B.   Any person actually, apparently or obviously intoxicated.
   C.   Any habitual drunkard.
   D.   An interdicted person. (1963 Code § 5-417; amd. Ord. 256, 6-13-1972;
2010 Code)
3-2A-13: PURCHASES BY UNQUALIFIED PERSONS:
Any person under the age of twenty one (21) years, or other person who
knowingly misrepresents his or her qualifications for the purpose of obtaining
liquor from such licensee shall be equally guilty with such licensee and shall,
upon conviction thereof, be guilty of a misdemeanor. (1963 Code § 5-418; amd.
Ord. 256, 6-13-1972; 2010 Code)
3-2A-14: INTOXICATED PERSONS:
No intoxicated person shall be permitted to remain in, loiter or loaf in the
place of business of any licensee, and the licensee and his agents, servants or
bartenders shall give any and all necessary and required assistance to any law
enforcement officer of the city, the county or state in evicting and removing
said person from the premises. (1963 Code § 5-419)
3-2A-15: RESTRICTIONS ON SALES AND ADVERTISING:
   A.   Liquor In Original Containers: It shall be unlawful for any licensee to
sell, keep for sale, dispense, give away or otherwise dispose of any liquor in
the original containers or otherwise than by retail sale by the drink for
consumption only upon the licensed premises.
   B.   Liquor Purchased From State Liquor Dispensary: No liquor shall be sold
by any licensee, except the same which has been purchased by the licensee from
the Idaho liquor dispensary through its regular retail stores and distributors.
   C.   Advertising: It shall be unlawful for any licensee to adopt or use any
name, sign or advertisement outside of the licensed premises advertising the
handling or sale of liquor therein. (1963 Code § 5-420)
3-2A-16: UNLICENSED ROOMS UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or maintain any room or premises in
which liquor is received or kept, whether owned by such person or by another,
or to which liquor is brought, for consumption on the premises by members of
the public or of any club, incorporated or unincorporated, or a corporation or
association, unless such person and the premises are licensed under this
article. (1963 Code § 5-422)
3-2A-17: LICENSE REVOCATION OR CANCELLATION:
The right shall be, and at all times shall remain, vested in the city council
to revoke or cancel the license of any person licensed hereunder for any
violation of this article; and upon verified complaint filed with the council,
the council shall, by written notice, cause such alleged offender to appear
before said council and be heard upon said complaint. A copy of such complaint
shall be served with such notice, and the day and hour of the hearing, which
shall be at least five (5) days from the serving of such complaint, shall be
specified in such notice, and such hearing shall be had in the city hall,
unless a different place shall be specified in such notice. If at said hearing,
upon the taking of evidence on behalf of the city and such alleged offender, it
shall appear to the council that cause exists for the cancellation or
revocation of such license, the same may be cancelled or revoked without
further process of law. Upon such cancellation or revocation, no refund of any
unexpired portion of the license fee shall be made to the licensee; and the
fact of such revocation shall immediately be certified to the director of Idaho
state police by the city clerk-treasurer, and if any conviction is had
hereunder, a certified copy of the judgment therein shall be immediately
certified to said director. (1963 Code § 5-423; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2A-18: CERTIFICATION OF CONVICTION:
Upon the conviction of any licensee of any provision of this article, the city
clerk-treasurer shall forthwith certify a copy of said conviction and forward
the same to the director of Idaho state police. (1963 Code § 5-425; amd. 2010
Code)
ARTICLE B. BEER
SECTION:
3-2B-1: Definitions
3-2B-2: Alcohol Content
3-2B-3: Licensing Requirements
3-2B-4: Application For License
3-2B-5: Qualifications Of Licensee
3-2B-6: License Fees; Term Of License
3-2B-7: Transfer Of License; Fee
3-2B-8: Power To Refuse, Revoke And Investigate
3-2B-9: Restrictions On Sales By Licensees
3-2B-10: Beer Consumption In Public Places
3-2B-11: Beer Sales At Certain Places Prohibited
3-2B-12: Hours Of Sale; View Into Premises
3-2B-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this article, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
BEER: Any beverage obtained by the alcoholic fermentation of an infusion or
decoction of barley, malt, and/or other ingredients in drinkable water.
RETAILER: Any person licensed to sell beer to the consumer at the premises
described in the license.
YEAR: A calendar year. (1963 Code § 5-301; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2B-2: ALCOHOL CONTENT:
Beer, as defined in Idaho Code section 23-1001, may be sold and distributed at
retail in the city under the conditions prescribed in this article and not
otherwise. (1963 Code § 5-302; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2B-3: LICENSING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or
corporation to sell beer, or offer beer for sale at retail to the consumer
without first obtaining a license therefor from the city, and a separate
license shall be required for each place of business where beer is sold. (1963
Code § 5-303)
   B.   Posting Of License: It shall be the duty of each person to whom a
license is issued under this article to keep the same displayed in a
conspicuous place within the premises for which issued. (1963 Code § 5-309)
   C.   Fractional Licenses: No fractional or part year licenses shall be
issued. (1963 Code § 5-310)
3-2B-4: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
All applications for licenses shall be in writing and filed with the city
clerk-treasurer upon forms to be furnished by said clerk-treasurer, and such
application shall be accompanied by the license fee prescribed therein, and
shall specify:
   A.   The name, age and citizenship of the applicant if an individual; and if
a corporation, the name of the state or county in which incorporated, its
principal place of business, together with its principal place of business in
Idaho, and the names and places of residence of its designated agent in Idaho;
and if a partnership, the names and residences of all partners.
   B.   If the application is made by an individual, a statement as to whether
or not he is a citizen of the United States, and if so, when and where born; if
a naturalized citizen, the time and place where he was naturalized.
   C.   Length of time the applicant has resided in the city, and if a
corporation, when and where it first commenced to do business in Idaho.
   D.   The name and location of the business place to be operated under the
license.
   E.   A statement that the applicant possesses all of the qualifications for
obtaining such license as prescribed by this article. (1963 Code § 5-304)
3-2B-5: QUALIFICATIONS OF LICENSEE:
   A.   No retail license shall be issued to an applicant who:
      1.   Is not a person of good moral character and/or repute, and twenty
one (21) years of age or older.
      2.   Is not a citizen of the United States, or has not been a bona fide
resident of the state of Idaho for a period of thirty (30) days prior to the
date of making application.
      3.   Shall have been convicted for violation of any law of the state of
Idaho or the United States of America or of this city regulating, governing or
prohibiting the sale of alcoholic beverages, or intoxicating liquor; provided,
however, in case the applicant is a partnership, the requirements relative to
residence shall be deemed satisfied when any member of the partnership or the
actual manager thereof has been a bona fide resident of the state for a period
of thirty (30) days prior to the date of making such application, and if the
applicant is a corporation, such corporation shall be qualified to do business
within the state, and the manager of such business place shall be such citizen
and shall have been such resident.
   B.   Furthermore, no person shall be permitted to receive or hold a license
under this article for use in connection with any business not under the
personal supervision, management and control of said person to whom said
license is issued. (Ord. 238, 7-1-1969)
3-2B-6: LICENSE FEES; TERM OF LICENSE:
   A.   Fees Enumerated; License Term:
      1.   The annual license fee for the year 2005-2006 and following years
shall be as follows:
         a.   The license fee for any retailer selling beer, any of which is
consumed or to be consumed on the premises where sold, shall be seventy five
dollars ($75.00) per year or any part thereof.
         b.   The license fee for any retailer selling beer, none of which is
consumed or to be consumed on the premises where sold, is hereby fixed at forty
dollars ($40.00) per year or any part thereof. (Ord. 390, 3-8-2005)
      2.   All licenses issued under the provisions of this article shall
expire concurrently with the state license issued. (Ord. 390, 3-8-2005; amd.
2010 Code)
   B.   Refunds: No refunds shall be allowed for any cancelled, revoked or
unused license. (1963 Code § 5-311)
3-2B-7: TRANSFER OF LICENSE; FEE:
A license granted under the provisions of this article shall be transferable
upon the payment of a transfer fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00) to the city
clerk-treasurer. (Ord. 291, 3-6-1979; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2B-8: POWER TO REFUSE, REVOKE AND INVESTIGATE:
   A.   Council Authority: The city council shall have the power to refuse a
license to any applicant, and/or revoke a license at any time when in the
judgment of the said council the business interests and the welfare of the
city, and/or the inhabitants thereof, will be best served by the denial or
revocation thereof; and for the purpose of ascertaining whether or not any
licensee is conforming with this article or any other provisions of the city
code, as well as the laws of the state, the law enforcement official shall have
the right, at all reasonable times, to inspect the places where beer is sold
under the licenses issued. Provided further, that any license issued under the
provisions of this article shall be forfeited, cancelled and revoked by order
of the council if, after the issuance thereof, and during the period for which
said license shall have been issued, the holder thereof shall fail to possess
all the qualifications enumerated as prerequisites to the obtaining of such
license. The city clerk-treasurer, upon such revocation, shall, in writing,
send by United States certified mail, a notification to the other issuers of
other retailer's license to such licensee, stating sufficient facts for
identification of the licensee, and the grounds and date of such revocation.
   B.   Investigation: No license shall be issued by the city clerk- treasurer
until each applicant has been properly and adequately investigated by the law
enforcement official, and the prior approval of the city council has been
obtained. (1963 Code § 5-312)
3-2B-9: RESTRICTIONS ON SALES BY LICENSEES:
It shall be unlawful to sell or serve beer to any person under the age of
twenty one (21) years, or to any person or classes of persons to whom the sale
of beer is prohibited by the state of Idaho or the United States of America.
(1963 Code § 5-313; amd. Ord. 255, 6-13-1972; 2010 Code)
3-2B-10: BEER CONSUMPTION IN PUBLIC PLACES:
No person shall drink beer upon any public highway or street or other public
place within the limits of the city unless said place has been licensed by the
city council as a place where beer may be sold at retail. (1963 Code § 5-314)
3-2B-11: BEER SALES AT CERTAIN PLACES PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful to sell beer or offer beer for sale or otherwise dispose
of the same at any public dance, or at any public dance hall, or any public
school grounds or in any public school building within the city. (1963 Code §
5-315)
3-2B-12: HOURS OF SALE; VIEW INTO PREMISES:
   A.   Beer Sales: It shall be unlawful to sell beer or offer beer for sale,
or otherwise dispose of the same, or permit beer to be consumed upon any
premises operated under licenses issued in accordance with the provisions of
this article except during hours authorized by Idaho law. (1963 Code § 5-316;
amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Other Businesses: It shall be unlawful for any premises licensed for
sale of beer within the city, under the provisions of this article, to be kept
open for the conduct or operation of any other business except during hours
authorized by Idaho law, and no patrons or customers shall be admitted to such
licensed premises during prohibited hours. (1963 Code § 5-317; amd. 2010 Code)
   C.   View Into Premises: During such prohibited hours, all blinds or shades
shall be rolled up, drawn back or removed from the windows and doors of such
licensed premises so as to permit full view into such licensed premises from
the exterior of said premises, and a night light shall at all times be kept
burning in the interior of said premises during such closed hours. (1963 Code §
5-317)
   D.   Customers Prohibited From Premises: No patrons or customers of any
licensed premises or any persons other than the employees of said premises or
law enforcement officers shall be permitted on such premises except during
hours authorized by Idaho law. (1963 Code § 5-317; amd. 2010 Code)
ARTICLE C. WINE
SECTION:
3-2C-1: Definitions
3-2C-2: Sale Of Wine Authorized
3-2C-3: Licensing Requirements; Fee
3-2C-4: Investigation Of Applicant
3-2C-5: Transfer Of License; Fee
3-2C-6: Restrictions On Purchases And Sales
3-2C-7: Wine Consumption In Public Places
3-2C-8: Restrictions Concerning Underage Persons
3-2C-9: License Revocation, Cancellation Or Suspension
3-2C-10: Violation A Misdemeanor
3-2C-1: DEFINITIONS:
All words and phrases used in this article, the definition of which is not
herein given, shall be given their ordinary and commonly understood and
accepted meaning.
The following terms, as used in this article, are hereby defined as follows:
COUNTY LICENSE: A retail wine license issued by the board of commissioners of
Lewis County, Idaho.
PERSON: Includes an individual, firm, copartnership, association, corporation,
or any group or combination acting as a unit, and includes the plural as well
as the singular unless the intent to give a more limited meaning is disclosed
by the context in which it is used.
RETAIL WINE LICENSE: A license issued by the city authorizing a person to sell
wine at retail for off premises consumption or for consumption on the premises,
but separate licenses shall be required for each type of sales activity.
RETAILER: A person to whom a retail wine license has been issued hereunder.
STATE LICENSE: A retail wine license issued by the director of the Idaho state
police.
WINE: Any alcoholic beverage containing not more than twenty one percent (21%)
alcohol by volume obtained by the fermentation of the natural sugar content of
fruits or other agricultural products containing sugar, as is defined in Idaho
Code section 23-1303. (Ord. 250, 6-29-1971; amd. Ord. 287, 12-5-1978; 2010
Code)
3-2C-2: SALE OF WINE AUTHORIZED:
The sale of wine at retail within the corporate limits of the city, for either
off premises or on premises consumption, is hereby authorized, subject to the
provisions of this article. (Ord. 287, 12-5-1978)
3-2C-3: LICENSING REQUIREMENTS; FEE:
   A.   License Required: No person shall sell wine at retail unless he
possesses a valid license therefor issued pursuant to the provisions of this
article. (Ord. 250, 6-29-1971)
   B.   Fee: There is hereby established a license fee of fifty dollars
($50.00) per year for the sale of wine for off premises consumption and a
license fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) for the sale of wine for on premises
consumption; provided, however, that the on premises license fee shall be ten
dollars ($10.00) for any person holding a valid city beer license. (Ord. 287,
12-5-1978)
   C.   Separate License For Each Premises: A separate retail wine license
shall be required for each premises; provided, however, nothing herein shall
prohibit a distributor or retailer from possessing licenses for more than one
premises. (Ord. 250, 6-29-1971)
   D.   Fractional License; Term Of License:
      1.   No fractional or part year license shall be issued except as
provided in this article. (Ord. 389, 2-8-2005)
      2.   All licenses issued hereunder shall expire on January 31 at twelve
o'clock (12:00) midnight in the year following the year in which issued. (Ord.
389, 2-8-2005; amd. 2010 Code)
   E.   Application; Fee: All applications for a license hereunder shall be
made on forms provided by the city clerk-treasurer and shall be accompanied by
the appropriate fee.
   F.   Form And Posting Of License: All licenses issued hereunder shall be on
forms provided by the city clerk-treasurer, and shall be posted by the licensee
in a conspicuous place in his place of business.
   G.   State And County Licenses Required: No retail wine license issued by
the city shall authorize the retailer to sell wine at retail unless such person
possesses state and county licenses. (Ord. 250, 6-29-1971)
3-2C-4: INVESTIGATION OF APPLICANT:
Upon the receipt of an application for a license under this article,
accompanied by the necessary license fee, the city council may make such
investigation of all matters pertaining thereto as it shall deem proper. If the
council shall determine that the contents of the application are true, that
such applicant is qualified to receive a license, that his premises are
suitable for the carrying on of the intended business, and that the
requirements of this article have been met and complied with, a license shall
be issued; otherwise the application shall be denied and the license fee
returned. (Ord. 250, 6-29-1971)
3-2C-5: TRANSFER OF LICENSE; FEE:
A license granted under the terms of this article shall be transferable upon
the payment of a transfer fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00) to the city
clerk-treasurer. Provided, however, no portion of a license fee shall be
refundable for an unused, cancelled or revoked license after said license is
once issued. (Ord. 291, 3-6-1979; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2C-6: RESTRICTIONS ON PURCHASES AND SALES:
   A.   Purchasing Wine: Any ordinance to the contrary notwithstanding,
including, but not limited to, subsection
3-2A-15B of this title, the holder of a license for the retail sale of liquor
by the drink, as defined in article A of this chapter, is hereby authorized to
purchase wine from persons holding valid wine distributors' licenses or wine
retailers' licenses. (Ord. 250, 6-29-1971)
   B.   Sales Of Wine: Retailers holding valid licenses for the retail sale of
liquor by the drink pursuant to article A of this chapter may sell wine for
consumption on or off the licensed premises. Retailers who do not possess a
valid license for the retail sale of liquor by the drink or a valid license
issued hereunder for on premises consumption shall not permit consumption of
wine on the licensed premises and may sell the wine only in its original
unbroken container. Wine sold for consumption on the retailer's premises may be
sold only during hours that beer can be sold pursuant to the laws of this
state. Wine sold by a retailer for consumption off the premises of the retailer
may be sold only during the hours that beer may be sold pursuant to the laws of
this state. (Ord. 287, 12-5-1978)
3-2C-7: WINE CONSUMPTION IN PUBLIC PLACES:
No person shall drink wine upon any public highway or street or other public
place within the limits of the city unless said place has been licensed by the
city council as a place where liquor by the drink may be sold at retail for on
premises consumption. (Ord. 250, 6-29-1971)
3-2C-8: RESTRICTIONS CONCERNING UNDERAGE PERSONS:
   A.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years may purchase, consume
or possess wine.
   B.   No person shall give, sell or deliver wine to any person under the age
of twenty one (21) years.
   C.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years shall by any means
represent to any retailer or to any agent or employee of such retailer that he
or she is twenty one (21) years or more of age for the purpose of inducing such
retailer or his agent or employee to sell, serve or dispense wine to such
person.
   D.   No person shall, by any means, represent to any retailer, or the agent
or employee of such retailer, that any other person is twenty one (21) years or
more of age, when in fact such other person is under the age of twenty one (21)
years, for the purpose of inducing such retailer, or the agent or employee of
such retailer, to sell, serve, or dispense wine to such other person. (Ord.
250, 6-29-1971; amd. Ord. 257, 6-13-1972; 2010 Code)
3-2C-9: LICENSE REVOCATION, CANCELLATION OR SUSPENSION:
The right shall be, and at all times shall remain, vested in the city council
to revoke, cancel or suspend the license of any person licensed hereunder for
any violation of this article or of any violation of any county ordinance,
state or federal law relating to the sale of wine; and, upon verified complaint
filed with the council, the council shall, by written notice, cause such
alleged offender to appear before such council and be heard upon said
complaint. A copy of such complaint shall be served with such notice, and the
day, hour and place of the hearing, which shall be at least five (5) days from
the date of delivery of such notice, shall be specified in such notice. If at
such hearing, upon the taking of evidence on behalf of the city and such
alleged offender, it shall appear to the council that cause exists for the
cancellation or revocation of such license, the same may be cancelled, revoked
or suspended without further process of law, and the fact of such cancellation,
revocation or suspension shall immediately be certified to the director of the
Idaho state police and the board of commissioners of Lewis County. (Ord. 250,
6-29-1971; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2C-10: VIOLATION A MISDEMEANOR:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this article or fails to
comply with any of the terms and conditions of this article shall be guilty of
a misdemeanor. (Ord. 250, 6-29-1971)
CHAPTER 3
PEDDLERS, SOLICITORS AND TRANSIENT MERCHANTS
SECTION:
3-3-1: Definitions
3-3-2: Certificate Of Registration
3-3-3: Notice Regulating Peddlers And Solicitors
3-3-4: Duties Of Solicitors And Peddlers
3-3-5: Uninvited Soliciting Or Peddling
3-3-6: Time Limit On Soliciting And Peddling
3-3-7: Violation; Penalties
3-3-8: Constitutional Rights
3-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the following words, as used herein, shall be
construed to have the meanings herein ascribed thereto:
ITINERANT VENDOR: Any person who transports tangible personal property for
retail sale within the city who does not maintain in the state an established
office, distribution house, sales house, warehouse, service center or residence
from which such business is conducted; provided, however, this term shall not
include any person who delivers tangible personal property within the city who
is fulfilling an order for such property which was solicited or placed by mail
or other means. It shall be prima facie evidence that a person is an "itinerant
vendor" if the person does not transact business from a fixed location or if
the person does not own, or lease for a term of at least six (6) months, the
property from which business is conducted.
PEDDLING: Selling or offering for sale, barter or exchange at retail any goods,
wares, merchandise or services of any kind whatsoever by traveling from place
to place along the streets of the city or from residence to residence therein,
but shall not include solicitation or canvassing for future delivery.
"Peddling" may, in some instances, include the activities of an "itinerant
vendor" or "transient merchant", as defined herein. If a peddler is also an
"itinerant vendor" or "transient merchant", as defined herein, then those
provisions shall also be applicable. To the extent that the provisions of this
chapter relative to "peddling" are inconsistent with those relating to
"itinerant vendors" and/or "transient merchants", the more restrictive
provisions shall apply.
REGISTERED SOLICITOR AND REGISTERED PEDDLER: Means and includes any person who
has obtained a valid certificate of registration as herein provided, where such
certificate is in the possession of, and on the person of, the one soliciting
or peddling during all soliciting or peddling.
REGISTERED TRANSIENT MERCHANT AND REGISTERED ITINERANT VENDOR: Any person who
is a "transient merchant" or "itinerant vendor" as defined herein and who has
obtained and has in his possession a valid certificate of registration.
RESIDENCE: Means and includes every separate living unit occupied for
residential purposes by one or more persons, contained within any type of
building or structure.
SOLICITING: Means and includes any one or more of the following activities:
   A.   Seeking to obtain orders for the purchase of goods, wares, merchandise,
foodstuffs, insurance, or services of any kind, character or description
whatever, for any kind of consideration whatever, all for future delivery;
provided, however, that seeking to obtain subscriptions to books, magazines,
periodicals, newspapers and every other type or kind of publication shall not
be deemed to be "soliciting", and such activities are not regulated by this
chapter.
   B.   Seeking to obtain gifts or contributions of money, clothing or any
other valuable thing for the support or benefit of any charitable or nonprofit
association, organization, corporation, or project.
TRANSIENT MERCHANT: Any person who is engaged temporarily in the retail sale of
goods, wares or merchandise in the city and who, for the purpose of conducting
such business, occupies any building, room, vehicle, structure of any kind, or
vacant lot; provided, however, this term does not include any person selling
goods, wares or merchandise which are raised, produced or manufactured by him,
to any person selling vegetables, fruit or perishable farm products at an
established city market, to any person operating a store or refreshment stand
at a resort, or to any person operating a stand or booth on or adjacent to
property owned by him or upon which he resides. It shall be prima facie
evidence that a person is a "transient merchant" if the person does not
transact business from a fixed location or if the person does not own, or lease
for a term of at least six (6) months, the property from which business is
conducted. (2010 Code)
3-3-2: CERTIFICATE OF REGISTRATION:
   A.   Certificate Required: A written application for a certificate of
registration as herein provided shall be secured by every person desiring to
engage in "soliciting" or "peddling", as herein defined, from persons in
residences within the city and, in addition, by every person desiring to engage
in soliciting from any business, office or manufacturing facility within the
city for gifts or contributions of money, clothing or other valuable thing
except for the support or benefit of any charitable or nonprofit association,
organization, corporation or project.
   B.   Application For Certificate: Application for a certificate of
registration shall be made upon a form provided by and filed with the city
clerk-treasurer. The applicant shall state, under oath, such information
requested on the application form as is required by the provisions of this
chapter and such other relevant information as determined by the city clerk-
treasurer.
   C.   Prohibited Registrants: No certificate of registration shall be issued:
1) to anyone seeking to solicit for a charitable or nonprofit association,
organization, corporation or project unless such charity or nonprofit group is
specifically approved in advance by the city council which may waive
requirement of individual registration and fees if a list of names and
addresses of individuals to be involved are supplied to the city clerk-
treasurer; or 2) to any person who has been convicted of the commission of a
felony under the laws of the state of Idaho or any other state or federal law
of the United States, within five (5) years of the date of the application; or
3) to any person who has been convicted of a violation of any of the provisions
of this chapter or to any person whose certificate of registration issued
hereunder has previously been revoked as herein provided unless specifically
approved by the city council.
   D.   Fees:
      1.   Fees Established: A fee shall be paid at the time of filing the
application, as follows:
 
Certificate Requested                     Fee
1 day:                                    $ 5.00
More than 1 day and not more than 1 week: 25.00
More than 1 week:                         50.00
 
      2.   Waiver Of Fees: The mayor may waive such fee in his or her
discretion, but all fee waivers shall be reported to the city council.
   E.   Issuance Or Denial Of Certificate; Contents:
      1.   Denial: The mayor, after consideration of the application and all
information obtained relative thereto, shall deny the application if the
applicant does not possess the qualifications for such certificate as herein
required. Endorsement shall be made by the mayor upon the application of the
denial of the application.
      2.   Issuance: When the applicant is found to be fully qualified, the
certificate of registration shall be issued by the mayor or his or her
designee.
      3.   Time Limit For Action: All applications shall be acted upon by the
mayor within seven (7) days after receipt of a completed application.
      4.   Contents: Each certificate of registration shall state the
expiration date thereof.
   F.   Revocation Of Certificate: Any certificate of registration issued
hereunder may be revoked by the mayor if the holder of the certificate is
convicted of a violation of any of the provisions of this chapter, or has made
a false material statement in the application, or otherwise becomes
disqualified for the issuance of a certificate of registration under the terms
of this chapter. Immediately upon such revocation, written notice thereof shall
be given by the mayor to the holder of the certificate in person or by
certified U.S. mail addressed to his or her address set forth in the
application. Immediately upon the giving of such notice of revocation, the
certificate of registration shall become null and void.
   G.   Records Kept: The city clerk-treasurer shall cause to be kept in his or
her office an accurate record of every application received and acted upon
together with all other information and data pertaining thereto and of all
certificates of registration issued under the provisions of this chapter, and
of the denial of applications. Applications for certificates shall be numbered
in consecutive order as filed, and every certificate issued, and any renewal
thereof, shall be identified with the duplicate number of the application upon
which it was issued. (2010 Code)
3-3-3: NOTICE REGULATING PEDDLERS AND SOLICITORS:
   A.   Notice Requirements: The owner or occupant of any residence who desires
to forbid trespasses by solicitors or peddlers, or unlicensed solicitors and
peddlers, may attach or exhibit upon or near the main front door, and the main
rear or side door (if any, and if to be protected), a card or plaque stating
such of the following, as may be appropriate, in letters at least one-third
inch (1/3") in height:
SOLICITORS AND PEDDLERS NOT INVITED
or
SOLICITORS AND PEDDLERS NOT INVITED
UNLESS REGISTERED WITH THE CITY
   B.   Nonexclusive Notice Provided By City: For the convenience of residents
of the city and for purposes of uniformity, cards or plaques containing the
foregoing legend shall be made available by the city. The form of card or
plaque provided for in this section shall not be deemed to be an exclusive form
of notice. Such card or plaque so exhibited shall constitute sufficient notice
to any solicitor of the determination by the occupant of the residence of the
information contained thereon. (2010 Code)
3-3-4:   DUTIES OF SOLICITORS AND PEDDLERS:
   A.    It shall be unlawful for any person to enter upon any property of
another in the city after receiving, immediately prior to such entry, notice
from the owner or occupant that such entry is forbidden, or to remain upon the
property of another after receiving notice from the owner or occupant to
depart.
   B.    A person shall be deemed to have received notice from the owner or
occupant, within the meaning of this chapter, if he has been notified
personally, either orally or in writing, or if a printed or written notice
forbidding such entry has been conspicuously posted at the main entrance to
said property or the forbidden part thereof.
   C.    Any solicitor who has gained entrance to any residence, whether
invited or not, shall immediately and peacefully depart from the premises when
requested to do so by the occupant. (2010 Code)
3-3-5:   UNINVITED SOLICITING OR PEDDLING:
   A.    Uninvited Soliciting Or Peddling Prohibited: Any person soliciting or
peddling who is forbidden entry by notice given in compliance with this chapter
shall be deemed guilty of remaining on the property after receiving notice to
depart if he shall remain on the property, or if he shall ring the doorbell or
knock or create any sound calculated to attract the attention of the occupant.
   B.    Exemptions: Notices exhibited pursuant to this chapter shall not be
deemed applicable to and shall not prevent access to residential property by a
solicitor or peddler who has received prior invitation, written or oral, from
the owner or occupant thereof. (2010 Code)
3-3-6:   TIME LIMIT ON SOLICITING AND PEDDLING:
It is hereby declared to be unlawful and shall constitute a nuisance for any
person, whether registered under this chapter or not, to go upon any premises
and ring the doorbell upon or near any door of a residence located thereon, or
rap or knock upon any door, or create any sound in any other manner calculated
to attract the attention of the occupant of such residence, for the purpose of
securing an audience with the occupant thereof and engage in "soliciting" as
herein defined, prior to nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. or after nine o'clock (9:00)
P.M. (2010 Code)
3-3-7:   VIOLATION; PENALTIES:
   A.    Violation; Penalty: Any person, firm or corporation who shall be found
guilty by a court of competent jurisdiction of violating any provision of this
chapter or of failing to comply with any requirement hereof, or of violating
any permit, any approval, or any directive issued under the provisions of this
chapter, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code, and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each
day during or on which a violation occurs or continues.
   B.    Reimbursement Of Costs: Any person, firm or corporation who shall be
found guilty by a court of competent jurisdiction of violating a provision of
this chapter or of failing to comply with any requirement hereof, or of
violating any certificate, any approval, or any directive issued under the
provisions of this chapter, shall, in addition to the fines provided, be
obligated to reimburse the city for its attorney fees, court costs, court
reporter costs, and expert witness fees, and all other out of pocket costs
incurred by the city in the prosecution of the said violation or violations.
   C.    Injunctive Relief: The city may make application to the circuit court
for an injunction requiring conformance with this chapter or make such other
order as the court deems necessary to secure compliance with this chapter.
(2010 Code)
3-3-8:   CONSTITUTIONAL RIGHTS:
Nothing in this chapter shall be interpreted or enforced to deprive any person
of any rights guaranteed under the constitution of the state or the United
States. (2010 Code)

CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
SECTION:
4-1-1: Definitions
4-1-2: Nuisance Declared
4-1-3: Prohibited Conduct
4-1-4: Automotive Hobby Projects
4-1-5: Commercial Enterprises
4-1-6: Enforcement; Right Of Entry
4-1-7: Abatement Procedure
