4-1-9: Removal Cost Assessment
4-1-10: Alternative Provisions
4-1-11: Jurisdiction
4-1-12: Penalty And Enforcement
4-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words shall have the meanings
respectively ascribed to them:
ABANDONED: To have a motor vehicle on private property without the permission
of the person having rights to the possession of the property or on a public
street or other property open to the public for the purposes of vehicular
traffic or parking, or upon or within the right of way of any road or highway,
for forty eight (48) hours or longer.
AUTOMOTIVE HOBBY PROJECT: A noncommercial accessory use involving the
restoration, maintenance, and/or preservation of motor vehicles taking place
exclusively on residential private property within the city limits of the city
of Craigmont.
AUTOMOTIVE HOBBY SITE: Any privately owned real property upon which the
resident is restoring, maintaining, and/or preserving one or more motor
vehicles.
CONTAINER: A garbage can, dumpster, or any other kind of storage device
customarily sold, rented, constructed, or utilized for use as for temporary
storage of waste matter, and lawfully located on the property in question.
FRONT YARD: All property, including driveways and entranceways extending
between side lot lines across the frontage of a lot adjoining a public street
other than an alley, and from any side of the principal building.
HAZARDOUS WASTE:
   A.    Any "hazardous waste" as defined by the resource conservation and
recovery act of 1976 (42 USC section 6901 et seq.), as amended from time to
time, and regulations promulgated thereunder;
   B.   Any "hazardous substance" as defined by the comprehensive environmental
response, compensation and liability act of 1980 (42 USC section 9601 et seq.),
as amended from time to time, and regulations promulgated thereunder;
   C.   Radon and material quantities of petroleum products;
   D.   Any substance the presence of which on the property is regulated by any
federal, state or local law relating to the protection of the environment or
public health; and
   E.   Any other substance which by law requires special handling in its
collection, storage, treatment or disposal.
HIGHWAY: A way or place of whatever nature, publicly maintained and open to the
use of the public for purposes of vehicular travel or parking. "Highway"
includes street or alley. "Highway" does not include those portions of said way
or place which are not utilized for vehicular travel, such as those portions of
aprons, setbacks, easement rights of way, or property owned by the public which
extends beyond the surface area normally utilized for vehicular travel or
parking. Said areas are to be considered public property for purposes of this
chapter.
INOPERATIVE: A vehicle that is incapable of being propelled under its own power
or operation.
PUBLIC PROPERTY: All property owned by the public. "Public property" does not
include a highway.
REAR YARD: A yard extending between side lot lines across the rear of a lot
opposite the side(s) of a building which fronts upon a public street and from
the rear lot line to the principal building.
VEHICLE: A device by which any person or property may be propelled, moved, or
drawn, whether or not utilized solely upon a highway, except a device moved
solely by human power or used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks,
whether or not in a condition capable of operation or use.
WASTE MATTER: Any kind of liquid or solid waste, hazardous waste, manufactured
goods, appliance, fixture, furniture, machinery, vehicle, personal property or
any other thing or part thereof, whether of value or valueless, that is
demolished, discarded, dismantled, partially dismantled, dilapidated, or so
worn, deteriorated, or in such a condition as to be generally unusable and/or
inoperable in its existing state.
This shall include by way of illustration only, and without limitation: trash
or refuse of any kind, litter, commercial waste, industrial or construction or
demolition debris of any kind, such as rubble, broken asphalt and concrete,
crates, cartons, metal, glass, appliances or appliance shells, boat bodies and
parts, used tires, vehicle bodies and parts, commercial or industrial equipment
bodies and parts, snowmobile bodies and parts, trailers and parts, recreational
vehicle bodies and parts, mobile home and manufactured home bodies and parts,
and inoperable or damaged vehicles of any kind, and any cast off tangible
personal property or fixtures. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-2: NUISANCE DECLARED:
Pursuant to the authority granted by Idaho Code section 50-334 and correlated
other provisions, the city council makes the following findings and
declarations: The accumulation and storage of waste matter on private or public
property is found to create a condition tending to reduce the value of
surrounding private property, to promote blight and deterioration, and to
invite plundering, to create fire hazards, to constitute an attractive nuisance
creating a hazard to the health and safety of minors, to create a harborage for
rodents and insects and to be injurious to the health, safety and general
welfare of entire neighborhoods and/or a significant number of persons.
Therefore, the presence of the following on private or public property, unless
expressly permitted herein, are declared to constitute a public nuisance and
are prohibited, and may be abated as such in accordance with the provisions of
this chapter:
   A.   Unlicensed, Abandoned Or Wrecked Vehicle: An unlicensed, abandoned,
wrecked, dismantled or inoperative vehicle, or part thereof, on private or
public property except as expressly hereinafter permitted. However, abandoned
vehicles shall be dealt with as prescribed by Idaho Code section 49-1801 et
seq.
   B.   Uncovered Containers Holding Waste Matter: An uncovered container
holding waste matter, or such a container with a cover which is not secure
against dogs, unless said container of a type that is not normally covered,
such as compost bins, or sludge drying bins.
   C.   Waste Matter Outside Containers: Waste matter not in a container.
   D.   Waste Matter Entering Waters: Waste matter stored in such fashion that
it or any of it may enter the waters of a stream or river, directly or
indirectly, or come to be in contact with such waters.
   E.   Waste Or Vegetative Matter Constituting Fire Hazard: Waste matter or
dry or dead vegetative matter so located as to constitute a fire hazard to
buildings or lands, and vegetative matter which will in the ordinary course
become such a hazard; but not hay or other agricultural products stored in a
fashion customary on farms in the community and in accord with the applicable
fire codes adopted by the city.
   F.   Unsightly Conditions: Waste matter or one or more containers which by
reason of its or their location and character are unsightly and interfere with
the reasonable enjoyment of adjacent or nearby property. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-
2009)
4-1-3: PROHIBITED CONDUCT:
In addition to the provisions of section
4-1-2 of this chapter, the following conduct is hereby prohibited:
   A.   Allowing Escape Of Waste From Waste Transportation Vehicle: To wilfully
cause or permit any vehicle to be used for the transportation of waste to be so
loaded or in such condition or so uncovered that waste matter escapes from the
vehicle while being driven.
   B.   Discharging Waste: To wilfully discharge waste matter onto the surface
of the earth other than into a container or beneath the surface of the earth,
or into any stream, river, or other water body.
   C.   Causing Or Permitting Nuisance: To wilfully cause or allow a nuisance
or permit a nuisance to continue on property in the possession of the offender
or on any abutting street, sidewalk or right of way. Any entity or person who,
upon receiving notice of the existence of a nuisance as described in the
abatement procedure set forth herein, fails to remedy the same within the time
established in said abatement procedure, shall be deemed to have wilfully
allowed or permitted a nuisance to continue.
   D.   Violations; Failure To Comply: To wilfully violate any other provision
or requirement of this chapter, or to fail to comply with any order issued
pursuant to the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-4: AUTOMOTIVE HOBBY PROJECTS:
   A.   Intent Of Section: It is the intent of this section to provide
standards for the restoration, maintenance, and/or preservation of personal
motor vehicles conducted as a hobby, and conducted at a person's residence or
upon private property.
   B.   Required Standards:
      1.   Automotive hobby projects may only be conducted on residential
property, and only as a noncommercial project. No commercial, retail or
wholesale sales of automobiles, or automotive parts or supplies, shall be
conducted upon a site claiming lawful use as an automotive hobby project. No
restoration, repair or maintenance of motor vehicles shall be conducted upon
any residential site for which monetary compensation is received.
      2.   All automotive hobby sites shall be maintained in a safe and orderly
manner so as not to create a public nuisance, an unsightly condition, an
undesirable condition, a health or fire hazard.
      3.   No automotive hobby sites may contain more than four (4) inoperable
dismantled or unregistered vehicles which constitute an automotive hobby
project. No automotive hobby projects may be stored in the front yard of any
lot. All automotive hobby sites must be located in the rear yard of any lot. If
any automotive hobby site contains more than two (2) automotive hobby projects,
said projects must be screened from view so that it or they are not visible at
a distance of six feet (6') observed from the property lines of adjacent
properties, by a sight obscuring fence of not less than, nor more than, six
feet (6') in height, or a hedge of not less than six feet (6') in height.
      4.   The restrictions set forth in this chapter do not apply to those
automobiles stored inside of a fully enclosed building. Further, the
restrictions set forth in this chapter do not apply to duly registered and
licensed vehicles which are inoperable but upon which repair is being
conducted, but only so long as said repair is conducted and completed within
sixty (60) days of the vehicle becoming inoperable. Automobiles being repaired
may only be stored or parked in improved parking areas or driveways, and shall
not be stored or parked in any front yard of a residential site.
      5.   Any motor vehicle restoration preservation, maintenance or repair
hobby operation involving welding, painting or use of flammable liquids shall
be conduced in a safe, prudent and lawful manner. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-5: COMMERCIAL ENTERPRISES:
No person or entity operating any commercial enterprise within the city shall
cause, allow, or permit waste matter to be present upon the property being
utilized unless within a fully enclosed structure. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-6: ENFORCEMENT; RIGHT OF ENTRY:
It shall be the right of the fire chief or other officer designated by the
mayor to inspect properties, investigate complaints, and determine whether or
not a nuisance exists in accordance with the terms of this chapter. The fire
chief, or such other designated officer, or his or her designated agent, shall
be authorized to enter upon private property or public property to investigate,
remove, or cause the removal of a vehicle or parts thereof declared to be a
nuisance pursuant to this chapter. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-7: ABATEMENT PROCEDURE:
The below described procedure shall apply for the abatement of public nuisances
other than dangerous buildings. Regardless of the exercise of any enforcement
remedy contained in this chapter, the city shall have the right of abatement
with respect to any public nuisance. The exercise of the right of abatement or
any procedures described herein shall not be a prerequisite to exercise of any
other remedies or enforcement of the criminal provisions contained in this
chapter.
   A.   Abandoned Vehicle: The procedures and requirements of Idaho Code
section 49-1801 et seq., or its successor provisions shall apply to all
abandoned vehicles or vehicles which constitute waste matter, or vehicles being
kept, maintained, or stored in violation of the provisions of this chapter,
whether located upon highways, public property, or private property.
   B.   Other Nuisances: The abatement procedure set out in section
4-1-8 of this chapter shall apply to all other nuisances. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-
2009)
4-1-8: DECLARATION OF PUBLIC NUISANCE:
   A.   Declaration And Notice: A nuisance may be declared by the fire chief or
other person or officer designated by the mayor who, upon identification of a
nuisance, shall cause a written declaration to be issued, by mailing the same
to the last registered owner(s) of the real property upon which he determines a
nuisance is present, as reflected on the tax assessment rolls of Lewis County,
and by posting the same in a conspicuous place on the real property on which
the nuisance is located. Each notice that is mailed shall be sent by certified
mail, return receipt requested. Notice shall be deemed to have been provided
upon mailing. Every person entitled to notice of the declaration of nuisance
shall have thirty (30) days to remove or remedy the condition creating the
nuisance, or to request a public hearing as described below. Every notice of
declaration of nuisance shall contain the following:
      1.   A descriptive statement of the nuisance which is declared to exist;
      2.   Its location;
      3.   The name of the person or persons thought to be responsible;
      4.   A statement of a date, not less than thirty (30) days after the
mailing of such notice, which shall be the last date on which the addressee or
other claimant of the affected property or offending objects can demand a
hearing, or cause removal or remedy of the nuisance described;
      5.   A statement that such hearing would be for the purpose of
determining anew whether the nuisance exists;
      6.   Directions for the mailing of such a demand for hearing to the city
clerk; and
      7.   A statement that if no hearing is demanded, or if the result of the
hearing is to the effect that a nuisance exists, the owner or other addressee
will have thirty (30) days to commence and thereafter diligently to pursue and
complete the abatement and assess back the costs thereof against the property
in like fashion as for tax assessments.
   B.   Failure To Request Hearing: Failure to request a public hearing within
the time required shall be deemed conclusive as to the existence of the
nuisance as described in the declaration posted and mailed.
   C.   Hearing Procedure:
      1.   Upon receipt of a request for a public hearing, the mayor shall
establish a date for a public hearing, to be held no less than ten (10) days
nor more than thirty (30) days from receipt of said report. The public hearing
shall be to determine if a nuisance exists, and assessment of administrative
costs, and directions for removal or remedy.
      2.   Notice of said hearing shall be provided by certified mail to any
person or entity requesting a public hearing, to the last registered owner of
the real property upon which the fire chief, or other official designated by
the mayor, has determined a nuisance is present. Notice shall be deemed
completed upon mailing.
      3.   The city council shall hear all facts and testimony deemed
pertinent. The facts and testimony may include testimony, pictures, videos,
etc., on the condition of the property, vehicles, waste matter, or any other
evidence regarding the existence of a nuisance. The city council shall not be
limited by the technical rules of evidence. The owner of the land on which the
alleged nuisance is located may appear in person at the hearing or present a
written statement in time for consideration at the hearing, and deny
responsibility for the presence of the nuisance with his or her reasons for
such denial.
      4.   The city council, upon a finding that a public nuisance exists, may
impose such conditions and take such action as deemed appropriate under the
circumstances to carry out the purpose of this chapter, including delaying the
time for removal or remedy of the nuisance or part thereof, if, in its opinion,
the circumstances justify it. At the conclusion of the public hearing, the city
council must make written findings of fact and conclusions of law, and may
order the nuisance remedied or removed from the property as a public nuisance
and disposed of as hereinafter provided, and determine the administrative costs
to be charged against the owner of the parcel of land on which the nuisance is
located. The order requiring removal shall include:
         a.   A description of the nuisance or part thereof and the correct
identification number and license number of any vehicle constituting a part or
all of the nuisance, if available, at the site.
         b.   A statement that the nuisance must be removed or remedied within
thirty (30) days of adoption of the order, unless some other time period is
specified by the city council.
      5.   If an interested party makes a written presentation to the city
council but does not appear, he shall be notified in writing of the decision.
   D.   Abatement By City: Upon the expiration of thirty (30) days after
mailing of a declaration of nuisance if no hearing is requested, or the later
of thirty (30) days after adoption of the order declaring a condition to be a
public nuisance, or thirty (30) days from the date of mailing of notice of the
decision to an interested person who makes a written presentation if such
notice is required by this section, or the date specified in the order if a
date is specified. If the nuisance remains in whole or in part, the fire chief
or other officer or person appointed by the mayor, shall take steps to cause
the abatement of the nuisance by removal of the offending materials, whether by
fire suppression exercise, by use of city employees, or by letting an
appropriate contract in accord with the contracting procedures of the city. The
waste matter which constitutes the public nuisance may be disposed of by
removal to a garbage transfer station, dump, scrap yard, or automobile
dismantler's yard, or to any other similar facility. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-9: REMOVAL COST ASSESSMENT:
The cost of abatement, together with the administrative costs, shall be
calculated and assessed. If such amount is not paid within thirty (30) days of
the date of abatement, the same shall become a lien upon the property pursuant
to Idaho Code sections 50-334 and 50-1008, and shall be transmitted to the tax
collector for collection. The assessment shall have the same priority as other
city taxes. The city shall also be entitled to recover said costs in a civil
action brought by the city, and assess the same as additional penalties in a
misdemeanor prosecution. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-10: ALTERNATIVE PROVISIONS:
This chapter is not the exclusive regulation of public nuisances, or the
exclusive regulation of abandoned, wrecked, dismantled or inoperative vehicles
within the city. This chapter shall supplement and be in addition to the other
regulatory codes, statutes and ordinances heretofore or hereafter enacted by
the city, the state, or any other legal entity or agency having jurisdiction.
(Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-11: JURISDICTION:
The abatement of nuisances under the provisions of this chapter shall apply
only to the corporate boundaries of the city. The city shall not extend their
authority under Idaho Code section 50-334 beyond the boundaries of the city.
(Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
4-1-12: PENALTY AND ENFORCEMENT:
A violation of this chapter is a general misdemeanor and is also subject to
abatement action. Enforcement shall be by that person or official so designated
by the mayor, or his or her designated agents. (Ord. 2009-405, 8-4-2009)
CHAPTER 2
TREES AND SHRUBBERY
SECTION:
4-2-1: Purpose
4-2-2: Definitions
4-2-3: Application Of Provisions
4-2-4: Enforcement
4-2-5: Permit Required; Application
4-2-6: Trimming Trees Overhanging Streets Or Sidewalks
4-2-7: Injurious Pests Or Diseases
4-2-8: Removal Of Trees
4-2-9: Planting New Trees
4-2-10: City Authority
4-2-11: Appeal
4-2-1: PURPOSE:
It shall be the purpose of this chapter to protect trees throughout the city
and to regulate the trimming and maintenance of trees near the public streets,
and to regulate the maintenance of trees within the streets adjacent to private
property, including the type of trees to be planted in the future, the care of
those trees, disease control, which impliedly then protects the streets,
sidewalks, and curbs. All of said control is for the purposes of furthering the
aesthetics and beauty of the city while at the same time providing reasonable
care of improvements. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
DISEASED TREE: Any tree which exhibits actual evidence of disease of whatever
character or form, including infestation by pests a degree that it is actually
affecting the tree itself.
INJURIOUS PEST: Any insect, fungus, or growing parasite which materially
injures any tree or shrub.
OCCUPANT: The person actually occupying any particular property and having
control over the particular property under any contractual relationship with
the owner thereof.
OWNER: The vested owner of real property as shown by the county records, and
any contract purchaser of real property as shown by the public records or other
evidence of ownership.
PARKWAY: That portion of the street between the traveled portion of the road
and a sidewalk.
PRUNING: The physical removal of limbs or any portion of trees or shrubbery for
purposes of reducing the size of trees or shrubs, or in any way shaping the
same.
ROADWAY: That portion of a street improved, designed, or ordinarily used by the
public for vehicular travel.
SIDEWALK: That portion of a street improved, designed, or ordinarily used by
the public for pedestrian travel.
STREET: All real property owned by the city for streets, alleys, or rights of
way as indicated by the public records or recorded plats of Lewis County, or
any public rights of way established by prescription, pursuant to Idaho law.
(Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-3: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
This chapter shall apply to all trees, shrubs, and other similar growing plant
life that now exists, and all similar plants that are planted in the future
within the incorporated limits of the city. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-4: ENFORCEMENT:
The mayor or his designated agent shall be the person responsible for the
regular review of all trees and shrubs which are subject to the provisions of
this chapter, with final authority being with the city council. (Ord. 356, 6-6-
1995)
4-2-5: PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
   A.   Permit Required; Exception: It shall be unlawful for any person to
plant, remove, trim, cut, or in any way damage any tree or shrubbery on or
within any street without first procuring a permit so to do from the city;
provided, that no permit shall first be required in situations where public
inconvenience would result from the delay entailed in obtaining a permit or
where such delay would place life, limb, or property in jeopardy.
   B.   Filing Of Application; Investigation: Any person desiring a permit to
plant, remove, cut, or in any way damage a tree on or within the city streets
shall file with the city an application so to do on forms to be furnished by
the city setting forth therein in detail the work that is contemplated and the
location and address of the same. Upon the filing of such application, the city
shall investigate the contemplated work and if it is desirable and should be
done, shall issue a written permit; provided, that the work authorized in such
permit shall be done under the supervision of the city. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-6: TRIMMING TREES OVERHANGING STREETS OR SIDEWALKS:
Any owner or occupant of any real property shall trim all trees on property
owned or occupied by him overhanging any street so that the branches thereon
will not interfere with pedestrians or public travel. Trees adjacent to streets
shall be pruned to a twelve foot (12') height above streets and a seven foot
(7') height above sidewalks. Furthermore, all trees shall be regularly pruned
so that dead or diseased limbs of trees shall be removed. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-7: INJURIOUS PESTS OR DISEASES:
   A.   Nuisance Declared: All injurious pests and diseases infecting any tree
within the city are hereby declared to be public nuisances.
   B.   Eradication Of Diseases Or Pests: It shall be the duty of the owner of
any private property in the city to take all proper measures for the
eradication of any injurious disease or pest infecting or infesting any tree or
shrub and to cause the same to be sprayed with an effective formula approved by
permit with the city.
   C.   Owner Responsibility: The owner of property abutting the public street
shall be responsible for prohibiting the infestation, or spread or continued
existence of injurious pests or disease, and their eggs or larvae, to any tree
located within the public street. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-8: REMOVAL OF TREES:
   A.   Permit Required: Property owners may remove trees from streets which
abut their property at their own expense after first receiving a permit from
the city. Furthermore, property owners may be required to remove trees that are
abutting their property if those trees are deemed a hazard or dangerous to the
public or other public or private property.
   B.   Owner Responsibility: All owners of property adjacent to the street
upon which are located existing trees shall have the obligation for the care of
trees and shrubbery adjacent to such property. Such financial responsibility
shall include disease control, insect infestation, pruning or trimming, and
removal if necessary. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-9: PLANTING NEW TREES:
   A.   Permit Required: New trees may in the future be planted on a portion of
the public street if there is appropriate space therefor, and with the consent
of the city, after obtaining a permit for the same.
   B.   Criteria For Granting Permit: No shrubs or bushes may be planted upon
the street until a permit from the city council is obtained. The principal
criteria for granting permission shall be site restriction, the location of
sidewalks, curbs, and the location of any existing or future expected
utilities.
   C.   Unlawful Planting A Misdemeanor: Anyone planting shrubs or trees in
violation of this chapter shall be guilty of a general misdemeanor under the
laws of the state and shall be punishable as such. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-10: CITY AUTHORITY:
   A.   Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit the city, without charge to the
owners of abutting property, from eradicating injurious pests and diseases, or
pruning trees located within the public street.
   B.   Furthermore, in the event of a violation of this chapter, and after a
thirty (30) day notice has been personally delivered to such person and the
violation continues to exist, the city may enter upon such property and cure
the violation, then having a right of action against said property owner for
all sums and costs incurred. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
4-2-11: APPEAL:
Any person aggrieved by the action of the city or its designee may appeal to
the city council by delivering written notice to the city clerk-treasurer. The
city shall set the matter at the next regularly scheduled council meeting for
hearing. The council shall make a decision within thirty (30) days of the
hearing. (Ord. 356, 6-6-1995)
CHAPTER 3
BILLPOSTING AND HANDBILLS
SECTION:
4-3-1: Littering Public Thoroughfares Prohibited
4-3-2: Posting Notices On Fences Or Poles Restricted
4-3-1: LITTERING PUBLIC THOROUGHFARES PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to scatter or throw upon the streets,
sidewalks, alleys or other public thoroughfares of the city, any handbills,
posters, advertisements or papers. Nothing herein shall be construed to
authorize any person to obstruct the public streets, sidewalks, alleys or
thoroughfares of the city or create any nuisance therein. The provisions of
this chapter shall not interfere or prevent the posting of notices required by
law to be posted. (1963 Code § 5-501)
4-3-2: POSTING NOTICES ON FENCES OR POLES RESTRICTED:
   A.   Consent Required For Posting To Fence Or Wall: It shall be unlawful for
any person to post, paint, tack or otherwise attach any notice or other
advertising matter to any fence, wall or building or other property until first
obtaining the consent of the owner of such property.
   B.   Attaching Notices To Poles Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any
person to post, paint, tack or otherwise attach any notice or advertising
matter to any telegraph, telephone, electric or other such poles. (1963 Code §
5-502)
CHAPTER 4
LIVESTOCK FEEDING AND BREEDING
SECTION:
4-4-1: Policy
4-4-2: Definitions
4-4-3: Prohibited Acts
4-4-4: Exceptions
4-4-5: Complaints; Assistance In Prosecution
4-4-1: POLICY:
It is hereby declared as the policy of the city in the exercise of its powers,
its power to prevent and remove nuisances, and the exercise of its power to
prevent the introduction and spread of contagious disease, as provided under
the provisions of Idaho Code section 50-304, as amended, to limit, restrict or
prohibit the keeping, feeding and breeding of livestock within the corporate
limits of the city. It is further declared that a feedlot within the city
limits is a health and public nuisance to the people of the city, and that it
infringes on the well being, comfort, repose and enjoyment of the ordinary
individual residing within the city. It is further declared that the breeding
of livestock within the city limits is a moral nuisance and interferes with the
peaceful use and enjoyment of property. (1963 Code § 8-301; amd. 2010 Code)
4-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases used in this chapter shall be given the
following interpretations:
BREED OR BREEDING: To produce offspring, the act of generating or producing
offspring.
CITY LIMITS: The incorporated limits of the city.
FEEDLOT: A place for the keeping and feeding of three (3) or more livestock.
LIVESTOCK: All breeds of cattle, horses, sheep, swine, hogs, and goats.
PERSON: Every individual, partnership, corporation, organization, or
association, singularly and collectively. (1963 Code § 8-302)
4-4-3: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   Feedlots: It shall be unlawful for any person to keep and maintain a
feedlot within the corporate limits of the city. (1963 Code § 8-303)
   B.   Breeding Livestock: It shall be unlawful for any person to breed
livestock or to allow others to breed livestock upon his property within the
city limits. (1963 Code § 8-304)
   C.   Keeping Certain Animals: It shall be unlawful to breed, feed, care for
or maintain one or more rabbits, sheep, goats, hogs, pigs or swine within the
corporate limits of the city. (1963 Code § 8-305; amd. 2010 Code)
4-4-4: EXCEPTIONS:
This chapter shall be subject to any exceptions or allowances that may be
hereinafter enacted by any zoning ordinance adopted by the city. (1963 Code §
8-306)
4-4-5: COMPLAINTS; ASSISTANCE IN PROSECUTION:
It is hereby made the duty of any officer of the city, knowing of any violation
of this chapter, to make complaints before the proper law enforcement officer
and to assist in the prosecution and conviction of offenders. Any officer
knowingly refusing to inform against or to prosecute any offender under the
provisions of this chapter shall be subject to removal from the office by the
mayor and city council. (1963 Code § 8-307; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 5
FIRE PREVENTION AND PROTECTION
SECTION:
4-5-1: Fireworks
4-5-2: General Precautions Against Fire
4-5-3: Smoking Prohibited Under Certain Conditions
4-5-1: FIREWORKS:
   A.   Definition: "Pyrotechnics", whenever used in this section, shall be
held to mean any sparkler, squib, rocket, firecracker, Roman candle, fire
balloon, signal light, railroad track torpedo, flashlight composition, pistol,
cane, cannon or other appliances using blank cartridges or caps, fireworks or
other devices or compositions used to obtain visible or audible pyrotechnic
displays. (1963 Code § 7-201)
   B.   Fireworks Prohibited; Exceptions: No person, firm or corporation shall,
within the city, have, keep, store, use, manufacture, sell or offer for sale,
handle or transport any pyrotechnics; provided, however:
      1.   That nothing in this section shall be held to apply to the
possession or use of signaling devices for current daily consumption by
railroads, trucks, and others requiring them.
      2.   That the chief of the fire department or the city clerk- treasurer
may, upon due application, issue a permit to a properly qualified person for
giving a pyrotechnic display of fireworks in the public parks or other open
places. (1963 Code § 7-202)
4-5-2: GENERAL PRECAUTIONS AGAINST FIRE:
   A.   Bonfires And Outdoor Rubbish Fires:
      1.   Permit Required: No person shall kindle or maintain any bonfire or
rubbish fire, or authorize any such fire to be kindled or maintained on or in
any public street, alley, road or other public ground without a permit or other
proper authorization from the appropriate agency.
      2.   Location Restricted: No person shall kindle or maintain any bonfire,
rubbish fire, or fire within a fire pit, or authorize any such fire to be
kindled or maintained on any private land unless: a) the location is not less
than fifty feet (50') from any structure and adequate provision is made to
prevent fire from spreading to within fifty feet (50') of any structure; or b)
the fire is contained in an approved waste burner with closed top, located
safely not less than fifteen feet (15') from any structure. (1963 Code § 7-501;
amd. 2010 Code)
      3.   Enforcement: The chief of the fire department may prohibit any or
all bonfires and outdoor rubbish fires when atmospheric conditions or local
circumstances make such fires hazardous. (1963 Code § 7-501)
   B.   Kindling Fire On Land Of Others: No person shall kindle a fire upon the
land of another without permission of the owner thereof or his agent. (1963
Code § 7-502)
   C.   Hot Ashes And Other Dangerous Materials: No person shall deposit hot
ashes or cinders, or smoldering coals, or greasy or oily substances liable to
spontaneous ignition, into any wooden receptacle, or place the same within ten
feet (10') of any combustible materials, except in metal or other
noncombustible receptacles. Such receptacles, unless resting on a
noncombustible floor or on the ground outside the building, shall be placed on
noncombustible stands, and in every case must be kept at least two feet (2')
away from any combustible wall or partition. (1963 Code § 7-503)
   D.   Accumulations Of Waste Materials: Accumulations of wastepaper, hay,
grass, straw, weeds, litter or combustible or flammable waste or rubbish of any
kind shall not be permitted to remain upon any roof or in any court, yard,
vacant lot or open space. All weeds, grass, vines or other growth, when same
endangers property, or is liable to be fired, shall be cut down and removed by
the owner or occupant of the property where such accumulations are located.
(1963 Code § 7-504)
   E.   Storage Of Combustible Materials:
      1.   Permit Required: No person shall store in excess of two thousand
five hundred (2,500) cubic feet gross volume of combustible empty packing
cases, boxes, barrels or similar containers, or rubber tires, or baled cotton,
rubber or cork, or other similarly combustible material without a permit from
the chief of the fire department.
      2.   Storage Requirements: Storage in buildings shall be orderly, shall
not be within two feet (2') of the ceiling, and not so located as to endanger
exit from the building. Storage in the open shall not be more than twenty feet
(20') in height, shall be so located, with respect to adjacent buildings, as
not to constitute a hazard, and shall be compact and orderly. (1963 Code § 7-
506)
   F.   Flammable Decorative Materials In Stores: Cotton batting, straw, dry
vines, leaves, trees, and other highly flammable materials shall not be used
for decorative purposes in show windows or other parts of stores unless
flameproofed; provided, however, that nothing in this subsection shall be held
to prohibit the display of saleable goods permitted and offered for sale. (1963
Code § 7-507)
   G.   Use Of Torches Or Flame Producing Devices For Removing Paint: Any
person using a torch or other flame producing device for removing paint from
any building or structure shall provide one approved fire extinguisher or water
hose connected to the water supply on the premises where such burning is done.
In all cases, the person doing the burning shall remain on the premises one
hour after the torch or flame producing device has been used. (1963 Code § 7-
509)
4-5-3: SMOKING PROHIBITED UNDER CERTAIN CONDITIONS:
   A.   Definition: "Smoking" shall mean and include the carrying of lighted
pipe, cigar, cigarette or tobacco in any form. (1963 Code § 7-701)
   B.   Designation Of Areas Where Smoking Prohibited: Where conditions are
such as to make smoking a hazard in any areas of warehouses, stores, industrial
plants, institutions, places of assembly, and in open spaces where combustible
materials are stored or handled, the chief of the fire department is empowered
and authorized to order the owner or occupant in writing to post "No Smoking"
signs in each building, structure, room or place in which smoking shall be
prohibited. The chief of the fire department shall designate specific safe
locations, if necessary, in any building, structure or place in which smoking
may be permitted. (1963 Code § 7-702)
   C.   No Smoking Signs: "No Smoking" signs required in accordance with
subsection B of this section shall read "By Order Of The Chief Of The Fire
Department". (1963 Code § 7-703)
   D.   Smoking And Removal Of No Smoking Signs Prohibited: It shall be
unlawful for any person to remove any legally required "No Smoking" sign or to
smoke in any place where such signs are posted. (1963 Code § 7-704)
CHAPTER 6
FIRE HAZARD INSPECTION
SECTION:
4-6-1: Inspection Authorized
4-6-2: Hazard Removal Upon Order
4-6-3: Failure To Remove Hazard
4-6-4: Serving Of Order
4-6-1: INSPECTION AUTHORIZED:
Authority is hereby given to the chief of the fire department to inspect or
cause to be inspected by fire department officers or members, as often as may
be necessary, all buildings, premises and public thoroughfares, except the
interiors of private dwellings, for the purpose of ascertaining and causing to
be corrected any conditions liable to cause fire, or any violations of the
provisions or intent of any laws of the city affecting the fire hazard. (1963
Code § 7-901)
4-6-2: HAZARD REMOVAL UPON ORDER:
Whenever an officer or member shall find in any building, upon any premises or
other place, combustible matter or dangerous accumulation of rubbish or
unnecessary accumulation of wastepaper, boxes, shavings, or any other highly
inflammable materials especially liable to fire, and which is so situated as to
endanger property, or shall find obstructions to or on fire escapes, stairs,
passageways, doors or windows liable to interfere with the operation of the
fire department, or egress of occupants in case of fire, he shall order the
same to be removed or remedied, and such order shall forthwith be complied with
by the owner or occupant of such premises or buildings, subject to appeal
within twenty four (24) hours to the city council, who shall, within five (5)
days, review such order and file its decision thereon; and unless the order is
revoked or modified, it shall remain in full force and be obeyed by such owner
or occupant. (1963 Code § 7-902)
4-6-3: FAILURE TO REMOVE HAZARD:
Any owner or occupant failing to comply with such order within ten (10) days
after said appeal shall have been determined, or, if no appeal is taken, then
within ten (10) days after the service of said order, shall be deemed guilty of
a misdemeanor. (1963 Code § 7-903)
4-6-4: SERVING OF ORDER:
The service of any such order shall be made upon the occupant of the premises
to whom it is directed by either delivering a true copy of same to such
occupant personally or by delivering same to and leaving it with any person in
charge of the premises, or in case no such person is found upon the premises,
by affixing a copy thereof in a conspicuous place on the door to the entrance
of the said premises. Whenever it may be necessary to serve such an order upon
the owner of the premises, such order may be served either by delivering to and
leaving with said person a true copy of the said order, or, if such owner is
absent from the jurisdiction of the office making the order, by mailing him
such copy to the owner's last known post office address. (1963 Code § 7-904)
CHAPTER 7
TALL GRASS AND WEEDS
SECTION:
4-7-1: Title
4-7-2: Purpose And Intent
4-7-3: Definitions
4-7-4: Land Subject To Regulations
4-7-5: Tall Grass And Weeds/Noxious Weeds
4-7-6: Prohibition On Deposit Or Accumulation Of Yard Waste/Vegetation Debris
4-7-7: Enforcement
4-7-8: Declaration Of Nuisance
4-7-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the CITY OF CRAIGMONT TALL GRASS AND WEEDS
ORDINANCE and may be so cited. (Ord. 417, 3-1-2016)
4-7-2: PURPOSE AND INTENT:
The City of Craigmont hereby finds that tall grass and weeds are a nuisance,
can have a blighting effect on neighborhoods, and can provide a refuge for
vermin and insects. The purpose of this chapter is to secure the public health,
safety and general welfare of the residents and property owners of the City of
Craigmont by regulating the height grass and weeds are allowed to grow in the
City of Craigmont. (Ord. 417, 3-1-2016)
4-7-3: DEFINITIONS:
 
                           Any type of grass or weed, but not including: a)
                           crops grown as a source of income, including but not
                           limited to corn, oats, hay, wheat or barley, or b)
GRASS:                     ornamental grasses intentionally planted and
                           maintained by the lot or parcel owner solely for
                           ornamental purposes so long as the same do not
                           otherwise constitute a fire hazard, detriment to
                           public health or nuisance.
                           The use of land for tilling of the soil, the raising
LAND USED FOR AGRICULTURE: of field or tree crops or animal husbandry, as a
                           source of income.
 
 
                      Any plant having the potential to cause injury to public
NOXIOUS WEEDS:        health, crops, livestock, land or other property; which
                      is designated as noxious by the State of Idaho and/or
                      Lewis County.
                      Any person who has the right to occupy a parcel of
OCCUPANT:             property due to being an owner or pursuant to a verbal or
                      written lease or rental agreement with the owner or agent
                      thereof.
                      Any person holding an ownership interest in land in the
                      City of Craigmont upon which there is tall grass growing.
OWNER:                For the purposes of this chapter, the name and address
                      listed on the County Tax Assessment Roll shall indicate
                      ownership interest in such land.
TALL GRASS AND WEEDS: Any grass or weed whose height exceeds ten inches (10")
                      above ground level grade.
                      Any plant, which in the opinion of the Craigmont City
                      Council, or its designee, designated as noxious by the
WEEDS:                Idaho Department of Agriculture, including grass over ten
                      inches (10") in height, other than that part of a
                      vegetable or flower garden, is regarded as a common
                      nuisance. (Ord. 417, 3-1-2016; amd. Ord. 445, 5-7-2024)
 
4-7-4: LAND SUBJECT TO REGULATIONS:
This chapter does not apply to the following:
   A.   Land used for agricultural or pasture purposes, including weeds in
fields devoted to growing any small grain crops such as wheat, oats, barley or
rye.
   B.   Portions of lots used for flower gardens, shrubbery or vegetable
gardens.
   C.   Naturally wooded areas, wetlands or meadows.
   D.   Areas designated by the Craigmont City Council as undeveloped open
space. (Ord. 417, 3-1-2016)
4-7-5: TALL GRASS AND WEEDS/NOXIOUS WEEDS:
   A.   Prohibition On Tall Grass And Weeds: It shall be unlawful for the owner
or occupant of any lot or parcel of land within the city to cause, allow,
permit or suffer any tall grass and weeds to remain standing or growing on such
lot or parcel. It shall be the duty of all said owners and/or occupants either
to cut down or otherwise dispose of by lawful means all tall grass and weeds,
as defined in this chapter, which are standing or growing upon said lot or
parcel, and to prevent said tall grass and weeds from perpetuating themselves
and from becoming an nuisance, fire hazard or detriment to public health.
   B.   Prohibition Of Noxious Weeds: It shall be the duty and responsibility
of all landowners to control noxious weeds on their land and property as
provided by Idaho law. The cost of controlling noxious weeds shall be the
obligation of the land owner. It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly
fail to control noxious weeds on any lot or parcel owned by the person in the
manner provided by Idaho law. (Ord. 445, 5-7-2024)
4-7-6: PROHIBITION ON DEPOSIT OR ACCUMULATIONS OF YARD WASTE/VEGETATION DEBRIS:
It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of any lot or parcel of land to
cause, allow, permit or suffer the deposit or accumulation upon any portion of
such lot or parcel of land, of any brush, yard debris, dead vegetation, or cut
grass or weeds so as to create a nuisance due to unsightliness, an unhealthy or
unsafe condition, traffic hazard or fire hazard. (Ord. 417, 3-1-2016; amd. Ord.
445, 5-7-2024)
4-7-7: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Enforcement Officer: This chapter shall be enforced by such persons who
shall be so designated by the Craigmont City Council.
   B.   Right Of Entry: The Ordinance Enforcement Officer, and his or her
authorized representatives, are hereby empowered to enter upon any premises or
land in the City of Craigmont for the purpose of inspecting, removing and/or
destroying of tall grass and weeds prohibited under this chapter. No person
shall molest or interfere with such person or persons while they are engaged in
carrying out the provisions of this chapter.
   C.   Violation Notice: After inspection, if any property is determined to be
in violation of this chapter, a violation notice will be sent to the property
owner and/or occupant of said premises. The notice shall be sent by both first
class mail and/or by posting a copy of said notice on the property. The notice
shall give the property owner seven (7) days from the date of the notice to cut
the tall grass and/or weeds.
   D.   Failure To Comply: If the tall grass and weeds are not cut within seven
(7) days after the mailing and/or posting of a violation notice, the City of
Craigmont shall have the authority to enter upon the land and/or to cause the
lawn to be mowed by an authorized representative. Said authorized
representative is hereby empowered to enter upon any premises or land in the
City of Craigmont for the purpose of mowing tall grass and weeds in violation
of this chapter even if the property owner and/or occupant failed to actually
receive said notice. The City of Craigmont, its agents and representatives,
shall not be responsible for damage to buildings, vehicles, landscape, trees,
shrubs, etc., during the mowing of property in violation of this chapter.
   E.   Assessment Of Costs: All expenses of such cutting, to include equipment
usage, transportation, man-hours involved and overhead, including any and all
cost incurred in the removal or relocation of debris, junk or other
miscellaneous obstructions which would be necessary or convenient to carry out
the requirements of this chapter shall be paid by the owner of such land plus
an administrative charge of fifteen percent (15%) thereof per residential
parcel, per cutting. The City of Craigmont shall submit a bill to the property
owner for the cost of such cutting. If the property owner does not pay the bill
within thirty (30) days of the date of the invoice the cost of such payment
shall be charged against the premises and it shall become a lien created by
general law for taxes. (Ord. 417, 3-1-2016)
4-7-8: DECLARATION OF NUISANCE:
Any violation of any provision of this chapter is hereby declared to be
nuisance and the City of Craigmont may seek enforcement of this chapter by suit
for injunction, damages or other appropriate legal action, as against a
nuisance, pursuant to all relevant provisions of Idaho law. (Ord. 417, 3-1-
2016)
TITLE 5
PUBLIC SAFETY
Law Enforcement   1
Fire Department   2
Minors   3

CHAPTER 1
LAW ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
5-1-1: Law Enforcement Contracted With County
5-1-1: LAW ENFORCEMENT CONTRACTED WITH COUNTY:
Pursuant to an intergovernmental agreement, the city has contracted with the
Lewis County sheriff's department to enforce state statutes and county and city
ordinances, including, but not limited to, traffic enforcement and criminal and
civil enforcement. (2010 Code)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
5-2-1: Definitions
5-2-2: Department Created; Officers
5-2-3: Chief Of Fire Department
5-2-4: Assistant Chiefs And Departmental Officers
5-2-5: Department Membership
5-2-6: Authority To Adopt Bylaws
5-2-7: Reimbursement Of Expenses
5-2-8: Apparatus And Equipment
5-2-9: Fire Alarms
5-2-10: Mutual Aid Agreements
5-2-11: Fire Calls Outside City
5-2-12: Vehicles Of Members
5-2-13: Prohibited Acts By Individuals
5-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meanings of terms used
in this chapter shall be as follows:
CHIEF: The appointed chief of the Craigmont volunteer fire department.
CITY: The city of Craigmont, Idaho.
COUNCIL OR CITY COUNCIL: The city council of Craigmont, Idaho.
DEPARTMENT: The Craigmont volunteer fire department. (1963 Code § 3-202)
5-2-2: DEPARTMENT CREATED; OFFICERS:
   A.   Creation: A department to be hereinafter known as the Craigmont
volunteer fire department, the object of which shall be prevention of fire and
protection of life and property within the city limits, is hereby created. The
fire department shall be a division of the department of public protection and
shall be under the supervision of the commissioner of public protection. (1963
Code § 3-201)
   B.   Officers: The department shall consist of a chief, a first assistant
chief, a second assistant chief, a secretary-treasurer, and such other officers
as the chief and the city council may deem necessary for the effective
operation of the department. (1963 Code § 3-203)
5-2-3: CHIEF OF FIRE DEPARTMENT:
   A.   Selection; Qualifications:
      1.   The membership of the Craigmont volunteer fire department shall
elect from their own membership a person to be recommended to the city council
for appointment as chief of the department. The person chosen shall be elected
by a majority of the membership of the department present and voting at said
election. The person so recommended shall, upon confirmation and approval of
the city council, be appointed by the council as chief of the department.
      2.   The chief shall be technically qualified by training and experience
and shall have the ability to command individuals and hold their respect and
confidence. (1963 Code § 3-204)
   B.   Term Of Office: The chief shall serve for a term of two (2) years and
may be from time to time rerecommended and reappointed. (1963 Code § 3-205)
   C.   Accountability; Report To Council: The chief shall be accountable to
the city council only and shall make written and verbal reports thereto as the
council may require. (1963 Code § 3-206)
   D.   Removal Of Chief: The chief cannot be removed from office during his
term except by a written notice served upon the fire chief setting forth the
grounds and charges against him. The grounds and charges may be preferred by
the city council, or by a majority of the membership of the Craigmont volunteer
fire department. Then the said fire chief cannot be removed unless he shall
have had a hearing with the right to defend himself against the charges, and a
vote of a majority of the members of the city council. (1963 Code § 3-209)
   E.   Duties Of Chief:
      1.   The chief shall be responsible to the city council for the
personnel, morale, and general efficiency of the department. (1963 Code § 3-
210)
      2.   The chief shall, at least once monthly, conduct suitable drills and
instruction: in the operation and handling of equipment; first aid in rescue
work; salvage; a study of the buildings in the city; fire prevention, water
supplies; and all other matters generally considered essential to good
firemanship and safety of life and property from fire. Weather conditions not
permitting, drills shall consist of discussion of firefighting equipment and
apparatus. (1963 Code § 3-210; amd. 2010 Code)
      3.   The chief is hereby required to assist the proper authorities in
suppressing the crime of arson by investigating or causing to be investigated
the cause, origin and circumstances of all fires.
      4.   The chief is hereby empowered to enter any and all buildings and
premises at any reasonable hour for the purpose of making inspections and to
serve written notice upon the owner or occupant to abate, within a specified
time, any and all fire hazards that may be found.
      5.   Any person so served with a notice to abate any fire hazards shall
comply therewith and promptly notify the chief.
      6.   The chief shall see that complete records are kept of all fires,
inspections, apparatus and minor equipment, personnel and other information
about the work of the department
      7.   The chief shall report quarterly to the city council: the condition
of the apparatus and equipment; the number of fires during the quarter, their
location and cause, the date of same and the loss occasioned thereby, the
number and purpose of all other runs made; the number of members responding to
each fire or other run and any changes in membership.
      8.   The chief shall make a complete annual report to the city council at
the last meeting at the close of the fiscal year, such report to include the
information specified in subsection E7 of this section, together with
comparative data for previous years and recommendations for improving the
effectiveness of the department.
      9.   The chief of the fire department shall be the chief executive
officer of the department, subject to the rules and regulations and orders of
the fire department and the city council, and shall have under such conditions,
control and command of all property belonging to the department and of all
subordinates in the service. He shall enforce the faithful observance of the
ordinances of the city and the rules and regulations of the fire department.
      10.   It shall be the duty of the chief of the fire department to see
that all property and apparatus provided for the use of the fire department is
protected from violence and kept clean, in good repair and in perfect condition
for immediate use, and to see that the fire plugs or hydrants of the city are
in good working order. (1963 Code § 3-210)
      11.   At all fires, the chief of the fire department shall have sole
command, and all members of the fire department and all law enforcement
officers shall, during the continuance of any fire, be subject to his order. He
may, when deemed necessary for extinguishment of any fire, call to his aid any
person present, age eighteen (18) years or older, and it shall be the duty of
every person so called upon by the chief of the fire department to render him
prompt service; provided, however, that in the absence of the chief or
assistant chiefs, the first firefighter to arrive upon the scene of said fire
shall be in command therewith until the arrival of the chief or assistant
chiefs or superior officer in the fire department. (1963 Code § 3-210; amd.
2010 Code)
5-2-4: ASSISTANT CHIEFS AND DEPARTMENTAL OFFICERS:
   A.   Selection; Accountable To Chief; Term:
      1.   The assistant chiefs and all other departmental officers except the
chief shall be elected by the members of the Craigmont volunteer fire
department from its own membership, and said persons shall be chosen by a
majority vote of members present and voting at said election and shall not be
subject to confirmation by the city council. Such officers shall be accountable
to the chief and subject to removal by majority vote of the members of the
Craigmont volunteer fire department.
      2.   The assistant chiefs and all other departmental officers shall be
elected for a term of two (2) years. (1963 Code § 3-207)
   B.   Duties Of Assistant Chiefs:
      1.   The first assistant chief and second assistant chief shall report to
the chief at fires and assist him in the discharge of his duties.
      2.   In the absence of the chief, the first assistant chief shall command
the department and be held responsible therefor in all respects with the full
powers and responsibilities of the chief.
      3.   In the absence of both the chief and first assistant chief, the
second assistant chief shall command the department with the full powers and
responsibilities of the chief. (1963 Code § 3-211)
   C.   Special Officers: The department may elect a president, vice president,
and secretary-treasurer, to be known as social officers. Such officers may be
elected in any manner and for any term the membership may decide upon, and
their duties shall be to arrange for and manage any or all social functions
sponsored by the department. (1963 Code § 3-233)
5-2-5: DEPARTMENT MEMBERSHIP:
   A.   Composition; Qualifications: The membership of the department shall
consist of not less than twelve (12) nor more than fifteen (15) persons,
including the chief and departmental officers, as may be elected to membership
by a majority of the membership of the Craigmont volunteer fire department, and
shall be able bodied citizens at least eighteen (18) years of age residing
within the city of Craigmont, preferably property owners whose business
activities are normally within the confines of the city of Craigmont and who
have telephones in their homes. Provided however, all present members of the
Craigmont volunteer fire department, irrespective of this subsection, are
hereby granted membership in the Craigmont volunteer fire department
established by this chapter. Provided further, that in addition to the maximum
membership of the department above set forth, the department is hereby
authorized to associate in membership five (5) additional persons who shall be
known as "standby firefighters". Standby firefighters shall attend all drills,
lectures, fire runs and alarms of the department. The status of standby
firefighters in the department shall be determined by the bylaws, rules and
regulations that the department is hereinafter authorized to make. (1963 Code §
3-212; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Suspension Or Discharge Of Members: Any member of the department may be
suspended or discharged from the department on charges preferred by the chief
to the membership of the department at any time the chief may deem such action
necessary for the good of the department. Such member shall not be discharged
unless a majority of the members of the department at a regular meeting shall
vote by secret ballot to discharge such member from membership. (1963 Code § 3-
213)
   C.   Members Issued Badge: Each member of the department shall be issued a
badge designating his rank. (1963 Code § 3-224)
   D.   Special Police Powers Granted: All regularly appointed members of the
department are hereby given the necessary special police powers for the purpose
of enforcing the provisions of this chapter. (1963 Code § 3-231)
5-2-6: AUTHORITY TO ADOPT BYLAWS:
The volunteer fire department is hereby authorized to adopt bylaws, rules and
regulations for the administration of the department not in conflict with the
laws of the state or the ordinances of the city. These bylaws, rules and
regulations shall be effective when approved by the city council and a copy
filed with the city clerk-treasurer. The membership of the Craigmont volunteer
fire department shall, within thirty (30) days after the effective date hereof,
adopt a set of bylaws, rules and regulations of the department. (1963 Code § 3-
214)
5-2-7: REIMBURSEMENT OF EXPENSES:
The reimbursement to be paid by the city to the fire department shall be in
addition to other reimbursements elsewhere provided in other ordinances of the
city, as follows:
   A.   The fire department shall receive for each member attending each drill
or lecture meeting a sum to be determined by resolution of the city council.
Attendance shall be determined by roll call by the secretary-treasurer
forthwith after the meeting has been called to order. The department shall
receive no reimbursement for members not present at said drill or meeting.
   B.   The department shall also receive reimbursement from the city when
actually engaged in fighting fires or when responding to a fire alarm, in an
amount as may be determined by city resolution. The city volunteer firefighters
shall not be considered employees of the city for any purpose. (Ord. 305, 5-1-
1984; amd. 2010 Code)
5-2-8: APPARATUS AND EQUIPMENT:
   A.   City Equipment: The department shall be equipped with the firefighting
apparatus and equipment as the city now owns and that which may be acquired
from time to time to maintain its efficiency and properly protect life and
property from fire. (1963 Code § 3-216)
   B.   Purchase Of Equipment: Recommendations of apparatus and equipment
needed shall be made by the chief and, after approval by the city council,
shall be purchased in such manner as may be designated by the city council.
(1963 Code § 3-217)
   C.   Housing Of Equipment: All equipment of the department shall be safely
and conveniently housed in such places as may be designated by the city
council. (1963 Code § 3-218)
   D.   Private Use Of Equipment Prohibited: No person shall use any fire
apparatus or equipment for any private purpose, nor shall any person wilfully
and without proper authority take away or conceal any article used in any way
by the department. (1963 Code § 3-220)
   E.   Unauthorized Persons Prohibited: No person shall enter any place where
fire apparatus is housed or handle any apparatus or equipment belonging to the
department unless accompanied by, or having special permission of, an officer
or authorized member of the department. (1963 Code § 3-221)
5-2-9: FIRE ALARMS:
Suitable arrangement or equipment shall be provided for citizens to turn in an
alarm, and for notifying all members of the department so that they may
promptly respond. (1963 Code § 3-219)
5-2-10: MUTUAL AID AGREEMENTS:
The fire department of the city is hereby authorized to enter into agreements
or contracts with nearby incorporated communities in the establishment of a
mutual aid system. All contracts and agreements shall have the proper approval
of the city council before they shall become effective. (1963 Code § 3-222)
5-2-11: FIRE CALLS OUTSIDE CITY:
No apparatus shall be hired out or permitted to leave the city except to
protect property in which the city has a legal obligation, either through
ownership, lease, rental or permissive use, or in response to a call for aid at
a fire in a neighboring community, and then only with the consent of the mayor
or, in his absence from the community, the commissioner of public protection.
The officer in charge of the department shall have the power to assign
equipment for response to calls for outside aid in accordance with this chapter
where the absence of such equipment will not jeopardize the fire protection in
the city. Provided however, that in general, only one fire truck shall be
permitted to leave at any one time for any cause unless the city is otherwise
protected by companies of other communities "covering in" as may be scheduled
in a mutual aid agreement. (1963 Code § 3-223)
5-2-12: VEHICLES OF MEMBERS:
   A.   Right Of Way: All motor equipment and all personal vehicles of
department members shall have right of way over all other traffic when
responding to an alarm. (1963 Code § 3-225; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Insignia Issued: Each member of the department driving a vehicle shall
be issued a suitable insignia to be attached to the vehicle. (1963 Code § 3-
226; amd. 2010 Code)
5-2-13: PROHIBITED ACTS BY INDIVIDUALS:
   A.   Driving Over Fire Hose: No person shall drive any vehicle over a fire
hose except upon specific orders from the chief or other officer in charge
where the hose is used. (1963 Code § 3-227)
   B.   Parking Near Fire Hydrant Or Station: No person shall park any vehicle
or otherwise cause any obstruction to be placed within twenty feet (20') of the
entrance to any fire station or other place where fire apparatus is stored, or
within twenty feet (20') of any fire hydrant or cistern. (1963 Code § 3-228)
   C.   Following Fire Truck Or Parking Near Fire: No unauthorized person with
any vehicle shall follow within three hundred feet (300') of any apparatus
belonging to the department, nor park any vehicle within three hundred feet
(300') of a fire. (1963 Code § 3-229)
   D.   False Alarms: No person shall maliciously turn in or cause to be turned
in a false alarm. (1963 Code § 3-230)
CHAPTER 3
MINORS
SECTION:
5-3-1: Curfew
5-3-2: Minors In Pool Halls
5-3-1: CURFEW:
   A.   Definitions: The following definitions shall apply to interpretation of
this section:
   LEGAL GUARDIAN: A person, other than a parent, having legal custody of a
minor.
   LOCAL TIME: Pacific Standard Time or Pacific Daylight Saving Time, as may be
in effect.
   MINOR: An unmarried person seventeen (17) years of age or under.
   OTHER CUSTODIAN: A person, other than a parent or legal guardian, to whom
legal or joint legal custody of the minor has been given by court order or who
is acting in loco parentis.
   PARENT: The biological or adoptive mother or father of a minor.
   PROPER WRITTEN PERMISSION: A written instrument, made and signed by the
minor's parent, legal guardian or other custodian, stating all of the
following: 1) the name, address and telephone number of the minor and of the
person making the instrument; 2) the date the instrument was signed; 3) a
statement of the dates and times for which the permission is effective; and 4)
a statement as to the specific purpose permission was given.
   PUBLIC PLACE: 1) Any property within the city of Craigmont owned by any
federal, state or local governmental entity, or political subdivision thereof,
including school districts and schools; and 2) public parks, streets, alleys,
sidewalks and rights of way; and 3) those portions of parking lots, situated on
private property, which are open to the public.
   B.   Prohibited Hours; Exceptions: It shall be unlawful for any minor to be
at or upon any public place within the city at the following times:
      1.   After ten thirty o'clock (10:30) P.M. local time on Sunday, Monday,
Tuesday, Wednesday and Thursday of each week; and until six o'clock (6:00) A.M.
local time the following morning.
      2.   After twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight local time Friday and Saturday
of each week and until six o'clock (6:00) A.M. local time the following
morning.
      3.   The provisions of subsections B1 and B2 of this section shall not
apply to minors:
         a.   In attendance at or going immediately to or from, without detour
or stop, an event sanctioned by a governmental entity, school, religious, civic
or fraternal organization; or
         b.   Who are accompanied by and under the immediate supervision of a
parent, legal guardian or other custodian; or
         c.   Who have in their possession an effective proper written
permission from the minor's parent, legal guardian, or other custodian,
evidencing said person's granting of permission to the minor to travel to or
from, or to be present at or upon a public place during the times prohibited by
subsections B1 and B2 of this section, as may be applicable, for a specific
purpose, and any such permission shall be effective for accomplishing the
stated specific purpose only. Provided, however, that no written permission
shall be effective more than five (5) days after the written instrument was
signed by the person making the instrument or after the specific purpose for
which permission was given has been fulfilled, whichever shall first occur; or
         d.   When the presence of the minor is connected with and required by
some business, trade, profession or occupation in which said minor is lawfully
engaged, including, but not limited to, agriculture; or
         e.   Who are involved in emergencies involving threat or injury to
life, health or property.
   C.   Encouraging Curfew Violations: It shall be unlawful for any person to
aid, abet or encourage a violation of this section.
   D.   Detention Of Minors; Notice To Parents Or Legal Guardians: Peace
officers shall have the authority to detain minors violating the provisions of
this section as provided for the detention of juveniles for misdemeanor
violations as set forth in Idaho Code title 20, chapter 5. If the peace officer
chooses to issue a uniform citation to violators pursuant to Idaho Code section
20-549, as amended, upon issuance of a uniform citation the peace officer shall
follow the procedures set forth in Idaho Code section 20-549, as amended, with
respect to obtaining endorsements on the citation and providing notice of the
citation to the minor's parents or legal guardians.
   E.   Violation A Misdemeanor: Violations of this section shall constitute a
misdemeanor. (Ord. 382, 12-3-2002)
5-3-2: MINORS IN POOL HALLS:
It shall be unlawful for any proprietor, manager or employee of any public pool
or billiard hall or other business establishment wherein intoxicating liquor or
alcoholic beverages are sold to be consumed on the premises to permit or allow
any child or minor under the age of eighteen (18) years to frequent or loiter
in such establishment; provided, however, that the same shall not be illegal in
places of business that are duly licensed by the state of Idaho as restaurants.
(1963 Code § 6-126; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 4
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
5-4-1: Trapping Regulations
5-4-1: TRAPPING REGULATIONS:
   A.   Definitions:
   TRAP: Any mechanical device or snare which is designed to hold, capture,
and/or kill an animal including, but not limited to, live traps, steel jaw
foothold traps, padded jaw traps, body gripping (Conibear) traps, snares,
deadfalls, leg hold type traps, or similar devices.
   B.   Prohibited: Unless authorized by the Idaho department of fish and game,
pursuant to Idaho Code title 36, chapter 11, no person shall set a trap to
catch an animal (other than skunks, fox squirrels, mice, rats, gophers, voles
or moles) within city limits, except a person specifically authorized by the
council or law enforcement personnel or designee.
   C.   Penalties: Any person violating these provisions shall be deemed guilty
of an infraction and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished pursuant to
this code and the Idaho Code, unless otherwise specifically provided for. (Ord.
2013-411, 5-7-2013)
ARTICLE A. DOGS
SECTION:
5-4A-1: Purpose
5-4A-2: Definitions
5-4A-3: Dog Licensing Requirements; Fees
5-4A-4: Kennel Operation License
5-4A-5: Rabies Quarantine
5-4A-6: Impoundment; Disposition; Fees
5-4A-7: Running At Large Prohibited
5-4A-8: Female Dogs In Heat
5-4A-9: Dangerous Dogs; Restrictions; Licensing
5-4A-10: Additional Offenses
5-4A-11: Enforcement; Animal Control Officers
5-4A-12: Interference Prohibited
5-4A-13: Immunity For City Officials
5-4A-14: Violations; Penalties
5-4A-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this article is to provide for regulation of the harboring of
dogs within the city limits, to promote public safety and welfare of the
citizens of the city, and to promote the welfare of dogs harbored within the
city limits. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996)
5-4A-2: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context otherwise indicates, the following words and terms, when
used in this article, shall mean:
ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER: The Lewis County sheriff, his deputies, and/or other
authorized representatives.
AT LARGE/RUN AT LARGE: A dog is "at large" or "running at large" if it is off
its harborer's premises and not under control of a person.
BITE: Any closure by an animal's mouth causing a redness, breaking, or tearing
of the skin of any person or which materially damages or destroys the personal
property of another.
COMMERCIAL KENNEL: Any Premises or portion thereof on which three (3) or more
dogs are maintained, harbored, possessed, trained, bred, boarded or cared for
in return for compensation.
DANGEROUS DOG: Any dog that:
   A.   Without justified provocation has inflicted serious injury on a person;
or
   B.   Has been previously found to be at risk and thereafter bites or
physically attacks a person without justified provocation.
DOG: Any member, male or female, of the family of canis familiaris.
HARBOR, HARBORING: To own or keep a dog within the city limits of the city of
Craigmont. It shall be prima facie evidence that a person is harboring a dog
for the purposes of this article if the person: a) is listed as the owner or
harborer of the dog within the city of Craigmont on any application for dog
licensing; or b) is over eighteen (18) years of age and resides at or is in
physical control of a premises, or part thereof, on which a dog remains, or to
which it customarily returns daily for food and shelter, for three (3)
consecutive days or more.
HARBORER: Any person who owns a dog or keeps a dog within the city limits of
the city of Craigmont. The parents shall be presumed to be the owner of any dog
in the possession, custody or control of the parent's child.
HARBORER'S PREMISES: All real property under a harborer's ownership, lease, or
control inside the inner line of a sidewalk, or if there is no sidewalk, inside
the curb, ditch, or shoulder marking the edge of the traveled or used portion
of the public right of way. "Premises" also includes the inside of a closed
motor vehicle.
JUSTIFIED PROVOCATION: An act or omission that a reasonable person with common
knowledge of dog behavior would conclude is likely to precipitate a bite or
attack by an ordinary dog.
LEASH: A leash, lead, cord, or chain not more than ten feet (10') in length, by
which a dog is physically controlled by the person accompanying it.
NEUTERED DOG: Any male or female dog rendered incapable of reproducing
offspring by surgery or other veterinary medical procedure.
NONCOMMERCIAL KENNEL: Any kennel which is not commercial kennel as defined
above.
OWNER: Legal owner of a dog.
PHYSICALLY ATTACK: An aggressive action upon a person by a dog in which there
is physical contact between the dog and the person.
SERIOUS INJURY: An injury to a person characterized by bruising, laceration, or
other injury that would cause a reasonably prudent person to seek treatment
from a medical professional without regard to whether the person actually
sought medical treatment.
UNDER CONTROL: A dog is under control if:
   A.   The dog is confined within the boundaries of the harborer's premises;
or
   B.   The dog is not on the harborer's premises but is: 1) confined within a
vehicle; or 2) in the control of a responsible person by use of a leash not
exceeding ten feet (10') in length.
VETERINARY CLINIC OR HOSPITAL: Any establishment maintained and operated by a
licensed veterinarian for the boarding of animals or the diagnosis, treatment,
and care of diseased or injured animals. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996; amd. 2010 Code;
Ord. 429, 11-7-2023)
5-4A-3: DOG LICENSING REQUIREMENTS; FEES:
   A.   License Required:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to harbor a dog within the city
limits not licensed as provided by this article.
      2.   No license shall be required for dogs which are harbored within the
city limits by the owner thereof, if the owner: a) is not a resident of the
city; and b) the dog is harbored less than thirty (30) consecutive days within
the city; and c) the dog is validly licensed by another governmental licensing
authority.
   B.   Application And Information Required:
      1.   All licenses required under this article shall be issued by the
clerk-treasurer. In addition to payment of all required fees, all applicants
for dog licenses shall provide the following information to the clerk-treasurer
as a condition precedent to issuance of a license:
         a.   The name, address, and phone number of the owner;
         b.   The name, address, and phone number of the harborer if different
from the owner;
         c.   The name, age, breed, and gender of the dog;
         d.   An accurate photograph of the dog or a written description of the
weight, size, color, and distinguishing characteristics of the dog;
         e.   Whether the dog has been neutered;
         f.   Proof of current rabies vaccination; and
         g.   Whether the dog has been declared a dangerous or vicious dog by
any governmental authority.
      2.   It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly provide false
information on any application or in applying for any license under this
article.
      3.   Except as may be directed by resolution of the city council, the
clerk-treasurer shall refuse to issue or renew a license to any person who:
         a.   Fails to provide any information required to be submitted under
subsection A of this section or fails to pay the required license fee;
         b.   Knowingly provides false information in making application for
any license under this article; or
         c.   Applies for licensing of a dog that has been declared dangerous
or vicious dog by any governmental authority if disclosed by the applicant or
otherwise made known to the clerk- treasurer. Nothing herein shall require the
city clerk-treasurer to undertake any independent inquiry of this issue with
any person or governmental authority other than the applicant.
      4.   In the event the city clerk-treasurer shall deny the applicant a
license or renewal, the applicant may apply to the city council for issuance of
a license. The city council may issue said license by resolution of the council
on such terms and conditions the city council shall deem in the best interest
of the city.
   C.   License Fees:
      1.   All dog license fees and cost shall be set by resolution by the City
Council.
      2.   No lifetime licenses shall be issued.
      3.   All licenses issued under this article shall expire at twelve
o'clock (12:00) midnight, December 31 of the year for which the license is
issued. A license for the succeeding calendar year may be obtained prior to
expiration of the current year's license but shall not be effective until the
expiration of the current license. No part of any dog license fee shall be
refundable.
