      4.   Any annual city dog license purchased for the 1996 licensing year
shall be valid until twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight, December 31, 1996, at
which time said license shall expire and renewal shall be required under this
article. Any "lifetime" city dog license purchased prior to the effective date
hereof shall be valid for a period of five (5) years from the effective date
hereof, and shall thereafter be deemed expired.
   D.   Collar And Valid Tag Required: Every dog harbored within the city
limits shall at all times wear a substantial, durable collar to which shall be
securely attached a valid current license tag issued by the city for the dog
wearing the tag as provided in this article.
   E.   Prohibited Tags; Exceptions; Transfer Prohibited:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to allow a dog harbored by the
person to wear any license tag or indicia of licensing other than a valid
license tag issued under this article for the dog wearing the tag. This
subsection shall not prohibit the wearing of nonlicense tags for the purpose of
identification, proof of vaccination, or similar tags if the dog is wearing a
valid current license tag issued under this article for the dog.
      2.   All licenses and tags issued under this article or predecessor
ordinances shall be nontransferable.
      3.   It shall be unlawful for any person to transfer or attempt to
transfer to another person any license or tag issued under this article or
predecessor ordinances.
   F.   Maximum Number Of Dogs Per Household: There shall be no more than two
(2) licensed dogs permitted per household or per harborer, unless the same is
qualified and licensed as a kennel. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996; amd. Ord. 439, 11-7-
2023)
5-4A-4: KENNEL OPERATION LICENSE:
No person shall operate or maintain a commercial or noncommercial kennel within
the city without first obtaining a license therefor as provided in this
chapter. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996; amd. Ord. 439, 11-7-2023)
5-4A-5: RABIES QUARANTINE:
   A.   Quarantine Authorized: The animal control officer shall have the
authority to order the harborer of any dog showing symptoms of rabies or any
dog which has bitten any person to take the dog to the city pound,
veterinarian, or any other place in the business of boarding dogs for
quarantine for a period not to exceed fifteen (15) days, or for such other
periods as indicated by a licensed veterinarian as necessary to determine if
the subject dog is infected with rabies.
   B.   Dog Determined Free Of Rabies; Payment Of Fee: If the dog is determined
to be free of rabies, the dog shall be returned to the harborer upon payment of
one hundred percent (100%) of the regular fee for keeping dogs impounded.
   C.   Failure To Pay Fee; Disposal Of Dog: If the fee is not paid, the dog
shall be subject to disposal as provided in this article.
   D.   Alternative To Impoundment: In lieu of submitting the dog to
impoundment, the harborer may at their expense admit the dog to a licensed
veterinarian for examination and provide the city with a certification that the
dog is free from rabies.
   E.   Disposal Of Dog Afflicted With Rabies: Any dog afflicted with rabies
shall be disposed of immediately, either by the harborer or the animal control
officer. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996)
5-4A-6: IMPOUNDMENT; DISPOSITION; FEES:
   A.   Impoundment Authorized; Notice To Owner:
      1.   All dogs running at large within the city limits may be impounded by
the animal control officer by the use of a tranquilizer gun or other humane
means of dog control.
      2.   If a dog is impounded, the animal control officer shall undertake a
reasonable inquiry to determine the identity of the owner or harborer of the
dog. Reasonable inquiry shall consist of and be limited to: a) examining any
tags affixed to any collar worn by the dog at the time of impoundment; and b)
examining the dog licensing records of the city. In the event the identity of
the owner or harborer of the dog is determined from said inquiry, the animal
control officer shall serve the owner or harborer of the dog with written
notice of the impoundment by: a) personal service; or b) regular first class
U.S. mail addressed to the last known mailing address of the owner or harborer
as shown by the records of the city clerk-treasurer, which service being
effective on the date of mailing. No such notice shall be required if the
identity of the owner or harborer is not determined from said inquiry.
      3.   The owner or harborer of any dog which may be taken up and impounded
under the provisions of this article may recover possession of the dog upon
payment to the city of any license fees, impoundment fees, and other costs
provided in this article.
   B.   Disposition Of Impounded Dogs: If the owner or harborer of any
impounded dog fails to pay any required fees and costs under this article
within seven (7) days after the date of service of any written notice required
under this section, or within five (5) days of the date of impoundment if no
notice is required, the animal control officer may dispose of the dog:
      1.   By delivering it to any person who will pay all fees and costs due;
or
      2.   By destroying the dog in a humane manner.
   C.   Fees Imposed; Payment Prior To Release: Impounded dogs shall not be
released until the owner or the harborer pays to the city clerk-treasurer:
      1.   Ten dollars ($10.00) capture fee;
      2.   Five dollars ($5.00) per day impoundment fee each day of
impoundment;
      3.   If the dog has not been issued a valid current city dog license
required under this article, a license fee as provided by this article;
      4.   Any other reasonable costs and expenses of impoundment incurred by
the city in impounding the dog, including any veterinary expenses reasonably
incurred. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996)
5-4A-7: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any harborer of a dog to permit a harbored dog to:
   A.   Be or run at large; or
   B.   Go or remain upon any public premises not owned by, leased by, or in
the control of the harborer without the consent of the owner or occupier of the
private premises. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996)
5-4A-8: FEMALE DOGS IN HEAT:
All persons harboring any female dog shall keep it shut up when in heat. Any
female dog running at large at such season may be disposed of by the animal
control officer without giving any notice required under section 5-4A-6 of this
article, or otherwise. The animal control officer may also dispose of, by
destroying in a humane manner, any dog found running at large which, in the
judgment of the animal control officer:
   A.   Displays symptoms of contagious disease; or
   B.   Displays serious physical injury or illness such that the animal
control officer deems, in the officer's sole discretion, that it is necessary
to destroy the dog to prevent further suffering; or
   C.   Displays vicious or aggressive behavior which poses an imminent risk of
physical injury to any person, and the dog cannot, in the discretion of the
animal control officer, be taken into control for impoundment by reasonably
humane methods. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996)
5-4A-9: DANGEROUS DOGS; RESTRICTIONS; LICENSING:
   A.   Keeping Restricted:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to harbor a dangerous dog within
the city limits, except as provided in this article.
      2.   The city clerk-treasurer shall not issue or renew any dog license
for any dog that has been declared dangerous by the city, or dangerous,
vicious, or other similar classifications by any governmental authority, except
as may be provided by resolution of the city council.
   B.   Dangerous Dog Declaration; Appeal:
      1.   The animal control officer may declare a dog to be a dangerous dog
if, upon investigation of any complaint, incident, or information otherwise
provided, the animal control officer finds that:
         a.   The dog is a “dangerous dog” as defined by this chapter; or
         b.   The dog has been declared a dangerous dog, other similar
declaration by any governmental authority.
   Notwithstanding the foregoing, no dog may be found or declared to be a
dangerous or at-risk dog when, at the time an injury or damage was sustained,
the precipitating cause constituted justified provocation. Justified
provocation includes, but is not limited to, the following:
            (1)   The dog was protecting or defending a person within the
immediate vicinity of the dog from an attack or assault;
            (2)   The person was committing a crime or offense upon the
property of the owner or custodian of the dog;
            (3)   The person was at the time, or had in the past, willfully
tormented, abused or assaulted the dog;
            (4)   The dog was responding to pain or injury or protecting its
offspring;
            (5)   The dog was working as a hunting dog, herding dog, or
predator control dog on the property of, or under the control of, its owner or
keeper, and the damage or injury sustained was to a person who was interfering
with the dog while the dog was working in a place where it was lawfully engaged
in such activity, including public lands;
            (6)   The dog was a service animal individually trained to do work
or perform tasks for a person with a disability;
            (7)   The person was intervening between two (2) or more animals
engaged in aggressive behavior or fighting; or
            (8)   If otherwise contrary to Chapter 28, Title 25, Idaho Code.
      2.   If the animal control officer makes said declaration, the animal
control officer shall notify the owner or harborer of the declaration and the
manner and time limits in which an appeal of the declaration may be taken. Said
notice shall be in writing and served by: a) personal service; or b) regular
first class U.S. mail to the address of the known harborer as shown by the
records of the city clerk-treasurer, with service being effective on the date
of mailing.
      3.   The animal control officer may impound any dog declared to be
dangerous, including, but not limited to, impounding of the dog during the
pendency of any appeal proceeding. The owner and harborer of the dog shall be
liable for all costs and fees of impoundment regardless of the final
disposition of the case.
      4.   The owner or harborer of a dog declared dangerous shall have five
(5) business days from the date of service of the written declaration to
request a hearing appealing the declaration. The request for hearing shall be
in writing, identify the name, address and telephone number of the requesting
party, and shall be served upon the city clerk-treasurer within the time limit
above provided. In the event no hearing is requested within the time and in the
manner above provided, the animal control officer may dispose of the dog as
provided in subsection
5-4A-6B of this article without further notice to the owner or harborer.
      5.   If a hearing is requested, a hearing shall be held within seven (7)
days of the date the request for hearing is received by the city clerk-
treasurer, or at such other time as is agreed to by the requesting party.
         a.   The mayor and two (2) city council members appointed by the mayor
shall constitute the hearing panel and shall hear the appeal. The hearing shall
be informal and the "Idaho Rules Of Evidence" shall not apply. The owner,
harborer and the animal control officer or other representative of the city
shall be given the opportunity to submit evidence, present witnesses and be
heard on the matter, including the right to cross examination.
         b.   In determining whether the dog is dangerous, the hearing panel
may consider, among other evidence, past incidents, provocation for the
dangerous behavior, whether the conduct occurred on the premises where the dog
was harbored, the legal status of the alleged victim on the premises and any
other fact or allegation relating to the incident from which the declaration
arises.
      6.   If the hearing panel shall find that the declaration was proper, the
hearing panel may order disposition of the dog as deemed in the best interest
of the City and public safety, including but not limited to:
         a.   Directing the Animal Control Officer to destroy the dog in a
human manner as provided by §
5-4A-6 (B)(2) of this chapter;
         b.   Directing that the dog may be released to the owner or harborer
on such conditions as the hearing panel shall deem in the best interest of the
City and public safety, which may include, but are not limited to, that 1) the
dog will be removed from the City limits immediately following release and not
allowed to return; 2) requiring the owner or harborer to take steps sufficient
to confine the dog in a manner to prevent harm to the public; 3) requiring the
owner and harborer to provide a surety bond or proof of liability insurance for
compensation for those who may suffer injury by reason of harboring of a
dangerous dog; and 4) any other conditions, restrictions and limitations
applicable to judicial declarations for dangerous dogs provided in Idaho Code §
25-2810, as amended.
      7.   The decision of the hearing panel shall become final unless the
decision is appealed to the district court within three (3) days following the
date of decision. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996; amd. Ord. 439, 11-7-2023)
5-4A-10: ADDITIONAL OFFENSES:
In addition to other provisions of this article:
   A.   Offenses Enumerated: It shall be unlawful for any person harboring or
in control of a dog to:
      1.   Permit the dog to scatter garbage, refuse and debris;
      2.   Permit the dog to chase any person, vehicle, or domestic animal;
      3.   Permit the dog to deposit fecal material on any property not that of
its owner or harborer without immediately removing the same from the property;
      4.   Permit the dog to bark, howl, or otherwise cause noise in a manner
which unreasonably disturbs, or is likely to disturb, the peace and quiet of
any person;
      5.   Harbor one or more dogs in such a manner that the keeping of the dog
results in a nauseous, foul, or offensive odor or so as to create a public
nuisance; or
      6.   Harbor a dog and fail to provide the dog with food, water, shelter,
or necessary veterinary care, which shall include a rabies vaccination every
three (3) years.
   B.   Cruelty To Dogs: It shall be unlawful for any person to beat, abuse or
otherwise engage in cruel or inhumane treatment of a dog. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996)
5-4A-11: ENFORCEMENT; ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICERS:
   A.   Enforcement: Any peace officer or Lewis County sheriff's deputy is
hereby appointed and designated as an animal control officer of the city. In
addition to all authority granted to such officer for general enforcement of
laws as a peace officer, said officer is further authorized and directed to
enforce all provisions of this article and perform all duties of animal control
under this article. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Appointment Of Additional Persons: The city council may appoint such
additional persons as it deems necessary and proper to act as animal control
officer(s) who shall be under the supervision and control of the mayor. Any
such appointment shall be reflected in the minutes of the city council meetings
or by resolution of the city council. The compensation and terms and conditions
of contracting or employment of such person shall be determined from time to
time by the city council.
   C.   Actions Of Officers: All persons designated as animal control officers
under this article may undertake any action or duty as animal control officer
provided under this article concurrently, jointly, or individually. (Ord. 365,
10-1-1996)
5-4A-12: INTERFERENCE PROHIBITED:
   A.   Interfering With Officers: It shall be unlawful for any person to
knowingly hinder, molest, or interfere with any animal control officer in the
discharge of any of his duties under this article. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996)
   B.   Removal Of Dogs From Pound: It shall be unlawful and a general
misdemeanor for any person to attempt to remove or remove any dog or dogs from
the city pound or the possession of the animal control officer without the
consent of the animal control officer or otherwise as provided by this article.
(Ord. 365, 10-1-1996; amd. 2010 Code)
5-4A-13: IMMUNITY FOR CITY OFFICIALS:
The city, its officials, employees, animal control officers and agents shall
not be liable for any acts or commissions in performing duties arising from
this article and shall be immune from suit on any claims arising by reason of
any such alleged act or omission. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996)
5-4A-14: VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
   A.   Violations And Remedies Cumulative: The violations, punishments, and
remedies provided in this article shall be cumulative with other provisions of
this code, and state and federal laws, and the city may cause any conduct or
condition in violation of this article constituting a public nuisance to be
abated as a public nuisance in the manner provided by law.
   B.   Violations/Penalties: In addition to other penalties and remedies
provided by this chapter, which shall be cumulative, any person violating any
provision of this ordinance shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. Provided,
however, that any person in violation of § 5-4A-3(A), (D), (E) or (F), or § 5-
4A-4, of this chapter shall be guilty of an infraction. (Ord. 365, 10-1-1996;
amd. Ord. 439, 11-7-2023)
ARTICLE B. LIVESTOCK AND POULTRY
SECTION:
5-4B-1: Running At Large Prohibited
5-4B-2: Freeing Impounded Animals Prohibited
5-4B-3: Tying Livestock
5-4B-1: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
   A.   Livestock: It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any horse,
cattle, rabbit, goat, sheep, pig or hog or other livestock to run at large in
the city at any time during the year, and it shall be unlawful for anyone to
herd or drive any of the above named animals through the streets without having
said animals under control by means of rope, strap or other device by which
they may be led, unless such animal is being driven in harness or hauled. (1963
Code § 6-501; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Poultry: It shall be unlawful for any person to keep fowl or poultry
unless such fowl or poultry are at all times kept upon his own premises and in
enclosures. (1963 Code § 6-502)
5-4B-2: FREEING IMPOUNDED ANIMALS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful to break open or in any manner, directly or indirectly,
aid or assist in breaking open any pen or enclosure with intent of releasing
any animal confined therein pursuant to the provisions of this article. (1963
Code § 6-507)
5-4B-3: TYING LIVESTOCK:
It shall be unlawful for any person to tie livestock within reach of any
sidewalk or crosswalk or within reach of the fences, buildings, improvements,
trees or shrubbery of any other person within the city, or tie livestock to any
telephone, telegraph or utility pole within the city. (1963 Code § 6-503)
CHAPTER 5
RECREATIONAL VEHICLES AS DWELLINGS
SECTION:
5-5-1: Definitions
5-5-2: Prohibited Conduct
5-5-3: Temporary Occupancy Permit
5-5-4: Violations
5-5-1:   DEFINITIONS:
As used in the chapter, the following terms shall have the following means:
 
                              A lot, tract, parcel or other real property
PRIVATE PROPERTY:             situated within the city of Craigmont that is
                              not owned by a governmental entity.
                              A motor home, travel trailer, fifth-wheel
                              trailer, park model recreational vehicle,
                              truck camper or folding camping trailer, with
RECREATIONAL VEHICLE:         or without motive power, designed for
                              recreational or emergency occupancy. School
                              buses or van type vehicles which are
                              converted to recreational use, are defined as
                              recreational vehicles.
TOURIST COURT, TRAILER CAMP-  Have the same meaning as provided for such
AUTOMOBILE, TRAILER COACH and terms respectively in Craigmont City Code §
MOBILE HOME PARK:             10-1-6, as amended. (Ord. 433, 4-4-2023)
 
5-5-2:   PROHIBITED CONDUCT:
Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, it shall be unlawful for any person
to reside in, use or occupy any recreational vehicle as a habitation, dwelling
or place of abode on any private property for more than fourteen (14) days in
any calendar year except within an approved Tourist Court, Trailer Camp-
Automobile or Trailer Coach and Mobile Home Park. (Ord. 433, 4-4-2023)
5-5-3:   TEMPORARY OCCUPANCY PERMITS:
   A.   Authority To Issue Permits: The city council may issue temporary
occupancy permits authorizing temporary residing in, use and occupancy of any
recreational vehicle situated on private property otherwise prohibited under
this chapter as provided in this §
5-5-3 .
   B.   Temporary Occupancy Permits:
      1.   Applications - Fees: Applications for temporary occupancy permits
must be filed with the city clerk and shall be referred to the city council for
decision as hereafter provided. Applications must be signed by the applicant
and the record fee title owner of the private property where the recreational
vehicle will be used or occupied under the permit consenting to the
application. The applicant shall provide the city all information deemed
necessary by the city council to process the application, including but not
limited to: 1) the legal description of the private property where the
recreational vehicle will be used or occupied; 2) the name and address of the
record owner of said private property; 3) the number of persons who will reside
in, use or occupy the recreational vehicle on the private property; and 4) the
requested duration for the permit. The city council may by resolution from time
to time establish and amend a fee schedule for applications for temporary
occupancy permits, including fees sufficient to pay the cost of any notices,
publications or inspections required by law or otherwise determined necessary
by the city to process the application. The applicant shall pay the applicable
application fee at the time the application is filed with the city. The city
shall have no obligation to process any application filed with the city unless
the applicable application fee is paid in full by the applicant. The city
council shall have the authority to waive all or any portion of the application
fee when it deems such a waiver to be in the best interest of the city.
      2.   Hearing - Decision - Conditions - Judicial Review: Prior to granting
or denying a temporary occupancy permit, the city shall comply with the notice
and hearing requirements under Chapter 65, Title 67 of the Idaho Code, as
amended, applicable to special use permit applications. Unless otherwise
determined by resolution of the city council, the public hearing on the
application shall be initially commenced within thirty (30) days after all
notices required by law have been duly given. In addition:
         a.   Approval/Denial of Application. The approval or denial of any
application shall be based upon standards and criteria set forth in the
Comprehensive Plan, this chapter and other applicable city ordinances and
regulations, as otherwise provided in Chapter 65, Title 67 of the Idaho Code,
as amended. In addition, no temporary occupancy permit may be granted unless
the city council finds that issuance of the conditional use permit is: a)
consistent with the Comprehensive Plan; and b) in the best interest of the
city.
         The approval or denial of any application provided for in this section
shall be accompanied by a written decision of the city in compliance with
Chapter 65, Title 67 of the Idaho Code, as amended.
         b.   Duration: Notwithstanding any other provision of this section, no
temporary occupancy permit may be issued nor shall remain in effect for an
effective duration longer than ninety (90) days from the date of issuance of
the permit. Provided, however, that the city council may issue renewed permits
upon new application by the permit holder, including but not limited to payment
any application permit renewal fee. Each temporary occupancy permit shall state
a commencement date and termination date for the permit subject to the
provisions of this subsection. The temporary occupancy permit shall
automatically terminate upon expiration of the termination date stated in the
permit unless the permit is renewed prior to expiration of the current
temporary occupancy permit as provided under this subsection.
         c.   Conditions On Permits - Violation of Permit Conditions: The city
council may attach conditions to temporary occupancy permits issued as deemed
in the best interest of the city, including but not limited to any conditions
authorized under Chapter 65, Title 67 of the Idaho Code, as amended. It shall
be unlawful for any person to violate any term or condition of any temporary
occupancy permit issued by the city pursuant to this chapter.
         d.   Judicial Review: Judicial review of any final decision of the
city under this section may be taken in the same manner as provided for
judicial review of final local land use planning decisions under Chapter 65,
Title 67 of the Idaho Code, as amended.
      3.   Applicability/Non-Transferability of Permits: Unless otherwise
provided in the issued temporary occupancy permit, a temporary occupancy permit
issued by the city shall apply to the applicant and permitted occupants for the
subject lot specified in the permit for the duration of the permit only. A
temporary occupancy permit is not transferable to any other person,
recreational vehicle or to other private property. A temporary occupancy permit
shall not be considered as establishing a binding precedent to renew any
existing occupancy permit or grant other or additional temporary occupancy
permits. (Ord. 433, 4-4-2023)
5-5-4:   VIOLATIONS:
Violations of this chapter or any term or condition of any temporary occupancy
permit issued by the city pursuant to this chapter, shall be an infraction,
punishable by civil penalty or fine as provided by law for punishment of
infractions. In addition to all other remedies of the city, which shall be non-
exclusive and cumulative, the city may revoke any temporary occupancy permit in
the event the permit holder is in violation of terms or conditions of the
permit or is otherwise in violation of the provisions of this chapter. (Ord.
433, 4-4-2023)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
Traffic Regulations   1
CHAPTER 1
TRAFFIC REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-1-1: State Laws Adopted
6-1-2: Speed Limits
6-1-3: Stopping, Standing And Parking Of Vehicles
6-1-4: Compression, Jake Brakes Prohibited
6-1-5: Snowmobiles
6-1-6: ATVs And UTVs
6-1-1: STATE LAWS ADOPTED:
   A.   Intent: It is hereby declared to be the intent of the city to aid and
assist, by whatever means possible, for the utmost consistency in traffic
regulation among and between agencies of Idaho having such jurisdiction. Toward
that end, adoption of the Idaho motor vehicle laws by the cities of Idaho is a
necessary means of assuring maximum uniformity within the state.
   B.   Laws Adopted: There is hereby adopted for the purpose of establishing
rules and regulations for the use of all streets and public thoroughfares of
the city, that certain code, identified as the Idaho motor vehicle laws, more
particularly Idaho Code title 49, published by the department of law
enforcement, and as the same may hereafter be revised by the Idaho legislature,
or amended by the city, and the same is hereby adopted and incorporated as an
ordinance of the city as fully as though set forth at length herein. (2010
Code)
6-1-2: SPEED LIMITS:
   A.   General Citywide Limits:
      1.   It shall be unlawful to operate a motor vehicle upon any of the
public thoroughfares or roads within the corporate limits of the city presently
existing or as may be hereafter established, at a speed in excess of twenty
five (25) miles per hour or as posted, except that the maximum rate of speed
shall be ten (10) miles per hour in all alleys.
      2.   Any speed in excess of the limit specified in this subsection shall
be prima facie evidence that the speed is not reasonable or prudent and that it
is unlawful.
   B.   Special Zones: It shall be unlawful to operate any such vehicle in any
school, church or special zone at a rate of speed greater than that prescribed
by the mayor and city council when appropriate signs are placed at such zones.
(2010 Code)
6-1-3: STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING OF VEHICLES:
   A.   Definition of Vehicle. The term “vehicle” as used in Section
6-1-3  of this ordinance shall mean every device in, upon, or by which any
person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a highway excepting
devices used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. The term “vehicle”
shall include, but is not limited to, motor vehicles, trailers, recreational
vehicles, motorhomes, travel trailers, fifthwheel trailers, fold down camping
trailers, semitrailers, and utility trailers as defined under Chapter 1, Title
49, Idaho Code.
   B.   Restrictions on Stopping, Standing and Parking Vehicles. Except as
otherwise provided in this ordinance, no person shall:
      1.   Stop, stand or park any vehicle, in whole or in part, upon or within
any portion of any street, alley, sidewalk or public right of way within the
city:
         a.   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge
or curb of a street;
         b.   On or within a sidewalk;
         c.   On or within an intersection;
         d.   On or within a crosswalk;
         e.   On or within a bike lane or bike path;
         f.   Alongside or opposite any street excavation or obstruction when
doing so would obstruct or interfere traffic;
         g.   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure or tunnel upon or
within any highway, street, alley or public right of way;
         h.   On any railroad track or within 50 feet of any railroad crossing;
         i.   On the same block face afterthe expiration of the posted time
limit on a traffic control device during the remainder of that calendar day;
         j.   Along any curbing or within any area designated as a temporary or
permanent “No Parking” area by the City or governmental highway agency with
jurisdiction within the city by use of yellow paint, red paint, official
signage or other traffic control device;
         k.   Along any curbing or within any area designated as temporary or
permanent “Accessible Parking” or “Handicapped Parking” by the City or other
governmental highway agency with jurisdiction within the city by use of blue
paint, official signage or other traffic control device, without a valid
accessible or handicapped parking placard or plates on the vehicle issued to
the operator or an occupant of the vehicle displayed as required by law;
         l.   In any area or location prohibited for stopping, standing or
parking under Titles 18 or 49, Idaho Code, as amended; or
         m.   In any manner in violation of 1) any restriction, term or
condition of any permanent or temporary special parking zone established by the
City Council or Mayor pursuant to Section 6-1-3(G) of this ordinance, 2) any
restriction, term or condition of any Special Parking Permit issued by City
pursuant to Section 6-1-3(H) of this ordinance, or 3) any lawful direction of
any peace officer, Mayor or City personnel, or any traffic control devices.
      2.   Stop, stand or park any vehicle, in whole or in part, upon or within
any portion of any street, alley, sidewalk or public right of way within the
city except momentarily to pick up or discharge a passenger:
         a.   In front of a public or private driveway;
         b.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant;
         c.   Within twenty feet (20') of a crosswalk or a bike/pedestrian curb
ramp, except at an intersection where a traffic control signal is in operation,
or in a parking meter zone;
         d.   Within thirty feet (30') upon the approach to any flashing
signal, stop sign, yield sign or traffic control signal located at the side of
a roadway;
         e.   Within twenty feet (20') of the driveway entrance to any fire
station, and on the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station
within seventy five feet (75') of said entrance when properly sign-posted;
         f.   At any place where such stopping, standing or parking is
prohibited under this ordinance or otherwise by law.
      3.   Stop, stand or park any vehicle, in whole or in part, upon or within
any portion of street, alley, sidewalk or public right of way within the city
in any manner in that a) obstructs, impedes or interferes with vehicle traffic
or pedestrians traffic, or with management, maintenance or repair of the
street, alley, sidewalk or public right of way by City or governmental highway
with jurisdiction within the city, or b) is unsafe or creates a hazard to the
public, vehicles traffic or pedestrian traffic.
      4.   Abandon, stop, stand or park any disabled, inoperable or junk
vehicle, in whole or in part, upon or within any portion of any street, alley,
sidewalk or public right of way within the city except as authorized by the
City or governmental highway agency with jurisdiction within the city.
      5.   Stop, stand or park any vehicle, in whole or in part, at any
particular location upon or within any portion of any street, alley, or public
right of way for a period of forty eight (48) contiguous hours or longer unless
authorized by City. For purposes of this subsection, a vehicle parked at a
particular location shall be deemed to have remained continuously parked at
said particular location for a contiguous period unless during said period the
vehicle has moved more than six hundred feet (600') away from said particular
location for a period of more than twenty four (24) contiguous hours.
   C.   Restriction on Occupancy/Use of Stopped, Standing or Parked Vehicles
for Habitation. No person shall reside in, occupy or use any vehicle as a place
of temporary, overnight, or permanent habitation, abode or residence while such
vehicle is stopped, standing or parked in whole or in part upon or within any
portion of any street, alley, sidewalk or public right of way without a valid
permit issued by City. Unless authorized by City, no person shall 1) cause any
public or private utilities, electricity, heating fuel, water or sewage
services to be provided, supplied or physically connected to any vehicle
resided in, occupied or used in violation of this subsection, or 2) cause any
utility or service line, connection, or equipment serving or intended for
serving said parked vehicle to be placed within or across, or be situated upon
or within, any portion of any street, alley, sidewalk or public right of way.
   D.   Removal of Unlawfully Stopped, Standing or Parked Vehicles. Any
vehicle, in whole or in part, stopped, standing, parked or otherwise present
upon any portion of any street, alley, sidewalk or public right of way in
violation of any provision of Section
6-1-3  or any Special Parking Permit issued by the City, may be removed
therefrom by the Mayor, the Mayor’s designee, or any peace officer to the
nearest place of safety or storage. The owner and operator of any such vehicle
shall be jointly and severally liable for all costs of removal, towing, storage
and disposition of the vehicle. Disposition of any such removed vehicle
pursuant to this section shall be subject to all applicable provisions of Title
49, Idaho Code, as amended, concerning disposition of vehicles removed from
public highways, streets, and rights of way.
   E.   Exceptions. The prohibitions in division
6-1-3  B. shall not apply to:
      1.   Peace officers, fire ambulance and rescue personnel, and government
officials, employees and agents while acting in the course of their official
duties;
      2.   Employees and agents of public and private utilities during the
course of their official duties while actively engaged in the inspection,
placement, servicing, maintenance, repair or other work on utilities situated
within or adjacent to a highway, street, alley, sidewalk or public right of
way;
      3.   Persons and entities otherwise authorized by the City or other
governmental highway agency with jurisdiction within the city;
      4.   Stopping, standing or parking momentarily a) to avoid conflicts with
traffic or traffic hazards, b) to comply with directions from any traffic
control device, peace officer, City or highway agency personnel, or the law, or
c) for the purpose of loading or unloading passengers, goods or merchandise
provided that this exception for loading and unloading shall not apply in any
area where stopping, standing or parking is prohibited under Section
6-1-3  B.3. or 4. and shall not exceed a period of five (5) contiguous minutes;
or
      5.   Temporary parking of a disabled vehicle for repair or towing,
provided that a) such temporary parking shall be subject to all other
provisions of this ordinance, including but not limited to Section
6-1-3  B.5., and b) the owner or operator of such disabled vehicle shall notify
the City or a peace officer with law enforcement jurisdiction in Lewis County,
Idaho, of such parking of the disabled vehicle within twenty four (24) hours
after the time the disabled vehicle, in whole or part, is initially parked
within any portion of street, alley, sidewalk or public right of way.
   F.   Special Parking Zones - Temporary Parking Zones.
      1.   Special Parking Zones. The City Council may by ordinance designate
any portion of any street, alley or public way within the city as a special
parking zone, including but not limited to a “No Parking Zone”, “Loading Zone”,
“Residential Parking Zone”, “Accessible Parking Zone”, “Handicapped Parking
Zone”, excepting or varying application of this ordinance within the special
parking zone subject to any other terms, conditions and restrictions as deemed
in the best interest of the City. Upon designation of any such special parking
zones, the City shall cause signage or markings identifying the zone to be
made, erected and placed along or within the special parking zone.
      2.   Temporary Parking Zones. The City Council or Mayor may temporarily
designate any portion of any street, alley or public way within the city as a
“No Parking Zone” or place other temporary restrictions, terms or conditions
upon stopping, standing or parking on any portion of any street, alley or
public way by resolution of the City Council or order of the Mayor as deemed in
the best interest of the City, including but not limited to for purposes of
special events, emergencies, construction or other exigency. The City shall
cause a copy of any such resolution or order shall be posted in a public place
at the city hall and within or along the portion of the street, alley, or
public way in which the temporary restrictions, terms or conditions apply, and
the portion of the street, alley or public way subject to the resolution or
order shall be identified by signage or markings. Provided, however, that any
such temporary restrictions a) ordered by the Mayor shall not remain in effect
for a period exceeding seventy two (72) hours unless said period is extended by
the city council by resolution and ordinance, or b) established or extended by
resolution of the city council shall not remain in effect for a period
exceeding sixty (60) days.
   G.   Special Parking Permits. The City Council may issue special parking
permits that temporarily except or vary application of this ordinance with
respect to any person or entity as deemed in the best interest of the City as
provided in this section.
      1.   All special parking permits issued by City pursuant to this section
shall:
         a.   Be issued to the applicant only and shall not be transferrable;
         b.   State name, mailing address and telephone number of the
applicant;
         c.   State the license plate number and the year, make, model and
color of the vehicle to be parked pursuant to the permit; and
         d.   State the location(s) and authorized date(s)/time(s) of parking
authorized under the under the permit, which shall in no event exceed a
contiguous period of seventy two (72) hours under each permit issued.
      2.   The City Council may place such otherterms and conditions on
issuance of the permit as the City Council deems in the best interest of the
city. City may amend or revoke any permit issued pursuant to this section at
any time if the City deems such amendment or revocation of the permit to be in
the best interest of the City. All permits issued underthis section a) shall be
subject to all other applicable laws, ordinances or regulations, b) shall
solely authorize parking of the permitted vehicle as provided in the permit,
and c) shall not vest the permittee or any other person with any rights in any
street, alley or public right of way.
      3.   The permittee shall at all times during the effective period of the
permit cause the entire face of the permit to be prominently displayed in the
front windshield of the permitted vehicle such that the entire face of the
permit is visible from outside of the vehicle. Notwithstanding any provisions
of the permit, all permittees shall at all times comply with all lawful
directions of any peace officers, the Mayor and City personnel, and shall move
or relocate the permitted vehicle as may be requested them for any lawful
purpose, including but not limited to for traffic control, parking, safety, law
enforcement, emergencies, or for management, maintenance or of any streets,
alleys, public right of ways, utilities, public property, or for any other city
or public purpose.
      4.   The City Council may by resolution establish and from time to time
amend a fee schedule for issuance of special parking permits authorized under
this section.
   H.   Authorities Reserved. Nothing in Section
6-1-3  is intended to, nor shall it, limit or impair the authority of the City,
Mayor or any peace officer with respect to traffic control, parking, safety,
removal or impoundment of vehicles, law enforcement, emergencies, or the
management, maintenance or repair or of any streets, alleys, public right of
ways, utilities, public property, or for any other lawful purpose as may
otherwise be provided by law.
   I.   Enforcement - Penalties for Violations. The provisions of division
6-1-3  B. and C. shall be enforceable by the Mayor and any peace officer with
law enforcement jurisdiction within Lewis County, Idaho. Any violation of any
provision of division
6-1-3  C. shall constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable by fine not
exceeding $1,000.00 or jail not exceeding six (6) months, or both. Any
violation of Section
6-1-3  B. shall constitute an infraction and shall be punishable by infraction
fine or civil penalty as provided under Idaho law for infractions. (Ord. 432,
4-28-2023)
6-1-4: COMPRESSION, JAKE BRAKES PROHIBITED:
The use of compression brakes, engine brakes, "jake brakes" and other similar
devices on trucks or other motorized vehicles within the city is hereby
prohibited. (Ord. 349, 9-1-1992)
6-1-5: SNOWMOBILES:
   A.   Purpose: The purpose of this section is to regulate in a reasonable
manner the operation of snowmobiles within the city, and to provide the
circumstances and conditions when and where snowmobiles may be legally operated
upon the public roadways of the city. (Ord. 254, 3-7-1972)
   B.   Definition: The term "snowmobile" shall mean every self- propelled
vehicle under one thousand (1,000) pounds unladen gross weight, designed
primarily for travel on snow or ice or over natural terrain, which may be
steered by tracks, skis or runners. (Ord. 254, 3-7-1972; amd. 2010 Code)
   C.   Operation Subject To Restrictions: It shall be lawful to operate a
snowmobile upon all the public roadways of the city upon the condition and
subject to the restrictions hereinafter set forth in this section.
   D.   Minimum Age Of Drivers: No person under the age of fourteen (14) years
shall drive or operate a snowmobile in the city.
   E.   Offenses By Persons Owning Snowmobiles: It shall be unlawful for any
person to knowingly permit, allow or encourage the operation or driving of a
snowmobile by a person under the age of fourteen (14) years.
   F.   Equipment: No snowmobile shall be operated in the city, unless it is
equipped with the following:
      1.   At least one, and not more than two (2), headlamps sufficient to
render clearly discernable persons and vehicles at a distance of two hundred
fifty feet (250') ahead.
      2.   Tail lamps, which when lighted shall emit a red light plainly
visible at a distance of two hundred fifty feet (250') to the rear.
      3.   At least one brake which may be operated by hand or foot.
      4.   A muffler in good working order and in constant operation to prevent
excessive or unusual noise and annoying smoke; and no person shall use a
muffler cutout, bypass or similar device.
      5.   A mast or antenna displaying a red or red-orange fluorescent flag or
pennant a minimum of five feet (5') above the ground; such flag or pennant
shall be either rectangular or triangular in shape with the leading edge being
a minimum of six inches (6") and the length a minimum of twelve inches (12").
   G.   Regulations For Operation:
      1.   It shall be unlawful to drive, operate or park a snowmobile on any
sidewalk in the city.
      2.   No snowmobile shall be operated at a speed in excess of fifteen (15)
miles per hour in the city.
      3.   No snowmobile shall carry passengers or weight in excess of the
capacity recommended by the manufacturer thereof.
      4.   No sled, toboggan, trailer or any other device shall be towed by a
snowmobile except by means of a rigid tow bar connecting the same to such
device.
      5.   No person on skis shall be towed behind a snowmobile.
      6.   It shall be unlawful to drive or operate a snowmobile while under
the influence of intoxicating liquor.
      7.   All snowmobiles shall come to a full stop at all street
intersections.
      8.   All snowmobiles shall be operated only in single file on the extreme
right hand side of the street.
      9.   Operation of snowmobiles on the streets of the city shall be limited
to ingress and egress to and from the city; and city streets are not to be used
as a place of recreation for snowmobiles.
      10.   No snowmobile shall be operated within the city limits after ten
o'clock (10:00) P.M., except for the purpose of going directly to or from the
place of residence of the operator of such snowmobile or to its place of
storage.
      11.   No person shall operate a snowmobile carelessly and heedlessly, or
without due caution and circumspection and at a speed or in a manner as to
endanger or be likely to endanger any person or property. (Ord. 254, 3-7-1972)
6-1-6: ATVS AND UTVS:
   A.   Definitions. For purposes of this ordinance, the following terms shall
have the following meanings:
ALL-TERRAIN VEHICLE OR ATV: Any recreational vehicle with three (3) or more
tires, weighing under nine hundred (900) pounds, fifty inches (50") or less in
width, having a wheelbase of sixty one inches (61") or less, traveling on low
pressure tires of ten (10) psi or less, has handlebar steering and seating
designed to be straddled by the operators.
CITY STREETS: All public highways, streets, alleys and rights of way within the
city limits of the city of Craigmont, excluding all public highways, streets
and rights of way within the city limits under the highway jurisdiction of the
Idaho Transportation Department.
UTILITY TYPE VEHICLE OR UTV: Any recreational motor vehicle other than an ATV,
motorbike or snowmobile, designed for and capable of travel over designated
unpaved roads, traveling on four (4) or more low pressure tires of twenty (20)
psi or less, maximum width less than seventy four inches (74"), maximum weight
less than two thousand (2,000) pounds, or having a wheelbase of ninety four
inches (94") or less. Utility type vehicle does not include golf carts,
vehicles specially designed to carry a disabled person, implements of husbandry
as defined in section 49-110(2), Idaho Code, or vehicles otherwise registered
under Title 49, Idaho Code.
   B.   Operation of ATVs/UTVs on City Streets - General Prohibition. No person
shall operate an ATV and UTV on or within a city street except as otherwise
expressly permitted under this ordinance.
   C.   Conditions for Permitted Operation of ATVs/UTVs on City Streets. All
city streets shall be open for travel by ATVs and UTVs subject to all of the
following conditions:
      1.   Limitations on Areas of Travel. ATVs and UTVs may only be operated
upon those portions of city streets designed and maintained for general
automobile traffic. ATVs and UTVs shall not be operated on sidewalks, curbing
or ditches within city streets, provided, however, that ATVs or UTVs with snow
removal attachments may be temporarily operated on sidewalks for the purposes
of snow removal. All ordinances of the city of Craigmont pertaining to
operation of vehicles and vehicle parking shall be applicable to ATVs and UTVs
operated on city streets.
      2.   Valid Driver’s Licenses and Vehicle Registration Required. No person
shall operate any ATVs and UTVs on any city street unless the person then has a
valid current Idaho driver’s license. All ATVs and UTVs operated on city
streets shall have a valid current off-road vehicle registration issued by the
state of Idaho for the vehicle. Proof of valid current registration, whether a
plate or sticker, shall be displayed on the ATV or UTV in a place readily
visible upon inspection. City streets shall be closed to all unregistered ATVs
and UTVs.
      3.   Required Equipment. All ATVs and UTVs shall be equipped with the
following safety equipment as described in title 9, chapter 49 of the Idaho
Code, in good working order:
         a.   Stop lamps, headlamps, and taillamps;
         b.   A mirror so located as to reflect to the operator a view of the
roadway a distance of at least two hundred feet (2001) to the rear of the ATV
or UTV; and
         c.   A horn audible at least two hundred feet (200') from the ATV or
UTV.
      4.   Proof of Liability Insurance. The operator of any ATV or UTV on any
city street shall have proof of valid liability insurance for the ATV and UTV,
as required by Chapter 12, Title 49, Idaho Code, in the operator’s possession
on or around the vehicle at all times the vehicle is in operation on any city
street. The operator shall display such proof of liability insurance to any
peace officer requesting to examine it. No person shall be convicted of
violating this section if that person produces at any time prior to conviction
the certificate or proof of liability insurance covering the motor vehicle that
person is accused of operating in violation of this section, where the
certificate or proof of liability insurance demonstrates the existence of
liability insurance described in Idaho Code § 49-1212, as amended, which was in
effect at the time of occurrence of the violation.
      5.   Limitation on Application to other Highways. Nothing in this section
is intended to, nor shall it be deemed to, authorize or regulate use of ATVs or
UTVs on any portion of U.S. Highway 95 or any other highway, street or right of
way under the highway jurisdiction of the Idaho Transportation Department
within the city limits of the city of Craigmont.
      6.   Incorporated Idaho Code Provisions, It shall be unlawful for any
person to operate any ATV or UTV on any city street in violation of Chapter 80,
Title 18, Idaho Code, as amended, and Chapters 6, 8, 12, 13 or 14, Title 49,
Idaho Code, as amended, which are all incorporated herein by reference and
shall apply to operation of ATVs and UTVs in the city of Craigmont, including,
but not limited to, ATVs and UTVs not required to be licensed or registered
under the laws of the state of Idaho.
   D.   Exceptions. This ordinance shall not apply to ATVs or UTV use by any of
the following persons:
      1.   Peace officers, fire ambulance and rescue personnel, and government
officials, employees and agents while acting in the course of their official
duties; or
      2.   Persons and entities otherwise authorized by the City or other
governmental highway agency with jurisdiction within the city.
   E.   Penalties. Except as otherwise provided by this ordinance, any person
violating this shall be guilty of an infraction, punishable by a civil penalty
or fine as provided for infractions under Idaho law. Provided, however, any
violation of any provision of the Idaho Code incorporated under division C. of
this section for which the Idaho legislature has provided misdemeanor penalties
shall be a misdemeanor which shall be punishable as provided in the
incorporated Idaho Code provision. (Ord. 431, 4-4-2023)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
Streets, Sidewalks And Public Ways   1
Sidewalk Construction And Repair   2
Municipal Airport   3
Airport Zoning   3A
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
7-1-1: Excavations
7-1-2: Snow And Ice Removal From Sidewalks
7-1-1: EXCAVATIONS:
   A.   Open Excavations: No landowner or tenant shall permit an excavation for
a basement, or other excavation hazardous to human life, to remain open on land
owned or occupied by any person, firm or corporation without covering the same
securely to prevent injuries to persons; provided, however, that the same may
remain open during the course of construction or for the purpose of cleaning
the same. (1963 Code § 4-101)
   B.   Warning Signs Required: No excavation hazardous to human life shall be
permitted to remain open unless the same is properly safeguarded at all times
by barricades and warning signs. (1963 Code § 4-102)
   C.   Abandoned Excavations: All excavations, hazardous to human life, which
are no longer in use or have been abandoned shall be filled with earth to the
level of the surrounding ground. An excavation for the basement of a building
shall be deemed to have been abandoned when construction has stopped for a
period of thirty (30) days. (1963 Code § 4-103)
   D.   Hazardous Excavations: Any excavation shall be determined to be prima
facie hazardous to human life if its depth exceeds two feet (2'). (1963 Code §
4-104)
7-1-2: SNOW AND ICE REMOVAL FROM SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Removal By Property Owner: The owner, tenant or occupant of any
premises within the city abutting or adjoining any public sidewalk shall remove
all snow and ice from any such sidewalk. (1963 Code § 9-101)
   B.   Notice To Remove: It shall be the duty of the city to notify any owner,
tenant or occupant of property herein described to remove or otherwise correct
the objectionable matter herein legislated against, which notice shall be sent
by registered mail to the last known address of such owner, tenant or occupant,
notifying him that he has a period of twenty four (24) hours from and after
receipt of such notice within which to correct or otherwise remove the
objections set forth in said notice. (1963 Code § 9-102)
   C.   Failure To Comply; Removal By City: Upon failure of the owner, tenant
or occupant of said premises to comply with the terms and conditions of said
notice, then and in that event the city shall have the right to remove such
snow and ice and assess the cost thereof against the premises abutting the
sidewalk. Such assessment shall be certified to the county assessor or other
proper county officials having charge of the making of the assessment roll, and
such assessment shall be placed on the assessment roll and collected in the
same manner as other municipal taxes are collected. (1963 Code § 9-103)
CHAPTER 2
SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION AND REPAIR
SECTION:
7-2-1: Council Determination
7-2-2: Notice To Construct
7-2-3: Failure To Construct
7-2-4: Repairs
7-2-5: Itemized Statement Of Costs
7-2-6: Duties Of City Attorney; Lien
7-2-7: Hearing On Notice To Construct
7-2-1: COUNCIL DETERMINATION:
   A.   Inspection: The city council shall designate one of its members whose
duty it shall be to inspect all sidewalks within the city and report to the
council, where, in his judgment the construction of a new sidewalk is
necessary; and all cases where there is no existing sidewalk, and in his
judgment it is necessary for a sidewalk to be constructed. Said council member
shall report such fact to the council with his recommendation.
   B.   Report; Council Action: After considering such report and
recommendation, the council shall make its determination. Whenever the council,
after considering such report and recommendation, in their judgment shall deem
it necessary to require property owners within the city to construct or repair
sidewalks, they shall take recorded action in an official council meeting,
naming the owner and location of property abutting where it is, in such
meeting, determined sidewalks shall be constructed and repaired. (1963 Code §
9-301)
7-2-2: NOTICE TO CONSTRUCT:
When any sidewalk is ordered to be constructed or reconstructed, under the
provisions of this chapter, the city clerk-treasurer shall, as soon as may be,
serve notice in writing upon the property owner, or any resident agent of the
property owner, directing such sidewalk to be constructed or reconstructed, of
the materials and according to the specifications in force in the district
where such walk is to be constructed or reconstructed, and describing the
premises adjacent to which such construction is to be made. The service of such
notice may be made by delivery of a copy thereof to the owner or his agent, or
if neither is to be found within the city, by mailing a copy thereof to the
owner at his last known post office address, and service by mail shall be
deemed complete upon the expiration of five (5) days from the date of the
mailing of such notice. (1963 Code § 9-302)
7-2-3: FAILURE TO CONSTRUCT:
If the work of building such sidewalk in accordance with the notice served by
the clerk-treasurer is not begun within ten (10) days after the serving of the
such notice, or if, after having been begun, the same is not completed within a
reasonable time thereafter, the mayor shall notify the city clerk-treasurer of
such fact and the clerk-treasurer shall call for bids by publication for two
(2) consecutive weeks issued in some newspaper published in or having a general
circulation in the city, for the construction and completion of such sidewalk.
Such bids shall be returned by the clerk-treasurer to the mayor and council and
opened and considered at the next or any general or special meeting; and after
laying over for not less than one day, the contract for the construction or
completion of such sidewalk shall be let to the lowest and best reasonable
bidder; and the work of construction or reconstruction shall be performed under
the general supervision of the street commissioner. (1963 Code § 9-303; amd.
2010 Code)
7-2-4: REPAIRS:
When any sidewalk within the city is in such condition as in the judgment of
the city council to require repairs thereof to be made, the city clerk-
treasurer shall serve upon the owner or his agent a written notice to make such
repairs, describing the same in general terms, which notice may require the
repairs to be made within such reasonable time, not exceeding ten (10) days
after the service of such notice, as may, in the opinion of the council be
deemed necessary. If such repairs be not made within the time required by such
notice, the same shall thereupon be made by the street commissioner. (1963 Code
§ 9-304; amd. 2010 Code)
7-2-5: ITEMIZED STATEMENT OF COSTS:
Upon completion of the construction or repairs, the costs thereof shall be paid
out of any unappropriated monies in the general fund of the city, or such other
fund as may be designated by the city council. As soon as may be thereafter,
the city clerk- treasurer shall serve upon the owner of such property, or his
agent, in the same manner as the notice to construct sidewalks is authorized to
be served, an itemized statement of the costs of such construction,
reconstruction or repair. If the costs thereof be not paid within five (5) days
after such service, the clerk- treasurer shall deliver a copy of such itemized
statement to the city attorney who shall proceed to collect the same. (1963
Code § 9-305)
7-2-6: DUTIES OF CITY ATTORNEY; LIEN:
   A.   Filing Of Suit For Costs: Upon the receiving of any such statement, the
city attorney shall, as soon as may be, bring suit in any court having
jurisdiction, for the recovery of the monies expended by the city in the
construction, reconstruction or repair of such walk, or shall file a lien upon
the property abutting upon such walk. (1963 Code § 9-306; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Foreclosure Of Lien: Such lien shall be verified and shall be filed and
foreclosed as in the case of other liens under the general laws of the state of
Idaho, and amendments which may hereafter be made thereto, and from the date of
the filing of the same, the costs of such construction, maintenance and repairs
shall be and remain a lien upon the property described as in the case of other
liens. (1963 Code § 9-306)
7-2-7: HEARING ON NOTICE TO CONSTRUCT:
Any time after the services of the notice to construct, reconstruct or repair,
as hereinbefore provided, and before the expiration of the time specified
therein, the owner or agent upon whom such service was made may appear before
the city council at any general or special meeting and show cause why the order
for such construction, reconstruction, or repair should be revoked. The council
shall hear and determine such application informally, and such application
shall not extend the period within which the work is to be begun unless
otherwise ordered by the council. (1963 Code § 9-307)
CHAPTER 3
MUNICIPAL AIRPORT
SECTION:
7-3-1: Definitions
7-3-2: Airport Operation; Commercial Activities
7-3-3: Use Of Airport; User Fees
7-3-4: Airport Liability
7-3-5: Airport Fees; Liability Insurance
7-3-6: Safety Requirements
7-3-7: Lease Agreements
7-3-8: Animals Prohibited
7-3-9: Requirements For Airport Maintenance
7-3-10: Airport Zoning
7-3-11: Airplane Fuel Requirements
7-3-12: Hazardous Materials, Chemicals And Fertilizers
7-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ANIMALS: Any domestic pet, or livestock, including dogs, cats, cattle, horses,
pigs and sheep.
BUSINESS OR COMMERCIAL ACTIVITY: Any activity which is conducted for profit or
in which a service is provided to another, or any activity in connection with a
business or commercial activity which may not be located on the airport.
LANDING AREA: The area of the airport used for the landing, taking off, or
taxiing of aircraft.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, association, partnership or corporation or joint
venture including representatives or agents thereof.
USE: Any activity, proposed or actual, which requires airport property
including any building or structure or commercial activity. (Ord. 321, 4-5-
1988)
7-3-2: AIRPORT OPERATION; COMMERCIAL ACTIVITIES:
   A.   Use Governed By City; Compliance Required: The city owns and operates
an airport for public and private users. All use of the airport shall be
governed by the terms and conditions of this chapter. The use of the airport is
a privilege and shall be regulated as provided for in this chapter.
   B.   Commercial Operations; Application For Approval: No person shall engage
in any business or commercial activity of any nature except in compliance with
this chapter. Any person proposing or desiring to conduct a business or
commercial activity shall first make application to the city clerk-treasurer
and secure the city's approval.
   C.   Minimum Standards For Aeronautical Commercial Activities: Any person
engaging in business or commercial activities shall be required to meet minimum
standards governing the quality and level of service provided in connection
with a particular aeronautical activity at the airport. (Ord. 321, 4-5-1988)
7-3-3: USE OF AIRPORT; USER FEES:
   A.   City Approval; Permit For Construction; Lease: Any use of the airport
shall be approved by the city. Any person proposing to construct any building
or structure shall apply for a permit for such construction and shall have
obtained a lease for such airport property.
   B.   User Fees: Persons proposing to use the airport shall be responsible
for the payment of fees for such use. Such fees may include fuel tax, landing
fees and tie down charges. (Ord. 321, 4-5-1988)
7-3-4: AIRPORT LIABILITY:
   A.   The city shall not be liable for loss, damage, or injury to person or
property arising out of any accident, incident or mishap of any nature
whatsoever to any individual aircraft or property occurring on the airport in
the use of any airport facility.
   B.   Any person engaging in a commercial activity at the airport shall
maintain aircraft, chemical, and premises liability insurance naming the city
as an additional insured. (Ord. 321, 4-5-1988)
7-3-5: AIRPORT FEES; LIABILITY INSURANCE:
   A.   Fees Enumerated; Exception:
      1.   All airplanes operating commercially from the Craigmont Municipal
Airport which are engaged in dry fertilizing and freighting operations shall
pay an annual fee of $4,000.00 per calendar year per operator for the privilege
of using the municipal airport runway.
      2.   Payments of the annual fee shall be made prior to the commencement
of any commercial operation to the City Clerk at her office in Craigmont,
Idaho.
      3.   Provided however, that the fees provided for tin this subsection
shall not apply to any person, firm, partnership, business association or
corporation leasing airport facilities or an airport area from the City of
Craigmont and who maintain a fixed base for their flying operation at the
airport.
   B.   Insurance: Provided, further, that all commercial operations subject to
this section, including those leasing airport facilities from the City, shall
provide the City with a Certificate of Liability Insurance, naming the City as
an additional insured under such policy which shall have a minimum amount of
coverage of at least $1,000,000.00, prior to the commencement of any commercial
operation. (Ord. 362, 5-7-1996; amd. Ord. 426, 2-18-2021)
7-3-6: SAFETY REQUIREMENTS:
Any hazardous activity or condition occurring on the airport shall be reported
immediately to the city clerk-treasurer. Any accident involving personal injury
or aircraft damage shall be reported to the city clerk-treasurer. (Ord. 321, 4-
5-1988)
7-3-7: LEASE AGREEMENTS:
The city may enter into a lease of real and personal property at the airport
upon such terms and conditions as the mayor and city council may deem
appropriate. The city may not lease the entire airport or the entirety of
particular area, as designated in the airport zoning map, to any one person but
shall provide for aircraft and motor vehicle access to the landing area from
adjoining areas whether or not they immediately adjoin the landing strip. (Ord.
321, 4-5-1988)
7-3-8: ANIMALS PROHIBITED:
No animals of any kind shall be permitted on the airport. (Ord. 321, 4-5-1988)
7-3-9: REQUIREMENTS FOR AIRPORT MAINTENANCE:
No person shall allow buildings, structures, or leased property to deteriorate
to an unsightly condition. All property shall be maintained in a good state of
repair and appearance. (Ord. 321, 4-5-1988)
7-3-10: AIRPORT ZONING:
The construction or erection of any building, in addition to the provisions of
this chapter, shall conform with the provisions of chapter 3, article A of this
title. (Ord. 321, 4-5-1988)
7-3-11: AIRPLANE FUEL REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Storage: All aeronautical fuel or oils shall be stored in underground
containers meeting appropriate federal and state statutes and regulations. The
location of such storage shall be determined according to the rules of the
planning and zoning commission.
   B.   Persons To Exercise Due Care: Persons engaged in fueling activities
shall exercise due care to prevent overflow and spillage of fuel.
   C.   Draining Of Tanks And Sumps: Fuel tanks and oil sumps shall not be
drained on the ground and may only be drained into approved containers. (Ord.
321, 4-5-1988)
7-3-12: HAZARDOUS MATERIALS, CHEMICALS AND FERTILIZERS:
   A.   Spilling Or Discharging Prohibited: Persons engaged in crop dusting,
spraying or fertilizing activities shall not spill, discharge or dispose of any
chemical or fertilizer on airport property.
   B.   Responsibility For Cleanup Expenses: All cleanup expenses and costs
shall be the responsibility of the person utilizing the chemicals and
fertilizers.
   C.   Disposal: All chemicals and fertilizers shall be disposed of off
airport property in a method that complies with applicable federal and state
laws and regulations. (Ord. 321, 4-5-1988)
ARTICLE A. AIRPORT ZONING
SECTION:
7-3A-1: Short Title
7-3A-2: Definitions
7-3A-3: Zones
7-3A-4: Height Limitations
7-3A-5: Use Restrictions
7-3A-6: Nonconforming Uses
7-3A-7: Permit Requirements And Restrictions; Variances
7-3A-8: Conflicting Regulations
7-3A-9: Penalty
7-3A-1: SHORT TITLE:
This article shall be known and may be cited as the AIRPORT ZONING ORDINANCE.
(Ord. 261, 1-9-1973)
7-3A-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this article, the following terms shall have the meanings ascribed
to them in this section, unless the context otherwise requires:
AIRPORT: The Craigmont airport.
AIRPORT ELEVATION: The established elevation of the highest point on the usable
landing area.
AIRPORT HAZARD: Any structure, tree or use of land, which obstructs the
airspace required for, or is otherwise hazardous to, the flight of aircraft in
landing or taking off at the airport.
AIRPORT REFERENCE POINT: The point established as the approximate geographic
center of the airport landing area and so designated.
BUILDING INSPECTOR: The duly appointed building inspector of the city of
Craigmont or his deputy.
HEIGHT: For the purpose of determining the height limits in all zones set forth
in this article and shown on the zoning map, the "datum" shall be mean sea
level elevation unless otherwise specified.
LANDING AREA: The area of the airport used for the landing, taking off or
taxiing of aircraft.
NONCONFORMING USE: Any preexisting structure, tree or natural growth or use of
land, which is inconsistent with the provisions of this article or an amendment
thereto.
RUNWAY: The surfaced portion of an airport landing strip.
STRUCTURE: An object constructed or installed by man, including, but without
limitation to, buildings, towers, smokestacks, and overhead transmission lines.
TREE: Any object of natural growth. (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973; amd. 2010 Code)
7-3A-3: ZONES:
In order to carry out the provisions of this article, there are hereby created
and established certain zones which include all of the land lying within the
approach zones, transition zone, horizontal zone and conical zone. Such areas
and zones are shown on the Craigmont airport zoning map consisting of one
sheet, prepared by Hoffman, Fiske, and Wyatt, Civil Engineers, and dated
October 2, 1972, which is attached to ordinance 261 and made a part hereof by
reference. The various zones are hereby established and defined as follows:
   A.   Visual Approach Zone: A visual approach zone shall have a width of five
hundred feet (500') at a distance of two hundred feet (200') beyond each end of
the runway, widening thereafter uniformly to a width of one thousand four
hundred feet (1,400') at a distance of five thousand feet (5,000') beyond each
end of the runway, its centerline being the continuation of the centerline of
the runway, and has a slope of twenty to one (20:1).
   B.   Transitional Zone: These zones extend outward and upward at right
angles to the runway centerline and the runway centerline extended at a slope
of seven to one (7:1) from the sides of the primary zone and from the sides of
the approach zones.
   C.   Horizontal Zone: A horizontal plane one hundred fifty feet (150') above
the established airport elevation, the perimeter of which is constructed by
swinging arcs of specified radii from the center of each end of the primary
zone of each runway of each airport and connecting the adjacent arcs by lines
tangent to those arcs. The radius of each arc is five thousand feet (5,000').
   D.   Conical Zone: A zone extending outward and upward from the periphery of
the horizontal zone at a slope of twenty to one (20:1) for a horizontal
distance of four thousand feet (4,000').
   E.   Primary Zone: A zone longitudinally centered on a runway. When the
runway has a specially prepared hard surface, the primary zone extends two
hundred feet (200') beyond each end of that runway; but when the runway has no
specially prepared hard surface, the primary zone ends at each end of the
runway. The elevation of any point on the primary zone coincides with the
elevation of the nearest point on the runway centerline. The width of a primary
zone is five hundred feet (500').
   F.   Approach Zone: A zone longitudinally centered on the extended runway
centerline and extending outward and upward from each end of the primary zone.
The inner edge of the approach zone is the same width as the primary zone and
it expands uniformly to a width of one thousand four hundred feet (1,400'). The
approach zone extends for a horizontal distance of five thousand feet (5,000')
at a slope of twenty to one (20:1). (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973)
7-3A-4: HEIGHT LIMITATIONS:
   A.   Height Limitations Established: Except as otherwise provided in this
article, no structure or tree shall be erected, altered, allowed to grow, or
maintained in any surface created by this article to a height in excess of the
height limit herein established for such zone. Such height limitations are
hereby established for each of the zones in question as follows:
      1.   Visual Approach Zone For Runway: One foot (1') in height for each
twenty feet (20') in horizontal distance beginning at a point two hundred feet
(200') from and at the centerline elevation of the end of the runway and
extending to a point five thousand two hundred feet (5,200') from the end of
the runway.
      2.   Transitional Zone: These zones extend outward and upward at right
angles to the runway centerline and the runway centerline extended at a slope
of seven to one (7:1) from the sides of the primary zone and from the sides of
the approach zones.
      3.   Horizontal Zone: A horizontal plane one hundred fifty feet (150')
above the established airport elevation, the perimeter of which is constructed
by swinging arcs of specified radii from the center of each end of the primary
zone of each runway of each airport and connecting the adjacent arcs by lines
tangent to those arcs. The radius of each arc is five thousand feet (5,000').
      4.   Conical Zone: A zone extending outward and upward from the periphery
of the horizontal zone at a slope of twenty to one (20:1) for a horizontal
distance of four thousand feet (4,000').
      5.   Excepted Height Limitations: Nothing in this article shall be
construed as prohibiting the growth, construction or maintenance of any tree or
structure to the height up to thirty feet (30') above the surface of the land.
   B.   More Restrictive Limitations Prevail: Where an area is covered by more
than one height limitation, the more restrictive limitation shall prevail.
(Ord. 261, 1-9-1973)
7-3A-5: USE RESTRICTIONS:
Notwithstanding any other provisions of this article, no use may be made of
land within any zone established by this article in such a manner as to create
electrical interference with radio communication between the airport and
aircraft, make it difficult for flyers to distinguish between airport lights
and others, result in glare in the eyes of flyers using the airport, impair
visibility in the vicinity of the airport or otherwise endanger the landing,
taking off, or maneuvering of aircraft. (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973)
7-3A-6: NONCONFORMING USES:
   A.   Regulations Not Retroactive: The regulations prescribed by this article
shall not be construed to require the removal, lowering, or other changes or
alterations of any structure or tree not conforming to the regulations as of
the effective date hereof, or otherwise interfere with the continuance of any
nonconforming use. Nothing herein contained shall require any change in the
construction, alteration or intended use of any structure, the construction or
alteration of which was begun prior to the effective date hereof, and is
diligently prosecuted. (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973)
   B.   Marking And Lighting: Notwithstanding the provisions of subsection A of
this section, the owner of any nonconforming structure or tree is hereby
required to permit the installation, operation, and maintenance thereon of such
markers and lights as shall be deemed necessary by the city council to indicate
to the operators of aircraft in the vicinity of the airport, the presence of
such airport hazards. Such markers and lights shall be installed, operated, and
maintained at the expense of the Craigmont airport. (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973; amd.
2010 Code)
7-3A-7: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS AND RESTRICTIONS; VARIANCES:
   A.   Future Uses:
      1.   Except as specifically provided in subsections A1a, A1b, and A1c of
this section, no material change shall be made in the use of land and no
structure or tree shall be erected, altered, planted or otherwise established
in any zone hereby created unless a permit therefor shall have been applied for
and granted. Each application for a permit shall indicate the purpose for which
the permit is desired, with sufficient particularity to permit it to be
determined whether the resulting use, structure or tree would conform to the
regulations herein prescribed. If such determination is in the affirmative, the
permit shall be granted.
         a.   In the area lying within the limits of the horizontal zone and
the conical zone, no permit shall be required for any tree or structure less
than seventy five feet (75') of vertical height above the ground, except when,
because of terrain, land contour or topographic features, such tree or
structure would extend above the height limits prescribed for such zone.
         b.   In the areas lying within the limits of the approach zones but at
a horizontal distance of not less than four thousand two hundred feet (4,200')
from each end of the runways, no permit shall be required for any tree or
structure less than seventy five feet (75') of vertical height above the
ground, except when such tree or structure would extend above the height limit
prescribed for such instrument or noninstrument approach zone.
         c.   In the areas lying within the limits of the transition zones
beyond the perimeter of the horizontal zone, no permit shall be required for
any tree or structure less than seventy five feet (75') of vertical height
above the ground, except when such tree or structure, because of terrain, land
contour or topographic features would extend above the height limit prescribed
for such transitional zones.
      2.   Nothing contained in any of the foregoing exceptions shall be
construed as permitted or intending to permit any construction, alteration or
growth of any structure or tree in excess of any of the height limits
established by this article except as set forth in section
7-3A-4 of this article.
   B.   Existing Uses: No permit shall be granted that would allow the
establishment or creation of an airport hazard or permit a nonconforming use,
