structure, or tree to be made or become higher, or become a greater hazard to
air navigation, than it was on the effective date hereof or any amendments
thereto, or than it is when the application for a permit is made. Except as
indicated, all applications for such a permit shall be granted.
   C.   Nonconforming Uses Abandoned Or Destroyed: Whenever the building
inspector determines that a nonconforming structure or tree has been abandoned
or more than eighty percent (80%) torn down, physically deteriorated, or
decayed, no permit shall be granted that would allow such structure or tree to
exceed the applicable height limit or otherwise deviate from the zoning
regulations. (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973)
   D.   Variances:
      1.   Any person desiring to erect or increase the height of any
structure, or permit the growth of any tree or use his property not in
accordance with the regulations prescribed in this article must obtain a permit
from the city council authorizing such action. Such variances shall be allowed
where literal application or enforcement of this article would result in
practical difficulty and unnecessary hardship, and the relief granted would not
be contrary to the public interest or create undue hazards to air flight. Any
such special permits may be allowed subject to such reasonable conditions as
the city council may deem necessary to effectuate the purposes of this article,
including the condition that the owners of the structure or tree in question
permit the city to install, operate and maintain at its own expense such
markers and lights as may be necessary to indicate to flyers the presence of an
airport hazard. (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973; amd. 2010 Code)
      2.   Whenever a permit is required or a variance requested under the
terms of this article, all the procedures, remedies, powers and jurisdiction
set forth in title 10, chapters 2 and 11 of this code shall apply insofar as
they do not conflict with this article. If a permit under this article, and a
permit under the zoning title of this code 1 , are sought simultaneously, the
permits may be treated as one, with only one permit fee necessary. (Ord. 261,
1-9-1973)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 10, chapter 2 of this code.
7-3A-8: CONFLICTING REGULATIONS:
Where there exists a conflict between any of the regulations or limitations
prescribed in this article and any other regulations applicable to the same
area, whether the conflict be with respect to the height of structures or
trees, the use of land, or any other matter, the more stringent limitation or
requirement shall govern and prevail. (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973)
7-3A-9: PENALTY:
Each violation of this article, or of any regulation, order, or ruling
promulgated hereunder shall constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code, and each day a violation continues to exist shall
constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 261, 1-9-1973; amd. 2010 Code)
TITLE 8
PUBLIC UTILITIES AND SERVICES
Utility Services   1
Water System Regulations   2
Cross Connection Control   2A
Sewer System Regulations   3
Refuse Collection And Disposal   4
CHAPTER 1
UTILITY SERVICES
SECTION:
8-1-1: Definitions
8-1-2: Utility Service Billings
8-1-3: Monthly Billings; Lien For Nonpayment
8-1-4: Discontinuance Of Service By Utility User
8-1-5: Installation Of Electrical Or Communication Facilities
8-1-6: Penalty
8-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
UTILITY CHARGE: The fee, rental, rate, charge, service charge or assessment
provided for in this title, as reimbursement to the city for the rendering to
the utility user of the services of that particular utility for which the
charge is made.
UTILITY SERVICE: The municipal water service, the municipal refuse service and
the municipal sewage service are each defined as a "utility service" of the
city of Craigmont.
UTILITY SERVICE BILL: The statement containing the combined total amounts of
all utility charges due and payable to the city for utility services furnished
and delinquency charges assessed.
UTILITY USER: The owner of the property to which one or all the utility
services of the city is supplied. (1963 Code § 8-501)
8-1-2: UTILITY SERVICE BILLINGS:
   A.   Joint Liability: The owner and occupant of any premises using the water
system shall be jointly and severally liable for all fees and charges assessed
by the city. (1963 Code § 8-502; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Monthly Billings On Itemized Statement:
      1.   Utility service billings shall be made monthly on an itemized
statement which shall contain the following information: period covered by
billings; water meter reading date; present water meter reading at billing
date; water meter reading at last billing; and a statement as to the amount of
water used or the estimated amount of water used.
      2.   In addition, the utility statement shall contain information in a
monetary amount as to: the water rental due, or estimated rental due; water
rental past due; refuse services due; refuse services past due; sewer rental
due; sewer rental past due; and delinquency or service charges, if any. The
utility service bill shall then contain a total of all utility charges due and
payable to the city. (1963 Code § 8-502)
   C.   Utility Charges Not Prorated: If any utility services are supplied to a
premises for any portion of a calendar month, such utility service shall be
billed to the utility user for the entire month. No utility charge shall be
prorated for a portion of any month. (1963 Code § 8-505)
   D.   Returned Check Charge: Accounts with returned checks will be assessed a
return check charge in such sum as set from time to time by resolution of the
city council. (2010 Code)
8-1-3: MONTHLY BILLINGS; LIEN FOR NONPAYMENT:
   A.   Delinquencies: All utility service bills are due and payable monthly on
the 26th day of the month following the month in which said services are used
and shall be delinquent if unpaid by the 27th day of the month following the
month in which such services were used. If not paid before delinquent, a charge
of $15.00 shall be added to the amount previously due the first month following
the month in which said services are used and an additional charge of $25.00
shall be added each month thereafter.
   B.   Authority to Discontinue Service: The 15th of the month following the
month the charges for utility services become delinquent, the City maintenance
supervisor is hereby authorized and directed to cut off the municipal water
service and the municipal sewer service from the premises to which utility
services were furnished. The City shall assess an additional fee of $25.00 for
turning off the water and an additional fee of $25.00 for turning the water
back on. Said services shall remain cut off until all of the utility service
bill, utility services charges, and delinquency charges have been paid in full.
   C.   Notice of Discontinued Service: Before turning off the municipal water
service, the city shall notify the owner of the property serviced by causing a
written notice of the pending action to be posted on the property at least ten
(10) days before the water service is turned off. (Ord. 341, 2-6-1990; amd.
2010 Code; Ord. 423, 7-7-2020)
8-1-4: DISCONTINUANCE OF SERVICES BY UTILITY USER:
Utility services may be discontinued by the utility user under certain
conditions by the exercise of one of the following options:
   A.   Option 1:
      1.   Whenever any utility user desires to discontinue such utility
services because the property to which such services are supplied has been
vacated or is uninhabited, or will be unused for a period of time, he shall
notify the city maintenance supervisor that he wishes all such utility services
to be discontinued. The utility user shall exhibit to the city maintenance
supervisor his most recent utility service bill showing that all utility
services, as well as all service charges, have been paid to date. If all
utility services and service charges have been paid in full to date, the city
maintenance supervisor shall immediately disconnect or turn off the municipal
water service from the utility user's premises and shall notify all the
appropriate city departments that all utility services are to be discontinued,
as well as the date of their discontinuance. Whenever a utility user desires to
recommence the utility services discontinued as above provided, the city
maintenance supervisor shall immediately turn on or reconnect the municipal
water service to the utility user's premises. The city maintenance supervisor
shall notify all the appropriate city departments that all utility services are
to be reinstated to the utility user's premises and the date at which utility
services are to commence. No fee or service charge shall be assessed for any of
the above services.
      2.   Pursuant to option 1 outlined in subsection A1 of this section, all
utility service billings shall be abated and discontinued, and all utility
services shall be discontinued until the utility user notifies the city
maintenance supervisor that the utility services should be reinstated.
   B.   Option 2:
      1.   Whenever any utility user desires to discontinue a portion of the
utility services because the property to which such services are supplied has
been vacated, is uninhabited or will be unused for a period of time, he shall
notify the city maintenance supervisor that he wishes to continue the municipal
water service and discontinue the municipal refuse service. The utility user
shall exhibit to the city maintenance supervisor his most recent utility
service bill showing that all utility services, as well as all service charges,
have been paid to date. If all utility services and service charges have been
paid in full to date, the city maintenance supervisor shall notify the
appropriate city department that the municipal refuse service is to be
discontinued and that the municipal water service is to be continued. No
service charge shall be assessed.
      2.   Pursuant to option 2 as outlined in subsection B1 of this section,
that portion of the utility service bill applying to the municipal refuse
service shall be abated and discontinued until the premises is used or
inhabited, or until the utility user has returned to the premises. That portion
of the utility service bill applying to the municipal water service and the
municipal sewage service shall continue to be assessed and billed to the
utility user. (1963 Code § 8-504; amd. 2010 Code)
8-1-5: INSTALLATION OF ELECTRICAL OR COMMUNICATION FACILITIES:
   A.   Scope And Exceptions.
      1.   It is found and determined by the City that the general public
necessity, convenience, health, safety, and welfare require that electrical or
communication facilities be constructed aboveground in an orderly manner in
accordance with the requirements specified in this chapter.
      2.   This section shall apply to everyone who owns electrical facilities
or communication facilities, including but not limited to telephone and cable
television facilities, within the corporate city limits.
   B.   Cost.
      1.   The cost of constructing new facilities aboveground or relocating
existing underground facilities aboveground shall be borne by the serving
utilities, the owners of the real property to be served, or others requesting
such aboveground services in accordance with the applicable rules, regulations,
and policies of the respective utilities furnishing such service.
   C.   Aboveground Requirements.
      1.   The following requirements shall apply to new facilities:
         a.   All major additions of new facilities shall be aboveground.
      2.   The following requirements shall apply to relocations or
rearrangements:
         a.   Relocations or rearrangements of underground facilities
necessitated by, but not limited to, road widening, sewer and water main
projects, shall be moved aboveground, if practicable.
      3.   The following requirements shall apply to service connections:
         a.   Service connections are facilities extending from a distribution
system and terminating on private property to serve a customer or subscriber.
Service connections must be aboveground.
   D.   Design Standards.
      1.   All conductors, switches, transformers, and regulating devices shall
be installed in accordance with the applicable national, state, and local
safety standards. All structural devices shall be designed in accordance with
the provisions of the International Building Code. All aboveground facilities
provided for in this section shall be installed in such manner as to coordinate
with other aboveground facilities.
   E.   Variance Process.
      1.    Any owner of electrical facilities or communication facilities
affected by this ordinance may apply to the City council for a variance from
the provisions of this ordinance. The council may, in its sole discretion,
grant relief from the terms of this ordinance. However, any underground
facilities permitted pursuant to this variance process must be placed in
appropriate conduit and located in compliance with existing city requirements.
(Ord. 421, 9-3-2019)
8-1-6: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall, upon conviction
thereof, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to
section
1-4-1  of this code. (1963 Code § 8-506)
CHAPTER 2
WATER SYSTEM REGULATIONS
SECTION:
8-2-1: Definitions
8-2-2: Enforcement And Authority

8-2-4: Notify Maintenance Supervisor At Beginning Of Service

8-2-7: Separate Service Connections Required; Exceptions
8-2-8: Location And Maintenance Of Service Pipes
8-2-9: Rates And Charges

8-2-11: Supplying Water To Persons Or Property; Permit
8-2-12: Emergency Cut Off Of Water; Nonliability Of City
8-2-13: Unlawful Connections
8-2-14: Unlawful Use Of Water
8-2-15: Water Use During Fires Prohibited
8-2-16: Unlawful Tampering With Service Pipes Or Water System
8-2-17: Certain Acts Prohibited
8-2-18: Obstructing Fire Hydrant And Other Acts
8-2-19: Refusing Access To Premises; Penalties

8-2-23: Services Outside City Limits Prohibited; Exceptions
8-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meanings of terms used
in this chapter shall be as follows:
PERSON OR CONSUMER: Any individual, firm, company, association, society,
corporation or group.
PREMISES OR PROPERTY: The real property or buildings served or proposed to be
served by the city water system.
PUBLIC COMMISSIONER OF UTILITIES: The enforcement official for this chapter,
his agent or representative.
SHALL; MAY: "Shall" is mandatory; "may" is permissible.
SUPERVISOR: The maintenance supervisor of Craigmont, his authorized agent or
representative.
WATER MAIN: A pipe or conduit for carrying domestic water.
WATER SYSTEM: All facilities for storing, pumping, treating and distributing of
water. (1963 Code § 3-341; amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-2: ENFORCEMENT AND AUTHORITY:
   A.   Water Division Established: The water division of the department of
public utilities of the city is hereby established. (1963 Code § 3-301)
   B.   Authority Of Commissioner Of Public Utilities: The commissioner of
public utilities shall have full supervision, charge and control of the water
division. He shall make and enforce such rules as he may deem necessary for the
efficient administration and regulation of the division. The maintenance
supervisor shall, subject to the direction and authority of the commissioner of
public utilities, have direct charge of the municipal water supply system of
the city. (1963 Code § 3-302; amd. 2010 Code)
   C.   Utility Account Collector: The city clerk-treasurer shall be
responsible to collect the water accounts and other utility accounts of the
city. (1963 Code § 3-339; amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-3: APPLICATION FOR CONNECTION:
   A.   Application: Any person, firm or corporation desiring to have property
connected with the water supply system of the city shall make an application
therefor to the superintendent of water on a printed form to be furnished by
the water division. (1963 Code § 3-303)
   B.   Form And Contents Of Application:
      1.   The application shall be made and signed by the owner or lessee of
the property, or the authorized agent of such owner or lessee and shall fully
state:
         a.   All the purposes for which the water shall be used.
         b.   The number of service pipes desired.
         c.   Whether there is to be more than one building or more than one
separate property supplied by the one service connection with the city main.
         d.   The number and kind of buildings and properties so supplied.
         e.   Probable consumption.
         f.   The size of service pipe or connection believed to be necessary
therefor.
         g.   The name of the applicant, and whether owner, authorized agent or
renter.
      2.   Such application shall contain an agreement that the applicant will
at all times conform to and be governed by the rules and regulations of the
water division and provisions of this chapter, and that he will pay for all
water used on the premises, at the rate supplied in said rules. (1963 Code § 3-
304)
8-2-4: NOTIFY MAINTENANCE SUPERVISOR AT BEGINNING OF SERVICE:
Any person occupying any premises and using water therein from the city water
system shall notify the supervisor at the time of beginning such service,
whether or not the water is turned on at said premises. If any person uses
water from the city water system without first notifying the supervisor, it
will be assumed that he has used such service since service was last
discontinued at such premises, and he shall be charged accordingly. (1963 Code
§ 3-319; amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-5: WATER METER REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Installation Of Meters:
      1.   New Services: Whenever any new service shall be installed connecting
any property with the water supply system of the city, a meter shall be
installed with the service and water will be supplied to the property through
such meter only. (1963 Code § 3-305)
      2.   Any Premises: Meters shall be installed on any premises whatsoever
when, in the opinion of the water division, the installation of a meter may for
any just reason be deemed necessary. (1963 Code § 3-306)
   B.   Meter Supplied By City: Five-eighths inch (5/8") meters shall be
supplied by the city at no charge to the consumer; however, in the event a
consumer wishes to have a meter larger than five- eighths inch (5/8")
installed, then such consumer shall pay to the city the difference in the cost
of such meter and the cost of a five-eighths inch (5/8") meter. (Ord. 284, 1-3-
1978)
   C.   Size And Design Of Meters: All meters shall be of a standard size and
design approved by the maintenance supervisor and each meter shall, before it
is installed, be separately examined, tested and approved by him. (1963 Code §
3-309; amd. 2010 Code)
   D.   Testing Accuracy Of Meters: When the accuracy of the record of a water
meter is questioned by a consumer, the meter shall be removed at his request
and shall be tested by the supervisor in the presence of the consumer and
record kept thereof. Both parties shall accept the findings so made. Before
making such tests, the consumer, at the time of filing his request, shall
deposit with the supervisor such sum as set by resolution of the city council.
If a test so made discloses an error against the consumer of more than three
percent (3%) in the meter register, the excess of such reading as applied to
the three (3) readings next preceding the test shall be calculated and the
amount of money due the consumer thereon credited to his meter account. The
water division shall bear the entire expense of the test and the deposit of the
consumer shall be returned to him. If no error in excess of three percent (3%)
against the consumer is found, the consumer shall pay the cost of the test out
of his deposit. No meter shall be removed or in any way disturbed nor the seal
broken except in the presence, and under the supervision of, the supervisor.
(1963 Code § 3-310; amd. 2010 Code)
   E.   Inspection And Examination Of Premises: The water division reserves the
right to enter at any reasonable time any premises where city water is used,
for the purpose of making an examination of the premises, or a test of the
meter, and it also reserves the right to remove the meter from the premises for
examination and test when necessary. (1963 Code § 3-311)
   F.   Meters Property Of City: All meters shall be and remain the property of
the city and shall not be removed from the service except for tests or repair,
replacement or on abandonment or discontinuance of the service. All meters
shall be so located and maintained as to be readily accessible at all
reasonable hours for reading, inspection and repairs. (1963 Code § 3-312)
   G.   Lost, Damaged Or Broken Meters: In cases where a meter has been lost,
damaged or broken, by or through the carelessness or negligence of the owner or
the occupant of the premises served, such meter shall be properly repaired and
restored under the direction of the supervisor and the cost thereof shall be
charged against the owner or occupant of the premises. In cases of nonpayment
of such charges, the water shall be turned off and not again turned on until
the cost of repairs and the penalty for shutting off and turning on the water
has been paid. (1963 Code § 3-313; amd. 2010 Code)
   H.   Meter Out Of Order; Estimate Of Charges: In the event of a water meter
getting out of order or failing to register properly, the consumer shall be
charged on an estimate made from the most reliable data in the possession of
the water division. (1963 Code § 3-314)
8-2-6: METERS AND MATERIALS PROPERTY OF CITY:
All meters furnished and all materials supplied by the water department in the
installation or repair of any meter or meters, and all materials supplied in
the installation of any service connection with the city mains, or tapping any
city main, shall remain the property of the city and may be removed by the
water department at any time for the nonpayment of any charges or installment
due. (1963 Code § 3-334)
8-2-7: SEPARATE SERVICE CONNECTIONS REQUIRED; EXCEPTIONS:
Every separate building supplied with city water must have its own separate
service connection with the city mains, except that two (2) or more buildings
located on the same lot, or on contiguous lots under a single ownership, may
be, upon written permission granted by the supervisor, supplied through the
same connection with the city main in cases where a water meter is installed in
the service, as long as said single ownership continues. Upon change from
single ownership, a new and separate connection shall be immediately made for
the building or premises theretofor having the indirect connection. (1963 Code
§ 3-315; amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-8: LOCATION AND MAINTENANCE OF SERVICE PIPES:
All service pipes from the city mains or from other service pipes to the
property line, including a service cock, shall be placed one foot (1') inside
the curb line, and shall be installed and maintained by the city. The property
owner must install and maintain at his own expense, all service pipes and all
plumbing within his own premises. Every service pipe shall be provided with a
stop and waste cock for each consumer, easily accessible and placed in such a
location that it will not be damaged by frost or freezing, and so situated that
the water can be conveniently shut off and drained from the pipes. All water in
buildings shall be so arranged as to drain toward the stop and waste cock
fixtures or drain cocks placed for that purpose. All water pipes shall be
either galvanized iron, brass or lead. All service pipes inside property lines
shall be laid to a depth of not less than two feet (2') so that they will not
be affected by frost or freezing. (1963 Code § 3-316)
8-2-9: RATES AND CHARGES:
   A.   Service Charges: Charges for water supplied by the city water system
shall be as set by resolution of the city council from time to time, as listed
on the "City Water Rate Schedule". (1963 Code § 3-335; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Deposit Required From Nonowner Residential Customers: An advance
deposit in such amount as set by resolution of the city council shall be
required from all nonowner residential customers before the city water will be
supplied in such customer's name. In the event, however, that the owner/
landlord of such residential property shall file with the city clerk-treasurer
a written statement guaranteeing payment of such account, then said deposit
shall be waived. (Ord. 359, 11-7-1995; amd. 2010 Code)
   C.   Charge For Turning Water Off Or On: Whenever water is turned off or on
by the city, the fee for the service shall be such sum as set by resolution of
the city council. (Ord. 402, 10-9-2007; amd. 2010 Code)
   D.   Installation Of Meters And Charge: The actual installation of all
meters shall be done by the water division. The City of Craigmont shall assess
and collect from each and every new consumer of water, a fee of two thousand
dollars ($2,000.00), plus the actual cost to the City to repair any damage to
any street or alleyway, for the installation of the water meter and connecting
water to the consumer’s premises to be paid prior to such service connection.
   E.   Determination Of Summer Irrigation Rates: The commissioner of public
utilities shall designate any continuous ninety (90) day period during the
months of June, July, August and September of each year during which period
summer irrigation rates shall be applied to all residential property, or
property in no way used for commercial purposes. (1963 Code § 3-336)
   F.   Surcharge On Nonresident Consumption: All water used by consumers on
premises located outside the city limits shall pay double that rate paid for
water by residents of the city. This charge is made to partially compensate the
city for not obtaining tax money from the premises served for use on the water
system. (Ord. 269, 7-9-1974; amd. 2010 Code)
   G.   Credit Allowed Fire Department Members: All active members in good
standing of the Craigmont volunteer fire department shall be allowed a maximum
credit in such amount as set by resolution of the city council per month
against their water accounts. This credit shall not be cumulative but shall be
used in full each month, nor shall this credit be in any way applied against
the sewer accounts. This sum is granted to them as partial consideration for
their services. The fire chief shall quarterly submit to the supervisor or to
the city clerk-treasurer a list of all active members of the volunteer fire
department. (1963 Code §§ 3-336, 3-338; amd. Ord. 269, 7-9-1974; Ord. 401, 10-
9-2007; 2010 Code; Ord. 430, 11-2-2021)
8-2-10: NEWLY INSTALLED SERVICES:
In all cases where a water service has been newly installed connecting any
premises or building with city mains, and in all cases of reconstruction,
alteration or repair of any building where new or additional water service or
fixtures have been installed, city water shall not be turned into such service
until all charges for water used on the premises for any purpose shall have
been paid. (1963 Code § 3-322)
8-2-11: SUPPLYING WATER TO PERSONS OR PROPERTY; PERMIT:
   A.   Permit Required:
      1.   No owner or lessee of property supplied with water from the city
mains shall furnish water to any other person or property without first
obtaining a written permit to do so from the maintenance supervisor.
      2.   No permit will be issued until the person desiring to use the water
has obtained and filed with the supervisor the written consent of the owner or
lessee of the property from which the water is to be taken, stating the
location of such property by street and number, and the location by street and
number of the property to be supplied with water, and stating the purpose for
which the water is to be used.
      3.   Upon receipt of a proper permit as above provided, from the owner or
lessee of the property from which the water is to be taken, and where water is
taken from premises paying a flat rate, upon payment in advance for the water
for the whole term for which the permit is issued, the supervisor may issue a
temporary permit allowing water to be supplied to other persons or property for
domestic and for other purposes, but no permit shall be issued for a longer
time than three (3) months.
   B.   Violation: Any person allowing water to be taken from the premises
owned or occupied by him by any person without such person having a permit from
the supervisor shall be in violation of this chapter. (1963 Code § 3-323; amd.
2010 Code)
8-2-12: EMERGENCY CUT OFF OF WATER; NONLIABILITY OF CITY:
   A.   City Authority: The maintenance supervisor may, in an emergency, order
the water cut off from any premises connected with the city mains, without
notice, for repairs or other necessary purposes.
   B.   Nonliability Of City: The city will not be liable for any damage that
may occur on account of the water being cut off for any of the above purposes,
or on account of the breaking of any pipe or fixture by pressure of the water
from the city mains. (1963 Code § 3-324; amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-13: UNLAWFUL CONNECTIONS:
It shall be unlawful for any person except a competent person authorized by the
supervisor to make any connection with a city service pipe or with any part of
the city water system. (1963 Code § 3-317; amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-14: UNLAWFUL USE OF WATER:
When water has been shut off from any premises, either upon the application of
the owner or occupant thereof, or for nonpayment of water charges, or for any
other cause, it shall be a misdemeanor for any person to again connect such
premises with the city water supply system except when specifically authorized
so to do by the supervisor; and the supervisor may cause the water to be shut
off at the main, or may remove a portion of the service connection in the
street. In addition to the penalty in this chapter provided for violation of
its provisions, the water department may also charge to and collect from the
owner or occupant of the premises so illegally connected, the whole cost of the
disconnection and reconnection, and a fee for shutting off the water, and a fee
for turning on the water, in such total amount as set by resolution of the city
council, the whole of such fees and charges to be paid before the water is
again turned on. (1963 Code § 3-320; amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-15: WATER USE DURING FIRES PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to use water for irrigation or sprinkling
during the progress of any fire in the city except for protection from fire,
and all such irrigation and sprinkling shall be immediately stopped when the
fire alarm is sounded and not resumed until the fire is extinguished. (1963
Code § 3-333)
8-2-16: UNLAWFUL TAMPERING WITH SERVICE PIPES OR WATER SYSTEM:
   A.   City Service Pipes: No person, other than the maintenance supervisor or
his authorized agent, shall use any street key or other device for the purpose
of shutting off water or turning on same outside of his property line; nor
shall any person uncover or attempt to uncover, or tamper with any pipe, valve,
meter, meter box, curb stop or curb stop box of a city service connection
without authority from the supervisor. (1963 Code § 3-318; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Water System: It shall be unlawful for any person to open or shut any
street cock or to in any way tamper with or injure any meter, valve or service
pipe connecting any premises or building with the city water supply, or to tap
or in any manner to tamper with any fire line, unless such person be a regular
employee of the water division. (1963 Code § 3-325)
8-2-17: CERTAIN ACTS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person, with intent to injure or defraud, to:
   A.   Break or deface any water meter.
   B.   Obstruct, alter, injure or prevent the action of any meter or other
instrument used to measure or register the quantity of water supplied to a
consumer.
   C.   Make any connection by means of a pipe, or otherwise, with any main or
pipe used for a delivery of water to a consumer thereof, in such manner as to
take water from said main or pipe without its passage through the meter or
other instrument provided for registering the amount or quantity consumed, or
use any water so obtained.
   D.   Make any connection or reconnection with such main or pipe, or turn on
or off, or in any manner interfere with any valve, stopcock or other appliance
connected therewith.
   E.   Prevent by the erection of any device or construction, or by any other
means, free access to any meter or other instrument for registering or
measuring the amount of water consumed, or interfere with, obstruct or prevent
by any means, the reading or inspection of such meter or instrument, by any of
the officers or authorized employees of the city. (1963 Code § 3-326)
8-2-18: OBSTRUCTING FIRE HYDRANT AND OTHER ACTS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct the access to any fire hydrant
by placing around, thereon, or within twenty feet (20') thereof any stone,
brick, lumber, dirt, rubbish or other material, or to open or separate any fire
hydrant, or to draw or attempt to draw water therefrom, or to wilfully or
carelessly injure the same, or to fill up or cover over any curb box, or in any
manner to tamper with or injure the same. In the event that any person shall
wilfully, carelessly or otherwise injure or break any fire hydrant, street
standpipe, public drinking fountain, or other device or thing connected with
the city water supply system, he shall at once report the occurrence to the
supervisor or to the law enforcement officer, and shall give such undertaking
as may be required of him that he will pay the costs of the repairs or
replacement thereto made necessary. Failure to so report and accept
responsibility for such damage shall also result in the offender being deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and punished accordingly. (1963 Code § 3-327; amd. 2010
Code)
8-2-19: REFUSING ACCESS TO PREMISES; PENALTIES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to refuse, neglect or fail to afford any
duly authorized representative of the water department free access at all
reasonable hours to any and all parts of buildings or premises supplied with
water from the city water supply system. For the purpose of making records,
readings and inspection of the location, condition and sufficiency of pipes,
fittings, values, cocks, fixtures and appliances, and noting the amount of
water used and the manner in which it is used. Violation of this provision, or
the abuse, threatening or attempted intimidation of any officer of the water
department, may result in the shutting off of the water and the imposition of
the usual penalties in addition to punishment for violation of this chapter as
elsewhere herein provided. (1963 Code § 3-328)
8-2-20: IRRIGATION WATER USE:
   A.   Irrigation With Unmetered Services: On unmetered service, a moderate
amount of water for irrigation may be used, which privilege may be cancelled by
the supervisor if water is used beyond a reasonable amount. (1963 Code § 3-329;
amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Irrigation Regulations: No water shall be used for irrigation except
through a nozzle, spray nozzle, or other sprinkling device; and no hose or
sprinkling device shall be left running unattended. (1963 Code § 3-330)
   C.   Authority To Prohibit Use: In case of shortage of water, the use for
irrigation may be prohibited by the maintenance supervisor. (1963 Code § 3-331;
amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-21: SHORTAGES AND EMERGENCIES:
If any person refuses to comply with the request of any employee of the water
department to conserve water during a shortage or emergency, water service may
be discontinued. (1963 Code § 3-332)
8-2-22: PRIVATE WATER SYSTEMS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to own, operate, or
maintain a private water well or system within the limits of the city. This
section shall not affect those private water systems which are in use on the
effective date hereof. (Ord. 269, 7-9-1974; amd. 2010 Code)
8-2-23: SERVICES OUTSIDE CITY LIMITS PROHIBITED; EXCEPTIONS:
No water mains shall be constructed or laid by the city outside of the city
limits to any premises. Provided however, mains may be laid to properties
belonging to the city. All proposed consumers who have property outside the
city limits and who desire to obtain city water shall construct their own mains
from the city limits to their property at their own expense. All city meters in
such cases shall be placed as near as practicable to the city limits. (1963
Code § 3-340)
ARTICLE A. CROSS CONNECTION CONTROL
SECTION:
8-2A-1: Purpose And Scope
8-2A-2: Definitions
8-2A-3: Cross Connections
8-2A-4: Use Of Backflow Prevention Devices
8-2A-5: Cross Connection Inspection
8-2A-6: Installation Permits
8-2A-7: Additional Remedies
8-2A-8: Civil Action
8-2A-9: Misdemeanor
8-2A-10: Liability
8-2A-1: PURPOSE AND SCOPE:
The purpose of this article is to protect the public health of water consumers
of the city of Craigmont by the control of actual and/or potential cross
connections. (Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
8-2A-2: DEFINITIONS:
BACKFLOW: The flow, other than the intended direction of flow, of any foreign
liquids, gases, or substances into the distribution system of the city water
supply.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICE: A device to counteract back pressure or prevent
back siphonage.
CITY: The city of Craigmont and its designated representatives.
CONTAMINATION: The entry into or presence in a city water supply of any
substance which may be deleterious to health and/or quality of the water.
CROSS CONNECTION: Any physical arrangement whereby the city water supply is
connected, directly or indirectly, with any other water supply system, sewer,
drain, conduit, pool, storage reservoir, plumbing fixture, or other device
which contains or may contain contaminated water, sewage or other waste or
liquids of unknown or unsafe quality which may be capable of imparting
contamination to the city water supply as a result of backflow. (Ord. 2011-409,
5-3-2011)
8-2A-3: CROSS CONNECTIONS:
No water service connection to any premises shall be installed or continued in
the city unless the water supply is protected by backflow prevention devices as
may be required by this article, Idaho Code, and all standards, rules, and
regulations of the state of Idaho, the Idaho department of health and welfare,
and any other federal, state, county, or city authority or agency thereof. The
installation or maintenance of a cross connection which will endanger the water
quality of the potable water supply of the city of Craigmont shall be unlawful
and is prohibited. Any such cross connection now existing or hereafter
installed is hereby declared to be a public nuisance and the same shall be
abated. The control or elimination of cross connections shall be in accordance
with this article, Idaho Code, and all standards, rules, and regulations of the
state of Idaho, the Idaho department of health and welfare, and any other
federal, state, county, or city authority or agency thereof, together with the
latest addition of appropriate manuals of standard practice pertaining to cross
connection control enacted by the city and any applicable county, state, and
federal authorities and agencies. The city shall have the authority to
establish requirements more stringent than state regulations if it deems that
the conditions so dictate. (Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
8-2A-4: USE OF BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICES:
   A.   Backflow prevention devices shall be installed in connection with water
service connections or within any premises where, in the judgment of the city,
the nature and extent of the activities, or the materials stored on the
premises, would present an immediate and dangerous hazard to health and/or be
deleterious to the quality of the water should a cross connection occur; even
though such cross connection does not exist at the time the backflow prevention
devices shall be installed under circumstances including, but not limited to,
the following:
      1.   Premises having an auxiliary water supply, unless the quality of the
auxiliary supply is in compliance with Idaho Code, and all standards, rules,
and regulations of the state of Idaho, the Idaho department of health and
welfare, and any other federal, state, county, or city authority or agency
thereof and is acceptable to the city.
      2.   Premises having internal cross connections that are not correctable,
or intricate plumbing arrangements which make it impracticable to ascertain
whether or not cross connections exist.
      3.   Premises where entry is restricted so that inspections for cross
connections cannot be made with sufficient frequency or at sufficiently short
notice to ensure that cross connections are not being established or
reestablished.
      4.   Premises having a repeated history of cross connections being
established or reestablished.
      5.   Premises on which any substance is handled under pressure so as to
permit entry into the city water supply, or where a cross connection could
reasonably be expected to occur. This shall include the handling of process
waters and cooling waters.
      6.   Premises where materials of a toxic or hazardous nature are handled
in such a way that if back siphonage should occur, a serious health hazard
might result.
      7.   The following types of facilities will fall into one of the above
categories where a backflow prevention device is required to protect the city
water supply. A backflow prevention device shall be installed at these
facilities unless the city and applicable state, county, and federal
authorities and agencies determine that no hazard exists:
         a.   Hospitals, mortuaries, clinics.
         b.   Laboratories, including school laboratories.
         c.   Metal plating industries.
         d.   Sewage treatment plants.
         e.   Food or beverage processing plants.
         f.   Chemical plants using a water process.
         g.   Petroleum processing or storage plants.
         h.   Dry cleaners.
Other premises as specified by the city, where backflow prevention devices are
required to protect the city water supply.
   B.   The type of protective device required shall depend on the degree of
hazard which exists:
      1.   An air gap separation or a reduced pressure principle backflow
prevention device shall be installed where the city water supply may be
contaminated with sewage, industrial waste of a toxic nature, or other
contaminant which could cause a health or system hazard.
      2.   In the case of a substance which may be objectionable but not
hazardous to health, a double check valve assembly, air prevention device shall
be installed.
      3.   Backflow prevention devices required by this article shall be
installed at the meter, at the property line of the premises when meters are
not used, or at a location designated by the city. The device shall be located
so as to be readily accessible for maintenance and testing, and furthermore,
where no part of the device will be submerged.
   C.   Backflow prevention devices required by this article shall be installed
under the supervision of, and with the approval of, the city.
   D.   Any protective device required by this article shall be approved by the
city, applicable state, county, and federal authorities and agencies. These
devices shall be furnished and installed by and at the expense of the customer.
   E.   Backflow prevention devices installed pursuant to this article, shall
be inspected and tested annually, or more often if necessary. Inspections,
tests, and maintenance shall be at the customer's expense, and, if requested by
the city, by a certified tester retained and paid by the customer. Whenever the
devices are found to be defective, they shall be repaired, overhauled, or
replaced at the customer's expense. Inspections, tests, repairs and records
thereof shall be accomplished in accordance with all standards, rules and
regulations of this article, Idaho Code, and all standards, rules, and
regulations of the state of Idaho, the Idaho department of health and welfare,
and any other federal, state, county, or city authority or agency thereof by
certified testers retained and paid by the customer.
   F.   No underground sprinkling device will be installed without adequate
backflow prevention devices at the point from which the water for irrigation is
taken from the city water supply.
   G.   Failure of the customer to cooperate in the installation, maintenance,
testing, or inspection of backflow prevention devices required by this article,
Idaho Code, and all standards, rules and regulations of the state of Idaho, the
Idaho department of health and welfare, and any other federal, state, county,
or city authority or agency thereof shall be grounds for the termination of
water service to the premises, or, in the alternative, the installation of an
air gap separation at the customer's expense. (Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
8-2A-5: CROSS CONNECTION INSPECTION:
   A.   No water shall be delivered to any structure hereafter built within the
city or within areas served by city water until the same shall have been
inspected by the city for possible cross connections and been approved as being
free of the same.
   B.   Any construction for industrial or other purposes which is classified
as hazardous facilities pursuant to subsection
8-2A-4A of this article, where it is reasonable to anticipate cross
connections, or as determined by the city, shall be protected by the
installation of one or more backflow prevention devices at the point of service
from the city water supply or any other location designated by the city, and
applicable county, state, and federal authorities and agencies.
   C.   Inspections may be made periodically of all buildings, structures, or
improvements of any nature now receiving water through the city's system, for
the purpose of ascertaining whether cross connections exist. Such inspections
shall be made by the city or applicable county, state, and federal authorities
and agencies. (Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
8-2A-6: INSTALLATION PERMITS:
If cross connection control device(s) are found to be necessary, the owner of
the property served must apply to the city for a specific installation permit.
(Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
8-2A-7: ADDITIONAL REMEDIES:
In the event an improper cross connection is not corrected within the time
limits set by the city, or, in the event the city is refused access to any
property for the purpose of determining whether or not cross connections exist,
the city may cease delivery of water to the property until the deficiency is
corrected to the city's satisfaction. In addition, the city without waiving any
terms of this article may, but shall not be required to, effect the necessary
repairs or installations at the expense of the property owner and refuse
delivery of water to the property until the cost thereof shall have been paid.
Violations of this article are hereby declared to be a nuisance, and the city,
after notice to the customer or property owner to remove or correct the
violation, may prevent, remove, and abate the same at the expense of the party
creating or maintaining the same, in which event the city may levy a special
assessment as provided in Idaho Code 50-1008 on the land or premises whereon
the nuisance is situated to defray the cost or to reimburse the city for the
cost of abating the same. (Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
8-2A-8: CIVIL ACTION:
In addition to, or in lieu of the foregoing, the city may bring any appropriate
civil action, including abatement, injunction, and/or damages in which event
the city shall be entitled to all costs including attorney fees in the
prosecution of such action. (Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
8-2A-9: MISDEMEANOR:
In addition to the foregoing, any person violating the provisions of this
article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof
shall be subject to the penalties as provided by law. (Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
8-2A-10: LIABILITY:
This article shall not be construed to hold the city responsible for any damage
to persons or property by reason of the inspection or testing herein, or the
failure to inspect or test or by reason of approval of any cross connections.
(Ord. 2011-409, 5-3-2011)
CHAPTER 3
SEWER SYSTEM REGULATIONS
SECTION:
8-3-1: Definitions
8-3-2: Use Of Public Sewers Required
8-3-3: Private Sewage Disposal
8-3-4: Building Sewers And Connections
8-3-5: Restrictions On Use Of Public Sewers
8-3-6: Protection From Damage
8-3-7: Powers And Authority Of Inspectors
8-3-8: Repairs And Connections; Assessment And Lien
8-3-9: User Rates And Charges
8-3-10: Privies And Cesspools Prohibited
8-3-11:    Prohibited Discharge Standards
8-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meanings of terms used
in this chapter shall be as follows:
 
                That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
                which receives the discharge from soil, waste, and other
BUILDING DRAIN: drainage pipes inside the walls of the building and conveys it
                to the building sewer, beginning five feet (5') outside the
                inner face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to the public sewer or
                other place of disposal.
COMBINED SEWER: A sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage.
GARBAGE:        Solid wastes from the preparation, cooking and dispensing of
                food, and from the handling, storage and sale of produce.
 
INDUSTRIAL WASTES:          The liquid wastes from industrial processes as
                            distinct from sanitary sewage.
NATURAL OUTLET:             Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or
                            other body of surface water or groundwater.
PERSON:                     Any individual, firm, company, association,
                            society, corporation or group.
                            The wastes from the preparation, cooking and
                            dispensing of food that have been shredded to such
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE:  degree that all particles will be carried freely
                            under the flow conditions normally prevailing in
                            public sewers, with no particle greater than one-
                            fourth inch ( 1/4") in any dimension.
                            A sewer in which all owners of abutting properties
PUBLIC SEWER:               have equal rights, and is controlled by public
                            authority.
                            A sewer which carries sewage and to which
SANITARY SEWER:             stormwater, surface water and groundwater are not
                            intentionally admitted.
                            A combination of the water carried wastes from
                            residences, business buildings, institutions and
SEWAGE:                     industrial establishments, together with such
                            groundwater, surface water and stormwater which may
                            be present.
SEWAGE TREATMENT PLANT:     Any arrangement of devices and structures used for
                            treating sewage.
SEWAGE WORKS:               All facilities for collecting, pumping, treating
                            and disposing of sewage.
SEWER:                      A pipe or conduit for carrying sewage.
SHALL; MAY:                 “Shall” is mandatory; “may” is permissive.
                            A sewer which carries stormwater and surface water
STORM SEWER OR STORM DRAIN: and drainage, but excludes sewage and polluted
                            industrial wastes.
 
SUPERVISOR:  The maintenance supervisor of the city of Craigmont, or his
             authorized deputy, agent or representative.
SUSPENDED    Solids that either float on the surface of, or are in
SOLIDS:      suspension in, water, sewage or other liquids, and which are
             removable by laboratory filtering.
WATERCOURSE: A channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously
             or intermittently. (1963 Code § 8-201; amd. 2010 Code)
 
8-3-2: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS REQUIRED:
   A.   Garbage Deposits: It shall be unlawful for any person to place,
deposit, or permit to be deposited in an unsanitary manner upon public or
private property within the city or in any area under the jurisdiction of the
city, any human or animal excrement, garbage or other objectionable waste.
   B.   Discharge Of Polluted Waters: It shall be unlawful to discharge to any
natural outlet within the city, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the
city, any sanitary sewage, industrial sewage, industrial wastes or other
polluted waters, except where suitable treatment has been provided in
accordance with subsequent provisions of this chapter.
   C.   Privies, Septic Tanks Prohibited: Except as hereinafter provided, it
shall be unlawful to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank,
cesspool, or other facility intended or used for the disposal of sewage.
   D.   Connection To Public Sewer Required: The owner of all houses, buildings
or properties used for human occupancy, employment, recreation, or other
purpose, situated within the city and abutting on any street, alley or right of
way in which there is now located or may in the future be located a public
sanitary or combined sewer of the city, is hereby required at his expense to
install suitable toilet facilities therein, and to connect such facilities
directly with the proper public sewer in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter, within ninety (90) days after date of official notice to do so;
provided, that said public sewer is within two hundred feet (200') of the
property line, and in an area physically capable of connecting to the public
sewer. (1963 Code § 8-202)
8-3-3: PRIVATE SEWAGE DISPOSAL:
   A.   Private System Allowed: Where a public sanitary or combined sewer is
not available under the provisions of section 8-3-2 of this chapter, the
building sewer shall be connected to a private sewage disposal system complying
with the provisions of this chapter.
   B.   Permit Requirements:
      1.   Before commencement or construction of a private sewage disposal
system, the owner shall first obtain a written permit signed by the supervisor.
The application for such permit shall be made on a form furnished by the city,
which the applicant shall supplement by any plans, specifications and other
information as are deemed necessary by the supervisor.
      2.   A permit for a private sewage disposal system shall not become
effective until the installation is completed to the satisfaction of the
supervisor. He shall be allowed to inspect the work at any stage of
construction and, in any event, the applicant for the permit shall notify the
supervisor when the work is ready for final inspection, and before any
underground portions are covered. The inspection shall be made within forty
eight (48) hours of the receipt of notice of the supervisor. (1963 Code § 8-
203; amd. 2010 Code)
      3.   No permit shall be issued for any private sewage disposal system
employing subsurface soil absorption facilities where the area of the lot is
less than fifteen thousand (15,000) square feet. No septic tank or cesspool
shall be permitted to discharge to any public sewer or natural outlet.
   C.   Connection To Public Sewer When Available: At such time as a public
sewer becomes available to a property served by a private sewage disposal
system, as provided in this chapter, a direct connection shall be made to the
public sewer in compliance with this chapter, and any septic tanks, cesspools,
and similar private sewage disposal facilities shall be abandoned and filled
with suitable material.
   D.   Sanitary Operation: The owner shall operate and maintain the private
sewage disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times, at no expense to
the city.
   E.   Additional Requirements: No statement contained in this section shall
be construed to interfere with any additional requirements that may be imposed
by the health officer. (1963 Code § 8-203)
8-3-4: BUILDING SEWERS AND CONNECTIONS:
   A.   Permit Required: No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any
connections with or opening into, use, alter, or disturb any public sewer or
appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the
supervisor.
   B.   Classes Of Permits; Application: There shall be two (2) classes of
buildings sewer permits: 1) for residential and commercial service; and 2) for
service to establishments producing industrial wastes. In either case, the
owner or his agent shall make application on a special form furnished by the
city. The permit application shall be supplemented by any plans,
specifications, or other information considered pertinent in the judgment of
the supervisor.
   C.   Costs Borne By Owner: All costs and expenses incident to the
installation and connection of the building sewer shall be borne by the owner.
The owner shall indemnify the city from any loss or damage that may directly or
indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the building sewer.
   D.   Separate Connections: A separate and independent building sewer shall
be provided for every building; except, where one building stands at the rear
of another on an interior lot and no private sewer is available or can be
constructed to the rear building through an adjoining alley, court, yard, or
driveway, the building sewer from the front building may be extended to the
rear building and the whole considered as one building sewer.
   E.   Old Building Sewers Used With New Buildings: Old building sewers may be
used in connection with new buildings only when they are found, on examination
and test by the supervisor, to meet all requirements of this chapter.
   F.   Laying Of Building Sewer: Whenever possible, the building sewer shall
be brought to the building at an elevation below the basement floor. No
building sewer shall be laid parallel to or within three feet (3') of any
bearing wall, which might thereby be weakened. The depth shall be sufficient to
afford protection from frost. The building sewer shall be laid a uniform grade
and in straight alignment insofar as possible. Changes in direction shall be
made only with properly curved pipe and fittings.
   G.   Drainage Requirements:
      1.   In all buildings in which any building drain is too low to permit
gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary sewage carried by such drain shall
be lifted by approved artificial means and discharged to the building sewer.
Drainage piping serving fixtures within a building located below the crown
level of the main sewer shall discharge into an approved watertight sump or
receiving tank, so located as to receive the sewage or wastes by gravity. From
such sump or receiving tank, the sewage or other liquid wastes shall be lifted
and discharged into the house drain or house sewer or ejectors, pumps or other
equally efficient approved mechanical device.
      2.   The discharge line from such ejector, pump, or other mechanical
device shall be provided with an accessible backwater valve and gate valve, and
if the gravity drainage line to which such discharge line connects is
horizontal, the method of connection shall be from the top through a "Y" branch
fitting.
      3.   All backwater valves, gate valves, motors, compressors, air tanks,
or other mechanical devices shall be located where they will be accessible for
inspection and repair at all times, and unless continuously exposed, shall be
enclosed in a watertight masonry pit, fitted with a removable cover. The pipe
leading to an ejector or other appliance for raising sewage or other waste
matter to the street sewer shall, where a water closet or closets are
installed, be provided with a vent pipe not less than four inches (4") in
diameter, and where fixtures other than water closets are installed, the waste
vent pipe shall be the same diameter as the waste pipe.
      4.   All sumps and receiving tanks shall be constructed of concrete,
metal or vitrified clay pipe. If constructed of concrete, the walls and bottom
shall be not less than six inches (6") thick. Metal sumps and receiving tanks
shall be of such thickness as to serve the purpose for which they are intended,
and shall be painted inside and outside with corrosion resisting paint. All
such sumps and receiving tanks shall be provided with substantial and tight
covers having a manhole that will permit access to the tank for repairs and
cleaning. Air tanks shall be so proportioned as to be of equal cubical capacity
to the ejectors connected therewith in which there shall be maintained an air
pressure of not less than two (2) pounds for each foot of height the sewage is
to be raised. No water operated ejectors shall be permitted.
      5.   When subsoil drainage systems are installed, they shall discharge
into an approved sump or receiving tank entirely separate and independent of
any other drainage piping. Automatic mechanical ejectors or pumps shall be used
to lift the drainage from such sump or receiving tank, and the discharge
therefrom shall terminate over a properly trapped and vented fixture of such
capacity as to prevent flooding. No water operated ejectors shall be permitted.
   H.   Excavations; Backfill: All excavations required for the installation of
a building sewer shall be open trench work unless otherwise approved by the
supervisor. Pipe laying and backfill shall be performed in accordance with ASTM
specification (C12-19) except that no backfill shall be placed until the work
has been inspected and approved. All backfills across streets or alleys must be
properly tamped.
   I.   Jointing Materials And Methods: Jointing materials and methods not
covered by building code requirements may be used only by approval of the
supervisor.
   J.   Connecting Building Sewer To Public Sewers:
      1.   The connection of the building sewer into the public sewer shall be
made at the "Y" branch, if such branch is available at a suitable location.
When a "Y" branch is not properly located or available, a neat hole may be cut
into the public sewer to receive the building sewer, with entry in the
downstream direction at an angle of about forty five degrees (45°). The
building sewer shall enter or be connected to the public sewer in the top one-
half (1/2) of the public sewer. The connection is to be made through a special
fitting which shall be the hub end of a section of the house sewer pipe cut off
or a V saddle type of connection, inserted into the tap opening of the main;
either type thoroughly caulked and cemented so as to make a tight and secure
joint.
      2.   In attaching the hub fitting to the main, the hub end of pipe shall
be cut short enough so that the shoulder of the hub shall rest flush on the
main with the end of the pipe to extend into the immediate wall of the main so
that the end thereof shall be flush with the inner face of the said wall. Each
system of piping shall be laid in a separate trench when practicable. If water
piping is laid in the same trench as a sewer, it shall be at least one foot
(1') above the top edge of the sewer and offset at least eighteen inches (18")
from the central line of the sewer, and such sewer shall be constructed of cast
iron soil pipe with approved leaded and caulked joints.
   K.   Cleanouts: Cleanouts shall be placed in every house connection sewer
when conditions are such that in the opinion of the supervisor the house sewer
line could not be readily cleared of obstructions with approved sewer cleaning
equipment applied from the nearest cleanout located in the sanitary building
drain connecting therewith. Cleanout fitting shall be of the same nominal size
as the pipes they serve, up to and including four inch (4") pipe, and not less
than four inches (4") for larger pipes.
   L.   Inspection And Supervision: The applicant for the building sewer permit
shall notify the supervisor when the building sewer is ready for inspection and
connection to the public sewer. The connection shall be made under the
supervision of the supervisor or his representative.
   M.   Guarding Of Excavations; Restoration Of Streets: All excavations for
building sewer installation shall be adequately guarded with barricades and
lights so as to protect the public from hazard. Streets, sidewalks, parkways
and other public property disturbed in the course of the work shall be restored
in a manner satisfactory to the city. (1963 Code § 8-204; amd. 2010 Code)
8-3-5: RESTRICTIONS ON USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS:
   A.   Stormwater, Other Drainage: No person shall discharge or cause to be
discharged any stormwater, surface water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface
drainage, cooling water or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary
sewer.
   B.   Prohibited Waters And Wastes: Except as hereinafter provided, no person
shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the following described waters
or wastes to any public sewer:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F).
      2.   Any water or waste which may contain more than one hundred (100)
parts per million, by weight, of fat, oil, or grease.
      3.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil, or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid or gas.
      4.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded.
      5.   Any ashes, cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags,
feathers, tar, plastics, wood, paunch manure, or any other solid or viscous
substance capable of causing obstruction to the flow in sewers or other
interference with the proper operation of the sewage works.
      6.   Any waters or wastes containing a toxic or poisonous substance in
sufficient quantity to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process,
constitute a hazard to humans or animals, or create any hazard in the receiving
waters of the sewage treatment plant.
      7.   Any waters or wastes containing suspended solids of such character
and quantity that unusual attention or expense is required to handle such
materials at the sewage treatment plant.
      8.   Any noxious or malodorous gas or substance capable of creating a
public nuisance. (1963 Code § 8-205)
   C.   Grease, Oil And Sand Interceptors:
      1.   Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the
opinion of the supervisor, they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid
wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand,
and other harmful ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be
required for private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall
be of a type and capacity approved by the supervisor, and shall be located as
to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection. Grease and oil
interceptors shall be constructed of impervious materials capable of
withstanding abrupt and extreme changes in temperature. They shall be of
substantial construction, watertight, and equipped with easily removable covers
which when bolted in place shall be gastight and watertight. (1963 Code § 8-
205; amd. 2010 Code)
      2.   Where installed, all grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be
maintained by the owner, at his expense, in continuously efficient operation at
all times.
   D.   Preliminary Treatment Facilities: Where preliminary treatment
facilities are provided for any waters or wastes, they shall be maintained
continuously in satisfactory and effective operation by the owner at his
expense.
   E.   Special Agreements With Industrial Dischargers: No statement contained
in this article shall be construed as preventing any special agreement or
arrangement between the city and any industrial concern whereby an industrial
waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by the city for
treatment, subject to payment therefor by the industrial concern. (1963 Code §
8-205)
8-3-6: PROTECTION FROM DAMAGE:
No unauthorized person shall maliciously, wilfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or
equipment which is a part of the municipal sewage works. Any person violating
this provision shall be subject to immediate arrest under charge of disorderly
conduct. (1963 Code § 8-206)
8-3-7: POWERS AND AUTHORITY OF INSPECTORS:
The supervisor and other duly authorized employees of the city bearing proper
credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter upon all properties
for the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling and testing,
in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. (1963 Code § 8-207)
8-3-8: REPAIRS AND CONNECTIONS; ASSESSMENT AND LIEN:
If any connection or any needed repair to an existing condition shall not be
made within the time herein provided, the city council is hereby authorized and
directed to cause the same to be made and to file a statement of the costs
thereof with the city clerk-treasurer, and thereupon a warrant shall be issued
under the direction of the city council by the city clerk-treasurer and against
the sewer revenue special fund of 1953, created by ordinance 172 for the
payment of such cost. The amount of such cost, together with a penalty of ten
dollars ($10.00), plus interest at eight percent (8%) per annum upon the total
amount of such costs and penalty, shall be assessed against the property upon
which said building or structure is situate and shall become a lien thereon as
hereafter provided. (1963 Code § 8-208)
8-3-9: USER RATES AND CHARGES:
   A.   Rates And Charges Established: The rates and charges for sewage
services provided by the city to individual properties served by the city sewer
system, which rates are expressed on the basis of use for each calendar month
and listed on a rate schedule, shall be set from time to time by resolution of
the city council, and shall be billed and paid accordingly. (1963 Code § 8-209;
amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Sewer Line Connection Fees/Costs: The city council may by resolution
establish and from time to time amend the fees charged by the city for
connecting a property to the city sewer system. In addition to any such
connection fees charged by the city, the city may charge and recover from the
applicant the actual costs incurred by the city to repair any damage to any and
all public property, streets, sidewalks, alleyways, or other public ways or
improvements resulting from making such connection. All said fees and costs
shall be paid by the applicant to the city prior to the city completing said
connection unless otherwise agreed by the city. (Ord. 400, 10-9-2007; amd. 2010
Code; Ord. 434, 6-6-2023)
   C.   Council Authority To Modify Or Revise Rates; Procedure:
      1.   Modify: Upon application being made or upon its own motion, the city
council shall have the authority, but not be obligated, to modify rates other
than those on the schedule referred to in subsection A of this section for
circumstances not adequately described in said schedule, or due to special
circumstances, after due notice to owners of property affected if it be shown
that such rates as applied to individual circumstances be at great variance
with similar equivalent usages as compared to uses on the schedule. Seasonal
usage, lot size, or number of persons using a particular business shall not
alone be considered special circumstances. Individual living units, whether
trailers, mobile homes or apartment units shall each be considered as an
individual residence whether or not connected to the city system by one or more
than one physical connection. (Ord. 400, 10-9-2007)
      2.   Revise: The city council hereby expressly reserves the right to
change or revise rates by council resolution adopted from time to time. (1963
Code § 8-210; amd. 2010 Code)
8-3-10: PRIVIES AND CESSPOOLS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Prohibition: It shall be unlawful for any person to dig, or use, or
cause to be dug, or used, any privy vault, or cesspool, or connect any plumbing
with a cesspool, or build, or cause to be built, any building within the limits
of the city. (1963 Code § 8-211)
   B.   Violation; Penalty: Any person violating the provisions of this section
shall, upon conviction thereof, be subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1963 Code § 8-211; amd. 2010 Code)
8-3-11: PROHIBITED DISCHARGE STANDARDS:
   A.   General prohibitions. No discharger shall introduce or cause to be
introduced into the POTW any pollutant or wastewater which causes pass through
or interference. These general prohibitions apply to all dischargers to the
POTW whether or not they are subject to categorical pretreatment standards or
any other national, state, or local pretreatment standards or requirements.
   B.   Specific prohibitions. No discharger shall introduce or cause to be
introduced into the POTW the following pollutants, substances, or wastewater:
      1.   Any liquids, solids or gases which by reason of their nature or
quantity are, or may be, sufficient either alone or by interaction with other
substances to cause fire or explosion or be injurious in any other way to the
POTW or to the operation of the POTW. In addition, waste streams with a close
cup flashpoint of less than one hundred forty (140) degrees Fahrenheit or sixty
(60) degrees Celsius using the test methods specified in 40 CFR 261.21 of the
Code of Federal Regulations.
      2.   Any solid or viscous substances which may cause obstruction to the
flow in a wastewater line or other interference with the operation of the
wastewater treatment facilities, such as, but not limited to: grease, garbage,
animal guts or tissues, paunch manure, bones, hair, hides or fleshings,
entrails, whole blood, feathers, ashes, cinders, sand, spent lime, stone or
marble dust, metal, glass, straw, shavings, grass clippings, rags, spent
grains, spent hops, wastepaper, wood, plastics, gas, tar, asphalt residues,
residues from refining or processing of fuel or lubricating oil, mud or glass
grinding or polishing wastes.
      3.   Any wastewater having a pH less than five (5) or greater than ten
(10), or wastewater having any corrosive property capable of causing damage or
hazard to structures, equipment and/or personnel of the city.
      4.   pH effluent limitations under continuous monitoring.
         a.   Where a permittee continuously measures the pH of wastewater
pursuant to a requirement of a wastewater discharge permit issued by the city,
the permittee shall maintain the pH of such waste water within the range set
forth in the permit, except excursions above ten (10) pH are permitted subject
to the following limitations:
            (1)   The total time during which the pH values are above ten (10)
pH shall not exceed seven (7) hours and twenty-six (26) minutes in any calendar
month; and
            (2)   No individual excursion above ten (10) pH shall exceed sixty
(60) minutes.
         b.   The city may adjust the requirements set forth above, with
respect to the length of individual excursions from the permitted range, if a
different period of time is appropriate based upon treatment systems, plant
configurations or other technical factors.
         c.   For purposes of this section, an ‘’excursion” is an unintentional
and temporary incident in which the pH value of discharge wastewater exceeds
the range set forth in a wastewater discharge permit.
      5.   Petroleum oil, non-biodegradable cutting oil, or products of mineral
oil origin, in amounts that will cause interference or pass through.
      6.   Pollutants which result in the presence of toxic gases, vapors, or
fumes within the wastewater system in a quantity that may cause acute worker
health and safety problems.
      7.   Sludges, screenings, or other residues from the pretreatment of
industrial wastes.
      8.   Medical waste, except as specifically authorized by the city in a
wastewater discharge permit.
      9.   Wastewater causing, alone or in conjunction with other sources, the
treatment plant’s effluent to fail a toxicity test.
      10.   Detergents, surface-active agents, or other substances which may
cause excessive foaming in the POTW.
      11.   Any wastewater containing toxic pollutants in sufficient quantity,
either singly or by interaction, to injure or interfere with any wastewater
treatment process, constitute a hazard to humans or animals, or to exceed the
limitation set forth in the categorical pretreatment standards.
      12.   Any noxious or malodorous liquids, gases or solids which, either
singly or by interaction, are capable of creating a public nuisance or hazard
to life or are sufficient to prevent entry into the city wastewater lines for
the purpose of maintenance and repair.
      13.   Any substance which may cause the POTW’s effluent or treatment
residues, biosolids or scums to be unsuitable for reclamation and reuse or to
interfere with the reclamation process. In no case shall a substance discharged
to the POTW cause the POTW to be in noncompliance with biosolids use or
disposal criteria, guidelines or regulations developed under Section 405 of the
Act; any criteria, guidelines or regulations affecting biosolids use or
disposal developed pursuant to the Solid Waste Disposal Act, the Clean Air Act,
the Toxic Substances Control Act or state standards applicable to the biosolids
management method being used.
      14.   Any substance which will cause the POTW to violate its NPDES/IPDES
and/or other disposal system permits.
      15.   Any substance with objectionable color not removed in the treatment
process, such as, but not limited to, dye wastes and vegetable tanning
solutions.
      16.   Any wastewater having a temperature which will inhibit biological
activity in the POTW treatment 19plant resulting in interference but, in no
case, wastewater with a temperature at the introduction into the POTW which
exceeds forty (40) degrees Celsius (one hundred four (104) degrees Fahrenheit),
unless the POTW treatment plant is designed to accommodate such temperature.
If, in the opinion of the city, lower temperatures of such wastes could harm
either the wastewater lines, wastewater treatment processes or equipment; have
an adverse effect on the receiving streams or otherwise endanger life, health
or property; or constitute a nuisance, the city may prohibit such discharges.
      17.   Any slug load, which shall mean any pollutant, including oxygen-
demanding pollutants (e.g., BOD) released in a single, extraordinary discharge
episode of such volume or strength as to cause interference to the POTW. In no
case shall a slug load contain concentrations or qualities of pollutants that
exceed for any time period longer than fifteen (15) minutes more than five (5)
times the average twenty-four-hour concentration, quantities or flow during
normal operation.
      18.   Stormwater, surface water, ground water, artesian well water, roof
runoff, subsurface drainage, condensate, deionized water, noncontact cooling
water, and unpolluted wastewater, unless specifically authorized by the city.
      19.   Any wastewater containing any radioactive wastes or isotopes of
such half-life or concentration that it exceed limits established by the city
in compliance with applicable state or federal regulations.
      20.   Any wastewater which, in the opinion of the city, can cause harm
