either to the wastewater lines, wastewater treatment process or equipment; have
an adverse effect on the receiving stream; or can otherwise endanger life,
limb, public property, or constitute a nuisance, unless permitted under special
agreement by the city. No special waiver shall be given from categorical
pretreatment standards.
      21.   Wastewater containing substances not amenable to treatment or
reduction by the wastewater treatment processes employed, or is amenable to
treatment only to such a degree that the wastewater treatment plant effluent
cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction over the
discharge to the receiving waters.
      22.   Any wastewater from septic tanks except as provided in sections of
this code.
      23.   Any trucked or hauled pollutants or wastes, except at discharge
points designated by the city.
   C.   Bypass of treatment facilities.
      1.   Definitions.
 
BYPASS:  The intentional diversion of waste streams from any portion of a discharger’s
         treatment facility.
         Substantial physical damage to property, damage to the treatment facilities
SEVERE   which causes them to become inoperable, or substantial and permanent loss of
PROPERTY natural resources which can reasonably be expected to occur in the absence of a
DAMAGE:  bypass. Severe property damage does not mean economic loss caused by delays in
         production.
 
      2.   Bypass not violating applicable pretreatment standards or
requirements. The discharger may allow any bypass to occur which does not cause
applicable pretreatment standards or requirements to be violated, but only if
it is for essential maintenance to assure efficient operation.
      3.   Notice.
         a.   If the discharger knows in advance of the need for a bypass, it
shall submit prior notice in writing to the city, if possible, at least ten
(10) calendar days before the date of the bypass.
         b.   The discharger shall submit oral notice of an unanticipated
bypass that exceeds applicable pretreatment standards to the city within
twenty-four (24) hours from the time the discharger becomes aware of the
bypass. A written submission shall also be provided within five (5) calendar
days of the time the discharger becomes aware of the bypass. The written
submission shall contain a description of the bypass and its cause; the
duration of the bypass, including exact dates and times, and if the bypass has
not been corrected, the anticipated time it is expected to continue; and steps
taken or planned to reduce, eliminate, and prevent recurrence of the bypass.
The city may waive the written report on a case-by-case basis if the oral
report has been received within twenty-four (24) hours.
      4.   Prohibition of bypass.
         a.   Bypass is prohibited, and the city may take enforcement action
against the permittee for a bypass, unless:
            (1)   Bypass was unavoidable to prevent loss of life, personal
injury, or severe property damage;
            (2)   There were no feasible alternatives to the bypass, such as
the use of auxiliary treatment facilities, retention of untreated wastes, or
maintenance during normal periods of equipment downtime. This condition is not
satisfied if adequate back-up equipment should have been installed in the
exercise of reasonable engineering judgment to prevent a bypass which occurred
during normal equipment downtime or preventative maintenance; and
            (3)   The discharger submitted notices as required under
subsections C.3.a. and b. of this section.
         b.   The city may approve an anticipated bypass, after considering its
adverse effects, if the city determines that it will meet the three (3)
conditions listed in subsection (c)(4)(a) of this section. (Ord. 425, 9-8-2020)
CHAPTER 4
REFUSE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL
SECTION:
8-4-1: Purpose
8-4-2: Definitions
8-4-3: System Established
8-4-4: Compulsory Use
8-4-5: Means Of Collection
8-4-6: Refuse Containers
8-4-7: Special Handling Of Rubbish
8-4-8: Collection Period
8-4-9: Collection Fees
8-4-10: Burning And Dumping
8-4-11: Vacated Premises
8-4-12: Inspection
8-4-13: Materials Not Acceptable For Collection
8-4-14: Garbage Hauling Vehicles
8-4-15: Penalty
8-4-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to eliminate unhealthy, unsanitary and unsightly
conditions in the city caused by the deposit and accumulation of refuse. (1963
Code § 8-401)
8-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
Words not defined in this section shall be defined as provided in
title 1, chapter 3 of this code. All other words shall be given the meanings
ordinarily applied to such words.
For the use of this chapter, the following terms are hereby defined:
COLLECTOR: The person holding a contract with the city of Craigmont for the
collection of garbage and refuse, or the persons employed by the city of
Craigmont and thereby authorized and designated by the city to collect, handle,
transport and dispose of refuse and waste.
GARBAGE: Shall include all putrescent waste, including waste accumulation of
animal, food or vegetable matter, and including waste that attends the
preparation, use, cooking, dealing in or storing of meat, fish, fowl, fruit and
vegetables, and shall include all of such wastes or accumulations of vegetable
matter of residences, restaurants, hotels and places where food is prepared for
human consumption. "Garbage" shall not include sewage and human body waste or
recognized industrial byproducts.
INSPECTOR: The authorized employee or employees of the city of Craigmont, or
some individual designated by the city council as having the duty of the
enforcement of this chapter.
REFUSE: Solid wastes, including garbage and rubbish.
RUBBISH: Refuse other than garbage (such as: tin cans, bottles, ashes, paper,
pasteboard, cardboard or wooden boxes, brush, leaves, weeds and cuttings from
trees, lawns, gardens and shrubs) produced in the normal course of doing
business or everyday living.
WASTE: Unwanted solid, liquid or gaseous materials. (1963 Code § 8-402)
8-4-3: SYSTEM ESTABLISHED:
There is hereby established a system of refuse collection, transportation and
disposal. It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of
collecting, transporting, hauling or conveying any refuse over the streets or
alleys, or to dump or dispose of the same unless and until such person has a
contract therefor as an authorized representative of the city. This regulation
does not prohibit a person from hauling or transporting extra loads or
accumulations of rubbish from the premises owned or occupied by said person to
one of the official disposal sites of the city that may be hereafter
established. (1963 Code § 8-403)
8-4-4: COMPULSORY USE:
   A.   Use Required: Every owner or occupant of the premises within the
prescribed limits of the city shall use the refuse collection and disposal
system herein provided, and shall deposit or cause to be deposited in
accordance with this chapter, all rubbish and garbage.
   B.   Failure To Use System; Payment Of Charges Required: The failure of any
person to use the collection and disposal system hereby provided shall not
exempt such person from the payment of the charges as set forth in the rules
and regulations on refuse control, save and except for the provisions as set
forth in this chapter. (1963 Code § 8-404)
8-4-5: MEANS OF COLLECTION:
   A.   Collection By City Or Contractor: It shall be optional whether the city
collects garbage and rubbish with its own equipment and employees, or makes a
contract with a person to collect garbage and rubbish. The city council shall,
by resolution, elect the method or methods to be used in the collection of
garbage and rubbish. The mayor and council shall be the sole authority to
contract or perform all services pertaining to sanitary collection and
disposal, and is hereby authorized to enter into contracts with one or more
contractors and establish reasonable rules and regulations governing the
conduct and operation of such contracts.
   B.   Bond Of Contractor: The city council may require of any such contractor
a bond in a reasonable amount, the condition of which shall be the satisfactory
performance of the contract. (1963 Code § 8-412)
8-4-6: REFUSE CONTAINERS:
   A.   Container Provided By Contractor: Refuse containers shall be provided
by the refuse contractor and shall be used by residents and property owners as
may be required by the refuse contractor.
   B.   Care Of Garbage: All garbage shall, before deposit in such container,
be wrapped in paper or other material so as to prevent the escape of liquids
therefrom.
   C.   Placement For Collection: All garbage or refuse containers shall be
placed in a place accessible to the collector; provided, that in the case of
isolated dwellings or places of business or where reasonable access cannot be
had by a truck, the containers may be kept in such places as may be agreed upon
by the owner and collector, or at such place as may be designated by the
inspector. Where there is no alley entrance, such containers shall be placed
adjacent to street curbs on collection days. (1963 Code § 8-406; amd. 2010
Code)
8-4-7: SPECIAL HANDLING OF RUBBISH:
Rubbish consisting only of cardboard or wooden boxes, brush, leaves, weeds and
cuttings from trees, lawns, shrubs and gardens may be kept separately without
disposing in such containers; provided, that bulk materials such as leaves
shall be in a container, box, sack or receptacle for ease of loading and that
brush, etc., shall be cut in lengths not more than four feet (4') long, and
tied in bundles. Compost piles may be maintained for fertilization purposes,
and matter used for fertilization purposes only may be transported, kept and
used. Nothing in this section shall be construed so as to permit the violation
of any ordinance or any rule or regulation of the fire department of the city.
(1963 Code § 8-407)
8-4-8: COLLECTION PERIOD:
Collectors shall collect rubbish and garbage from each customer at least once
each week, or as may otherwise be provided by the rules and regulations of the
city council. (1963 Code § 8-409)
8-4-9: COLLECTION FEES:
   A.   Commercial: Commercial container rates shall be negotiated between the
contractor and the commercial business.
   B.   Residential: Residential refuse collection rates shall be in such
amounts as set by resolution of the city council. (1963 Code § 8-410; amd. 2010
Code)
   C.   Fee For Collection From Cart: For the fees and rates hereby
established, there shall be collected from each residence, a ninety five (95)
gallon cart.
   D.   Financial Hardship; Special Permit And Fees: Provided, however, that
where the enforcement of the provisions of this chapter will work a financial
hardship, or where the garbage and refuse is of such small amounts as not to
warrant the collection of the full fees and charges as provided by this
section, the city council may issue a special permit altering the provisions of
this chapter and the fees and rates herein established. (Ord. 399, 10-9-2007)
8-4-10: BURNING AND DUMPING:
No person shall burn, incinerate, bury, dump, collect, remove or in any other
manner dispose of rubbish or garbage except as hereinafter provided.
   A.   Interior Incinerator: Any person, firm or corporation may use an
incinerator in the interior of a building between the hours of seven o'clock
(7:00) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) P.M., for rubbish, provided such
incinerator meets the requirements of the building code.
   B.   Exterior Incinerator: Burning of rubbish will be allowed in exterior
incinerators between the hours of nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. and nine o'clock (9:
00) P.M. Such incinerators shall be built of noncombustible material of not
lighter than one-eighth inch (1/8") metal, block or brick, covered by a one
inch (1") wire mesh screen. Nothing herein contained shall be construed to
prohibit the use of outdoor fireplaces, barbecue pits or grills, in preparing
food or for recreational purposes. (1963 Code § 8-405)
   C.   Open Burning: Burning of rubbish may be done in vacant lots by the
owner thereof upon obtaining a permit from the EPA through the Nez Perce Tribe
in Lapwai, Idaho, for such burning. (1963 Code § 8-405; amd. 2010 Code)
8-4-11: VACATED PREMISES:
It shall be unlawful for any person, upon vacating or removing from dwellings,
storerooms or any other building situated in the city, to fail to remove all
garbage and rubbish from such buildings and premises and also the grounds
appurtenant thereto, or to fail to place the same in a thoroughly sanitary
condition within twenty four (24) hours after the said premises shall be
vacated. (1963 Code § 8-408)
8-4-12: INSPECTION:
The law enforcement officer or such other person as may be designated as
sanitary inspector, or any other person concerned with the enforcement of laws,
shall have the right of ingress and egress to any premises for the purpose of
inspection of places and containers where rubbish or garbage is accumulated or
kept. (1963 Code § 8-411)
8-4-13: MATERIALS NOT ACCEPTABLE FOR COLLECTION:
Dirt or earth debris for construction or lawn renovation, rocks, stones,
automobile bodies and parts, dead animals, building materials such as masonry,
plaster, scrap lumber and wood shavings are not acceptable for collection, and
such items shall be collected and disposed of by the building contractor, owner
or occupant of the premises. (1963 Code § 8-413)
8-4-14: GARBAGE HAULING VEHICLES:
All collectors shall furnish vehicles designed for the collection and hauling
of garbage and rubbish. The collectors shall keep such vehicles clean,
sanitary, neatly painted and in good running order, and shall wash, clean and
disinfect all such vehicles at least once a week. Each vehicle shall be
equipped with a tight metal body, or, if a wooden body, shall be metal lined so
as to be watertight, and each vehicle shall at all times be provided with a
suitable cover securely fastened in such a manner as to retain dust and prevent
the scattering or dropping of rubbish or garbage upon public or private
property. (1963 Code § 8-414)
8-4-15: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall, upon conviction
thereof, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to
section 1-4-1 of this code. (1963 Code § 8-415)
TITLE 9
BUILDING REGULATIONS
Building Codes And Regulations   1
Numbering Buildings   2
Fences   3
CHAPTER 1
BUILDING CODES AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
9-1-1: Building Codes Adopted
9-1-2: Certificates Of Occupancy
9-1-3: Building Permits
9-1-1: BUILDING CODES ADOPTED 1 :
   A.   It is hereby adopted for use by the City of Craigmont the most current
version of The International Building Code, The International Residential Code,
The Idaho State Plumbing Code, and the National Electrical Code, all as adopted
by the State of Idaho, including all appendices thereto, and the same is hereby
adopted and incorporated as though fully set forth at length herein. The
adopted versions of the foregoing codes shall be deemed superseded by
successive versions of such codes as they are adopted or approved by the Idaho
Building Code Board effective on any date such codes are made effective by the
Idaho Building Code Board.
   B.   The City Clerk shall maintain not less than one (1) duly certified copy
of the most current version of The International Building Code, The
International Residential Code, The Idaho State Plumbing Code, and The National
Electrical Code at the office of the City Clerk for use and examination by the
public during normal business hours, in accordance with Idaho Code Section 50-
901. (2010 Code; amd. Ord. 418, 2-6-2018, eff. 2-6-2018; Res. 1058, - - )
 
Notes
1 1. IC §§ 39-4101, 39-4116.
9-1-2: CERTIFICATES OF OCCUPANCY:
   A.   Certificate Required: It is unlawful to use or occupy or permit the use
or occupancy of any building or premises, or both, or part thereof hereafter
created, erected, changed, converted or wholly or partly altered or enlarged in
its use or structure, until a certificate of occupancy shall have been issued
therefor by the City building inspector stating: that the proposed use of the
building or land conforms to the requirements of this chapter; that a stamped
certification from a licensed design professional has been submitted to the
City Clerk-Treasurer stating that the stormwater system was constructed in
accordance with the approved design and is functioning properly; and that the
building, proposed use of the building and land conforms to all other
conditional provisions that may have been imposed.
   B.   Temporary Certificate: A temporary certificate of occupancy may be
issued by the building inspector for a period not exceeding six (6) months
during alterations or partial occupancy of a building pending its completion.
   C.   Fees And Charges: The City Council shall establish by resolution a
schedule of fees and charges for occupancy permits.
   D.   Records Kept: The City Clerk-Treasurer shall maintain a record of all
certificates of occupancy, and copies shall be furnished upon request to any
person as provided by law.
   E.   Limitations And Restrictions:
      1.   Failure to obtain a certificate of occupancy shall be a violation of
this section.
      2.   Certificates issued on the basis of plans and applications approved
by the building inspector authorize only the use and arrangement set forth in
such approved plans and applications or amendments thereto, and no other use,
arrangement or construction. Use, arrangement or construction contrary to that
authorized shall be deemed a violation of this section.
   F.   Violation And Penalty: In addition to taking whatever criminal action
allowed by law, the City Attorney may take steps to civilly enjoin any
violation of this section. Penalties for failure to comply with or violations
of the provisions of this section shall constitute a misdemeanor punishable by
fine or imprisonment as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. Each day such violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. The landowner, tenant, subdivider, builder, public official
or any other person who commits, participates in, assists in or maintains such
violation may be found guilty of a separate offense. Nothing contained in this
section shall prevent the City Council or any other public official or private
citizen from taking such lawful action as is necessary to restrain or prevent
any violation of this section or of the Idaho Code. (2010 Code)
9-1-3: BUILDING PERMITS:
   A.   Permit Required: It shall be unlawful to construct, alter, or demolish,
or use any building or structure, including fences, within the City, nor shall
any excavation commence or be completed, nor shall any foundation, footing or
other base or arrangement be made preliminary to any contemplated construction
without first having obtained a permit to do so from the City.
   B.   Time Limit For Commencement Of Work: All permits for construction,
demolition, or alteration, including fences, must have work commenced within
sixty (60) days of the date of issuance of the permit, or the permit becomes
null and void. All permits expire after a period of one year unless a request
is made in writing to the City Council and the City Council, upon payment of
applicable fees, may grant six (6) month extensions.
   C.   Fees And Penalties Set By Resolution: If fees for building permits are
established independently from the fees provided in the adopted Building Code,
such fees for building permits shall be established by resolution of the City
Council. The City Council may also establish by resolution penalty fees for
constructing (or starting construction of) a building without an approved
building permit.
   D.   Time Limit For City Review And Decision: The City Council shall fix by
resolution the minimum number of days required by the City to review and issue
or deny a building permit.
   E.   Scale Map: A request for a building permit shall be accompanied by a
scale map or drawing showing actual dimensions of the lot or parcel, the
location and size of any building and such other information as may be
requested by the City.
   F.   Proof Of Compliance: A request for a building permit shall be
accompanied by proof in writing that all required fees imposed by other public
agencies have been paid and other conditions imposed by other public agencies
with jurisdiction have been met. (2010 Code)
CHAPTER 2
NUMBERING BUILDINGS
SECTION:
9-2-1: Numbering Required; Procedure
9-2-2: Method Of Assigning Numbers
9-2-3: Plat And Schedule Of Numbers
9-2-1: NUMBERING REQUIRED; PROCEDURE:
All buildings fronting on all streets in the territorial limits of the city
shall be numbered with plain, distinct figures not less than three inches (3")
in length, placed at some conspicuous portion on the front of such buildings;
such numbering to be as follows:
   A.   Former Towns Of Ilo And Vollmer: In that portion of the city comprising
the former town of Ilo and additions, and that portion of the former town of
Vollmer lying southeast of the Camas Prairie Railroad, and that portion of the
town of Vollmer fronting on the main street of the former town of Ilo as
extended to the intersection of the same with Prairie Avenue, and Main Street
of the former town of Vollmer, numbering shall be a follows:
      1.   The intersection of Main Street and Division Street in the former
town of Ilo shall be the place of beginning. On all streets running north and
south from Main Street, the first number on each street shall be 100 and up
through the first block, 200 and up through the second block, and so on
consecutively therefrom, north and south to the city limits as the same are now
or may hereinafter be constituted and laid out; even numbers to be on the west
side of the street, and odd numbers on the east side thereof. On all streets
running east and west from Division Street, the first number shall be 010 and
up through the first block, 100 and up through the second block, and so on,
numbered consecutively to the city limits as the same are now or may
hereinafter be constituted and laid out; even numbers to be on the north side
of the street, and odd numbers to be on the south side thereof.
      2.   All streets running north from Main Street shall have the word
"North" prefixed to their names, and all streets running south from Main Street
shall have the word "South" prefixed to their names. All streets running east
from Division Street shall have the word "East" prefixed to their names, and
all streets running west from Division Street shall have the word "West"
prefixed to their names.
   B.   Portion Of Former Town Of Vollmer: In that portion of the city
comprising that part of the former town of Vollmer lying south of the south
line of Boulevard Avenue and west of the west line of Ransdell Road, and north
to the south line of Front Street, numbering shall be as follows:
      1.   The main street of the former town of Vollmer shall be known as East
Main Street.
      2.   Commencing in block 36 of the former town of Vollmer fronting on
Prairie Avenue and fronting on Front Street, and block 23 of the former town of
Vollmer fronting on Villard Avenue and running southeast therefrom, the first
number on each street shall be 200 and up through the first block, 300 and up
through the second block, and so on consecutively therefrom southeasterly to
the intersection of said streets and avenues with Ransdell Road. Commencing in
block 21 of Vollmer fronting on Florence Avenue, the first number on the street
shall be 400 and up through the first block, 500 and up through the second
block, and so on consecutively therefrom southeast to the intersection of
Florence Avenue with Ransdell Road. Commencing in block 15 of the former town
of Vollmer fronting on Eaves Avenue, the first number on the street shall be
500 and up through the first block, 600 and up through the second block, and so
on consecutively therefrom southeasterly to the intersection of Eaves Avenue
with Ransdell Road; even numbers shall to on the northeast side of the street,
and odd numbers to be on the southwest side thereof.
      3.   On all streets running northeast from Front Street, the first number
on each street shall be 400 and up through the first block, 500 and up through
the second block, and so on consecutively northeast to their intersection with
Ransdell Road or Boulevard Avenue; even numbers to be on the northwest side of
the street, and odd numbers to be on the southeast side thereof.
   C.   Vollmer's First Addition:
      1.   In that portion of the city of Vollmer known as Vollmer's first
addition, the streets running east and west and connecting as continuations of
Eaves Avenue, Florence Avenue, Villard Avenue and Norma Avenue shall be
numbered as continued blocks of the avenues with which they connect.
      2.   Commencing at the intersection of Boulevard Avenue and Ransdell
Road, Ransdell Road running north and south from Boulevard Avenue, the first
number on Ransdell Road shall be 100 and up through the first block, 200 and up
through the second block, and so on consecutively from north and south to the
city limits as the same are now or may hereinafter be constituted and laid out;
even numbers to be on the west side of the street, and odd numbers to be on the
east side thereof. That portion of Ransdell Road lying north of Boulevard
Avenue shall have the word "North" prefixed of its name, and that portion of
Ransdell Road running south from Boulevard Avenue shall have the word "South"
prefixed to its name.
   D.   Farris Addition And Laufer Subdivision: In that portion of the town of
Vollmer lying north of Boulevard Avenue and including Boulevard Avenue, the
Farris addition and the Laufer subdivision to the city of Craigmont, each
street running east from Division shall be numbered 100 and up through the
first block, 200 and up through the second block, and so numbered consecutively
east to the city limits as the same are now or may hereinafter be constituted
and laid out; even numbers to be on the north side of the street, and odd
numbers to be on the south side thereof. Each street running north from
Boulevard Avenue shall be numbered 100 and up through the first block, 200 and
up through the second block, and so on consecutively north to the city limits
as the same are now or may hereinafter be constituted and laid out; even
numbers to be on the west side of the street, and odd numbers to be on the east
side thereof. (1963 Code § 9-701)
9-2-2: METHOD OF ASSIGNING NUMBERS:
From the intersection of Second Avenue and Main Street of the former town of
Ilo, east to and including that portion of the town of Vollmer fronting on the
main street of the former town of Ilo as extended to the intersection of the
same with Prairie Avenue and the main street of the former town of Vollmer, a
number shall be assigned to every twelve and one-half feet (121/2'), but less
than fifty feet (50'), the lowest designated number shall be assigned to the
building. In the instance of a building or a residence and yard covering
seventy five feet (75') and thus having three (3) numbers designated, the
middle number shall be assigned to the building or residence. (1963 Code § 9-
702)
9-2-3: PLAT AND SCHEDULE OF NUMBERS:
It shall be the duty of the person designated by the city council for such
purpose to assign a number to each and every tract, piece and parcel of land
within the limits of the city and to make a plat of all the streets of the city
on which the numbers so assigned shall be shown; and when said plat and
schedule of numbers have been made, and the same shall be filed with the clerk-
treasurer for a permanent record; then it shall be the duty of the clerk-
treasurer to furnish the owner or occupant of any premises bearing a number in
accordance herewith a certificate designating such number. (1963 Code § 9-703)
CHAPTER 1
FENCES
SECTION:
9-3-1: Definitions
9-3-2: Fence Standards; Penalties
9-3-3: Conflicts Between This Chapter And Land Use Planning Ordinances
9-3-1:   DEFINITIONS:
The following terms shall have the following meanings as used in this chapter:
 
CORNER LOT:                         A lot adjacent to an intersection of two
                                    (2) or more public streets.
                                    A barrier, railing, wall, lattice or other
                                    upright exterior structure more than
                                    eighteen inches (18") in height constructed
                                    for the purpose or with the effect of
                                    enclosing, screening, or restricting access
                                    or egress to any lot or any portion
                                    thereof. Except where otherwise provided in
                                    this chapter, regulations governing the
                                    height, location and opacity of fences
                                    shall apply to hedges, plantings,
                                    vegetation or landscaping placed,
                                    maintained or used in lieu of a fence or in
                                    combination with a fence. The term fence
                                    shall also include, but is not limited to,
FENCE, OPEN FENCING, SOLID FENCING: any and all component parts and portions of
                                    a fence, including but not limited to the
                                    base, footings, supporting columns, posts,
                                    braces, gates, structural members,
                                    fixtures, extensions or any other of its
                                    appurtenances. "Open fencing" means fencing
                                    that is constructed in such a way that no
                                    more than twenty percent (20%) of the
                                    surface area of the fence obstructs a view
                                    through the fence from a position
                                    perpendicular to the fence. "Solid fencing"
                                    means fencing that is constructed in such a
                                    way that more than twenty percent (20%) of
                                    the surface area of the fence obstructs a
                                    view through the fence from a position
                                    perpendicular to the fence.
 
 
              An open, unoccupied space on a lot facing or abutting a public
FRONT YARD:   street and extending from the front of the lot to the front of
              the principal building, between the side lot lines.
INTERIOR LOT: A lot other than a corner lot.
              Any platted lot, tract or other parcel of land held under private
LOT:          ownership situated in whole or in part within the city of
              Craigmont. The term lot shall exclude all lands owned by the city
              or by any governmental entity.
MAINTAIN:     To cause or enable a condition or thing to continue or to remain
              unchanged from its current condition or status.
              A space unoccupied by the principal structure on a lot extending
REAR YARD:    for the full width of the lot between a principal structure and
              the rear lot line.
              An open unoccupied space on the same lot with the building,
SIDE YARD:    situated between the building and a side line of the lot, and
              extending from the front yard to the rear yard. (Ord. 446, 5-7-
              2024)
 
9-3-2:   FENCE STANDARDS; PENALTIES:
   A.   Compliance With Chapter: No fence may be placed, erected, constructed,
or maintained in whole or in part on any lot in any zoning district except in
compliance with this chapter..
   B.   Fences Encroaching On Public Property Prohibited: No fence, or any
portion thereof, may be placed, erected, constructed, or maintained such that
any portion of thereof encroaches upon any public property, street, sidewalk,
alley or right-of-way unless authorized by the city or applicable governmental
agency with jurisdiction.
   C.   General Standards: The owner of a lot whereupon any fence is located:
1) shall cause such fence to be placed, erected, constructed and maintained in
a structurally sound and safe condition so as to not endanger life or property;
and b) shall not allow such fence to become a nuisance.
   D.   Limitations On Fencing Within Traffic Vision Triangle: Fencing over
three feet (3') in height shall not be placed, erected, constructed or
maintained in any vision triangle, said height being measured from the existing
center line street elevation within the vision triangle. The term "vision
triangle" is defined as the triangular area at the intersection of two (2)
streets adjacent to any lot, including a corner lot, in which the placement,
erection, construction or maintenance of fencing or other improvements therein
may cause a traffic hazard by limiting or obstructing the sight distance of
motorists entering or leaving the intersection, said triangular area being
measured from the intersection of the edges of said two (2) adjacent streets
forty feet (40') along each street and connecting the two (2) points with a
straight line. The edge of the street shall be defined as the curb or the outer
edge of the maintained roadway if no curb is installed. Driveways are not
considered roadways for this definition.
   E.   Compliance With Other Laws; Building Permits: In addition to the
provisions of this chapter, all fences are subject to and shall be placed,
erected, constructed and maintained in compliance with all other applicable
laws, regulations, codes and ordinances, including but not limited to all
applicable city building codes and permitting requirements.
   F.   Removal Of Fencing Encroaching On Public Property Or Visual Triangle:
In addition to all other remedies of the city provided in this chapter or as
otherwise provided by law, which shall be cumulative, the city may remove any
fencing placed, erected, constructed or maintained in violation of sections (B)
or (D) of this section at the lot owner's expense and without any compensation
to the lot owner if the lot owner fails to remove said non-compliant fence
within seven (7) days after the city's service of a written notice on the lot
owner ordering removal of the non-compliant fence. Service of any such written
notice on the lot owner may be accomplished by personal service, in which case
service is effective on the date of personal service, or by certified mail
addressed to the lot owner at the lot owner's mailing address as shown on the
records of Lewis County Assessor for mailing of real property tax notices for
said lot, in which case service is effective as of the date of the city's
deposit of the written notice in the US Mail. Provided, however, that nothing
herein is intended to, nor shall it, affect the city's right to remove any such
non-compliant fence in the event of an emergency or imminent danger or threat
to persons or property.
   G.   Prohibited Fencing Materials:
      1.   Electric, concertina, barbed or razor wire fences in all zoning
districts shall be prohibited excepting:
         a.   Livestock containment areas for horses or other permitted farm
animals permitted in the applicable zoning district may utilize electric or
barbed wire fences.
         b.   Commercial and industrial zoning districts may utilize electric,
concertina, barbed or razor wire fencing, but only as the top section of the
fence. The beginning of said top section must be at least six feet (6') above
grade. This exclusion shall not apply along the front property line and the
side property lines within twenty feet (20') of the front property line for all
properties fronting a minor or major arterial roadway.
         c.   Public detention, correctional or penal facilities are exempted
from the prohibitions of this section (E)(1) regardless of the zoning district
in which they are situated.
      2.   The following materials shall not be utilized as component parts for
any fence:
         a.   Boxes or cardboard.
         b.   Sheet or corrugated metal.
         c.   Broken or decayed wood.
         d.   Broken masonry blocks.
         e.   Plywood.
         f.   Cinder or concrete blocks.
         g.   Hubcaps.
         h.   Hazardous materials.
         i.   Loose or unaffixed materials that cause or allow any portion of
the fence to move or shift due to natural forces or physical contact.
         j.   Other materials not designed or intended for use in fencing.
   H.   Additional Fence Standards/Setbacks: Fences shall be placed, erected,
constructed and maintained in compliance with the following additional
standards as applicable:
      1.   Residential District Zones: The following standards shall apply to
fences in all residential zoning districts (Zoning Districts R-1 and R-2):
         a.   Interior Lots:
            (1)   Front Yard Property Line And Setback Area:
               Open Fencing Height: Maximum four feet (4'), unless otherwise
limited to a maximum of three feet (3') in vision triangle areas.
               Solid Fencing Height: Maximum three feet (3').
               Setback: Five feet (5') from an existing curb with no sidewalk
or flush along the edge of an existing sidewalk.
            (2)   Interior Side And Rear Property Line And Setback Area:
               Open Fencing Height: Maximum six feet (6') along the rear
property line and the side property line. Except that, as the fence runs along
the side property line, once it reaches twenty feet (20') from the front
property line, the maximum height is four feet (4'), unless otherwise limited
to a maximum of three feet (3') in vision triangle areas.
               Solid Fencing Height: Maximum six feet (6') along the rear
property line and the side property line. Except that, as the fence runs along
the side property line, once it reaches twenty feet (20') from the front
property line, the maximum height is three feet (3').
               Setback: No setback from either the side or the rear property
line.
         b.   Corner Lots:
            (1)   Front Yard Property Line And Setback Area:   
               Open Fencing Height: Maximum four feet (4'), unless otherwise
limited to a maximum of three feet (3') in vision triangle areas.
               Solid Fencing Height: Maximum three feet (3').
               Setback: Five feet (5') from an existing curb with no sidewalk
or flush along the edge of an existing sidewalk.
            (2)   Interior Side And Rear Property Line And Setback Area:
               Open Fencing Height: Maximum six feet (6') along the rear
property line and the interior side property line. Except that, as the fence
runs along the side property line, once it reaches twenty feet (20') from the
front property line, the maximum height is four feet (4'), unless otherwise
limited to a maximum of three feet (3') in vision triangle areas.
               Solid Fencing Height: Maximum six feet (6') along the rear
property line and the interior side property line. Except that, as the fence
runs along the interior side property line, once it reaches twenty feet (20')
from the front property line, the maximum height is three feet (3').
               Setback: No setback from either the side or the rear property
line.
            (3)   Side Yard Line And Setback Area Adjoining A Street:
               Open And Solid Fencing Height: Maximum four feet (4') along the
side property line, unless otherwise limited to a maximum of three feet (3') in
vision triangle areas.
               Setback: Five feet (5') from an existing curb with no sidewalk
or flush along the edge of an existing sidewalk.
         c.   Maximum Height: For purposes of this section (H), the term
maximum height shall mean the maximum height of the fence above the grade as
measured at the point/line upon which the fence shall sit, and includes
lattices and berms. Additional height shall be allowed for arbors, arches and/
or other architectural appurtenances extending over gates and/or other
entryways, as well as gateposts, said appurtenances and gateposts not exceeding
six feet (6') maximum height.
      2.   Commercial And Industrial Zones: The following standards shall apply
to fences in all commercial, commercial-industrial and industrial zoning
districts (Zoning Districts C, l-C, and I):
         a.   Interior And Corner Lots - All Yard Property Lines And Setback
Areas - Open Or Solid Fencing Height: Maximum eight feet (8'), unless otherwise
limited to a maximum of three feet (3') in vision triangle areas. No setbacks
are required.
   I.   Nonconforming Fences ; Removal of Noncompliant Fences ; Variances:
      1.   Nonconforming Fences. Except as provided in this subsection (I)(1),
fences that are nonconforming for any reason, but which were in place prior to
the adoption date of this chapter, may continue to be maintained in their
present location if maintained in good condition and repair and provided they
do not impede the safety of motorists or otherwise present a hazard. Safety
and/or hazardous issues shall be remedied immediately. Provided, however, that
any such nonconforming fence shall be brought into compliance with this chapter
in the event more than a total of twenty five horizontal lineal feet (25') of
the fence is replaced or reconstructed at any time after the adoption date of
this chapter.
      2.   Removal Of Noncompliant Fences: Fences placed, erected or
constructed after the adoption date of this chapter, or nonconforming fences
required to be in compliance with this chapter under subsection (l)(1) of this
section after the adoption date of this chapter, that do not comply with this
chapter shall immediately be removed by the lot owner at the lot owner's
expense. Prior to any removal, the affected lot owner shall be afforded an
opportunity for a hearing before the city council; said hearing must be
requested within ten (10) days of service of an order to remove a fence by the
city on the lot owner, which shall be served as provided in subsection (F) of
this section. Failure to request such a hearing will result in the lot owner
being required to immediately remove the noncompliant fence.
      3.   Variances: A lot owner who desires to place, erect or construct a
new fence, or who desires to replace or reconstruct any portion of any
nonconforming fence required to be compliance with this chapter under
subsection (l)(1) of this section, may request a variance from the city by
filing a written application for a variance with the city under the provisions
of Chapter 11, Title 10, Craigmont City Code, as amended, which shall apply to
any such request for variance, including but not limited to any appeal from any
decision of the city with respect the requested variance.
   J.   Violations; Penalties; Civil Remedies:
      1.   Violations; Penalties: Any person or corporation, whether owner,
lessee, principal agent, employee or otherwise, who violates any of the
provisions of this chapter or fails to comply with any lawful order of the city
issued under this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a
fine or jail, or both, as provided for misdemeanors under Idaho Code § 18-113,
as amended.
      2.   Civil Remedies; Public Nuisance: Any violation of this chapter by
any person or lot owner, or any fence maintained in violation of this chapter,
is hereby declared to be a public nuisance. The city reserves the right and may
pursue all civil remedies to abate said nuisance as provided under the laws of
the state of Idaho, including but not limited to institution of abatement
proceeding and the levy of special assessments against any lot whereon the
nuisance is situated to defray the cost or to reimburse the city for the cost
of abating said nuisance as provided under Chapters 3 and 10, Title 50, Idaho
Code, as amended. (Ord. 446, 5-7-2024)
9-3-3:   CONFLICTS BETWEEN THIS CHAPTER AND LAND USE PLANNING ORDINANCES:
In the event any portion of this chapter conflicts with any provision or
standards of any zoning ordinance, subdivision ordinance, building code or
other land use planning ordinance adopted by the city as related to
construction and maintenance of fences, the most restrictive provision or
standard shall control and govern with respect to the conflicting issue. (Ord.
446, 5-7-2024)

CHAPTER 1
TITLE, PURPOSE AND DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
10-1-1: Title
10-1-2: Authority
10-1-3: General Purposes
10-1-4: Interpretation; Minimum Standards
10-1-5: Severability
10-1-6: Definitions
10-1-1: TITLE:
This title shall be known as the ZONING ORDINANCE OF CITY OF CRAIGMONT, IDAHO.
It shall consist of the text contained in this title and a "zoning map" which
readily identifies the location of districts and subdistricts. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-
1981)
10-1-2: AUTHORITY:
This zoning title is adopted pursuant to authority granted by Idaho Code title
67, chapter 65, and article XII, section 2 of the Idaho constitution, as
amended and codified. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-1-3: GENERAL PURPOSES:
It is the intent of the city council to provide uniform, equitable and
reasonable standards to govern the usage of land and structures. In order to
promote the health, safety, and general welfare, the city seeks:
   A.   To ensure that adequate public facilities and services are provided to
persons at a reasonable cost.
   B.   To protect against fire, nuisances, and other hazards.
   C.   To conserve and stabilize property values.
   D.   To avoid air and water pollution.
   E.   To ensure that the development of land is commensurate with the
physical characteristics of the land.
   F.   To stabilize expectations regarding future development. (Ord. 297A, 5-
5-1981)
10-1-4: INTERPRETATION; MINIMUM STANDARDS:
In their interpretation and application, the provisions of this title are held
to be minimum requirements. Whenever the requirements of this title conflict
with the requirements of any other lawfully adopted rules, regulations,
ordinances or resolutions, that imposing the higher standards shall govern.
(Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-1-5: SEVERABILITY:
Should any section of this title be declared by the courts to be
unconstitutional or invalid, such decision shall not affect the validity of the
title as a whole or any other part. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-1-6: DEFINITIONS:
   A.   Words not defined herein shall be given the meanings ordinarily applied
to such words.
   B.   The present tense includes the future tense, the singular number
includes the plural and the plural number includes the singular.
   C.   The word "shall" is a mandatory requirement; the word "may" is a
permissive requirement; and the word "should" is a preferred requirement.
For the purpose of this title, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ACCESSORY USE OR BUILDING: A subordinate use or building customarily incident
to and located upon the same lot occupied by the main building or utilized for
the main purpose.
ACREAGE: Any tract or parcel of land which has not been subdivided or platted.
AGRICULTURE: The tilling of the soil, the raising of crops, horticulture,
livestock, farming, dairying or animal husbandry, including all uses
customarily accessory and incidental thereto, but not including
slaughterhouses, fertilizer works, boneyards or plants for the reduction of
animal matter.
ALLEY: A street or way shown on the official plat of the city or its additions
and designated therein as an alley.
ALTER; ALTERATION: Any change, addition or modification in construction or
occupancy.
APARTMENT HOUSE: A building or portion thereof used or intended to be used as
the home of three (3) or more families or households living independently of
each other.
AUTO WRECKING OR JUNKYARD: Any place where two (2) or more motor vehicles not
in running condition, or parts thereof, are stored in the open and are not
being restored to operation; any land, building or structure used for wrecking
or storing of such motor vehicles or parts thereof and including any farm
vehicles or farm machinery or parts thereof, stored in the open and not being
restored to operating condition; and including the commercial salvaging and
scavenging of any other goods, articles or merchandise.
AUTOMOBILE: A passenger vehicle.
AUTOMOBILE SERVICE STATION: Any premises used for supplying gasoline and oil at
retail direct to the customer, including accessories and services for
automobiles.
BASEMENT: A story partly or wholly underground. Where more than one-half (1/2)
of its height is above the average level of the adjoining ground, a basement
shall be counted as a story for the purpose of height measurement.
BILLBOARD: Any structure or portion thereof upon which are placed signs or
advertisements used as an outdoor display. This definition does not include any
bulletin boards used to display official court or public office notices, or a
sign advertising the sale or lease of the premises on which the sign is
located.
BLOCK: That property so designated on an official map of the city or part of
the city or bounded by a street or streets, and railroad right of way, or
unsubdivided acreage.
BOARDING HOUSE: A building or portion thereof, other than a hotel or barracks,
where meals and lodging for three (3) or more persons are provided for
compensation.
BREEZEWAY: A covered passageway between buildings which does not exceed ten
feet (10') in width and which has at least one side open, except for necessary
supporting columns.
BUILDING: Any structure having a roof supported by columns or walls, and
designed or intended for the shelter, support, enclosure or protection of
persons, animals or chattels.
BUILDING AREA: The buildable area of a lot is the space remaining after
adherence to the minimum open space requirements.
BUILDING HEIGHT: The vertical distance at the center of a building's principal
front measured from the established grade to the highest point of the roof,
beams, or in case of a flat roof, to the deckline or mansard, or to the center
height between eaves and ridges for gable, hip or gambrel rooflines. The height
may be measured from the average elevation of the finished sidewalk grade along
the front of the building.
BUILDING INSPECTOR: State certified building code inspector.
BUILDING LINE: For the purpose of this title, the building line is the same as
a front yard setback line.
BUILDING, PRINCIPAL: A building in which is conducted the main use of the lot
in which it is situated.
CARPORT: A structure attached or made a part of the main structure which is
open to the weather on at least two (2) sides, intended for the use of
sheltering not more than two (2) motor driven vehicles.
CLUB OR LODGE: An association of persons for the promotion of some common
object, members to which are admitted only on invitation and the chief activity
of which is not conducted for profit.
COMMISSION: Whenever the word "commission" is used herein, it shall be deemed
to refer to the planning and zoning commission of the city.
CONDITIONAL USE: See definition of Special Use.
CONVALESCENT HOME: A building and premises in and on which two (2) or more
sick, injured or infirm persons are housed or intended to be housed for
compensation.
COURT: An open, unoccupied space, other than a yard, on the same lot with a
building, and bounded on two (2) or more sides by a building, or buildings,
including the open space in a dwelling group providing access to the units
thereof.
CURB GRADE: The established elevation of the curb measured at the center of the
front of a building. Where no curb grade has been established, the city shall
establish such curb level or its equivalent for the purpose of this title.
DISTRICT: A section or sections of the incorporated area of the city for which
the regulations and provisions governing the use of buildings and land are
uniform for each class of use permitted therein.
DUPLEX: A building arranged or designed to be occupied by two (2) families.
DWELLING: A building or portion thereof, but not an automobile house trailer
designed exclusively for residential occupancy, including one-family, two-
family and multiple-family dwellings, but not including hotels, boarding and
lodging houses.
DWELLING, MULTIPLE: A building or portion thereof designed for occupancy by
three (3) or more families living independently of each other.
DWELLING, TWO-FAMILY: A building or portion thereof designed for occupancy by
two (2) families living independently of each other.
DWELLING UNIT: Two (2) or more rooms in a dwelling or apartment hotel designed
for occupancy by one family for living purposes and having only one kitchen.
EASEMENT: Authorization by a property owner for the use by another, and for a
specified purpose, of any designated part of his/her property.
ESTABLISHED GRADE: The sidewalk line grade at the front lot line as established
by the engineer or otherwise as given and established under the direction of
the city council.
EXISTING BUILDING: A building or structure or portion thereof lawfully existing
at the effective date hereof.
EXISTING USE: A use which lawfully occupied a building or land at the effective
date hereof.
FAMILY: Any number of individuals living together as a single housekeeping
unit.
FRONT PROPERTY LINE: The front lot line as shown upon the official plat of the
property in question.
FRONT YARD: Any open unoccupied space on the same lot with a building between
the front line of the building (exclusive of steps) and the front property
line.
FRONTAGE: All the property fronting on one side of a street between
intersecting or intercepting streets, or between a street and a right of way,
waterway, end of a dead end street, or city boundary, measured along the street
line. An intercepting street shall determine only the boundary of the frontage
on the side of the street which it intercepts.
GARAGE, PRIVATE: An accessory building for the storage of not more than three
(3) motor driven vehicles, of which not more than one shall be a commercial
vehicle of not more than two (2) ton capacity.
GRADE: The average of the finished ground level at the center of all walls of a
building. In case walls are parallel to, and within five feet (5') of, the
sidewalk, the ground level shall be measured at the sidewalk.
HOME OCCUPATION: An occupation carried on by the resident of a dwelling as a
secondary use within the same dwelling, and in connection with which there is
no display, no advertising and no selling of a commodity upon the premises.
HOTEL: A building designed for occupancy as the more or less temporary abiding
place of individuals who are lodged with or without meals, in which there are
six (6) or more guestrooms; and in which no provisions are made for cooking in
any individual room or suite.
INSTITUTION: An organization or society for some public or social purpose.
JUNKYARD: Any land, property, building, structure or combination thereof used
for the storage of junk, including scrap materials and metals, or wrecked
vehicles and machinery, whether or not the sale of such junk is made or
proposed.
KENNEL: Any lot or premises on which four (4) or more dogs more than four (4)
months of age are kept.
LABORATORY: A place devoted to experimental study such as testing and
analyzing. Manufacturing of a product or products is not to be permitted within
this definition.
LOADING AREA: An open area, other than a street or alley, used for the loading
or unloading of vehicles.
LODGING HOUSE: A building with not more than five (5) guestrooms where lodging
is provided for compensation pursuant to previous arrangement, but not open to
the public or transients.
LOT: Land occupied or to be occupied by a principal building and accessory
buildings including such open space as is required under this title and having
a frontage upon a street or alley, where not appearing on any dedicated plat by
number. But, where appearing on a dedicated official plat by a number, a lot
near the area and surface as shown on said plat and given a prescribed number
excepting whereby any lot is subdivided and occupied by separate buildings or
units, then the term "lot" shall include each subdivision of the dedicated lot.
LOT AREA: The total area of a lot computed exclusive of any portion of the
right of way of any public or private street.
LOT, CORNER: A lot on a corner fronting on two (2) intersecting streets.
LOT DEPTH: The horizontal distance between the front and rear lot lines,
measured along the median between the two (2) side lot lines.
LOT, INTERIOR: A lot other than a corner lot.
LOT LINES: The established division lines between parcels of land, public or
private.
LOT, THROUGH: A lot having frontage on two (2) parallel or approximately
parallel streets.
LOT WIDTH: The horizontal distance between the side lot lines measured at right
angles to the lot depth at a point midway between the front and rear lot lines.
MANUFACTURE: Preparation, making, treatment, or processing of articles as
merchandise.
MOBILE HOME: A detached single-family dwelling unit with the following
characteristics:
   A.   Designed for long term occupancy and containing sleeping
accommodations, a flush toilet, tub or shower, and kitchen facilities with
plumbing and electrical connections; and
   B.   Designed to be transported after fabrication on its own wheels, or on a
flatbed; and
   C.   Arriving on the site where it is to be occupied as a dwelling complete,
including major appliances and furniture, and ready for occupancy except for
minor and incidental unpacking and assembly operations, location on foundation
supports, and connection to utilities.
MOTEL: A tourist court.
MOTOR HOME: A vehicle designed to be driven and used for human habitation.
NONCONFORMING USE: A building or land occupied by a use which does not conform
with the regulations of the use district in which it is situated.
NURSERY SCHOOL: A school used exclusively for the daytime care of preschool age
children.
NURSING HOME OR REST HOME: A private hospital for the care of children, the
aged or infirm, or a place of rest for those suffering bodily disorders, but
not including facilities for the treatment of sickness or injuries or for
surgical care.
PARKING AREA, PRIVATE: An open area, other than a street or alley, used for the
parking of the automobiles or unoccupied camping trailer of an occupant of a
dwelling.
PARKING AREA, PUBLIC: An open area, other than street, used for the temporary
parking of more than four (4) automobiles and available for public use, whether
free, for compensation or as an accommodation for client or customers.
PARKING LOT: An open lot or parcel of land used for the storage of motor
vehicles capable of being moved under their own power and exclusive of lots or
parcels of land used for the purpose of dead storage, auto wrecking or
exhibition for sale.
PARKING, OFF STREET: An area adequate for parking an automobile with room for
opening doors on both sides, together with property related access to a public
street or alley and maneuvering room; but shall be located totally outside any
street or alley right of way.
PLANNED UNIT DEVELOPMENT: An area of land in which a variety of residential,
commercial, industrial, and/or other land uses are provided for under single
ownership and control, and are accommodated in a preplanned environment with
more flexible standards, such as lot sizes and setbacks, than those
restrictions that would normally apply under this title.
PORCH: A roofed entrance to a building, projecting out from the wall or walls
at the main structure and commonly open in part to the weather.
PREMISES: Land and/or buildings or other improvements thereon.
PUBLIC BUILDING: A building owned or used by the federal, state, county or city
government or any political subdivision thereof.
PUBLIC GARAGE: Any premises used for the storage or use of more than three (3)
motor vehicles, or where such vehicles are repaired or kept for hire, use or
sale.
REAR YARD: An open unoccupied space on the same lot with a building between the
rear line of the building and the rear line of the lot.
SCHOOL, ELEMENTARY OR HIGH: An institution which offers instructions in the
several branches of learning and study required to be taught in the public
schools by the educational code of the state of Idaho. High schools include
junior and senior.
SETBACK LINE: A line within a lot paralleling the street line, between which
lines the construction of buildings is prohibited.
SIDE YARD: An open unoccupied space on the same lot as the building between the
side wall line of the buildings and the side lines of the same lot.
SIGN, OUTDOOR ADVERTISING: A sign of any type or material, installed and placed
for outdoor advertising purposes.
SINGLE-FAMILY DWELLING: A building arranged or designed to be occupied by not
more than one family.
SPECIAL USE: An activity specified by this title as a principal or an accessory
use, permitted when authorized by the city council and subject to certain
conditions.
STABLE, PRIVATE: A detached accessory building for the keeping of horses owned
by the occupants of the premises and not kept for remuneration, hire or sale.
STORY: That portion of a building included between the surface of any floor and
the surface of the floor next above it, or if there be no floor above it, then
the space between such floor and ceiling next above it.
STORY, HALF: A story under a gable, hip or gambrel roof, the wall plates of
which, on at least two (2) opposite exterior walls, are not more than four feet
(4') above the floor of such story.
STREET LINE: The property line or boundary between a street and abutting
property.
STRUCTURE: Anything constructed or erected, except fences, the use of which
requires permanent location on the ground or attached to something having a
permanent location on the ground.
TERRACE, OPEN: A level and rather narrow plane or platform which, for purposes
of this title, is located adjacent to one or more faces of the main structure
and which is constructed not more than four feet (4') in height above the
average level of the adjoining ground.
THIS TITLE: Wherever the term "this title" is used herein, it shall be deemed
to include not only the provisions of this title, but all amendments to this
title as the same may hereafter from time to time be adopted.
TOURIST COURT: A group of attached or detached buildings, including auto
courts, motels or motor lodges, containing individual sleeping or living units,
designed for or used by tourists or transients, with garage attached or parking
space conveniently located to each unit.
TRAILER: A vehicle without motive power used for human habitation, including a
trailer coach or house trailer designed to be drawn by a motor vehicle.
TRAILER CAMP, AUTOMOBILE: Any premises occupied or designed to accommodate more
than one automobile house trailer.
TRAILER COACH AND MOBILE HOME PARK: Any plot of ground which is prepared for
occupancy by more than one trailer coach or mobile home, to be occupied for
dwelling purposes and located thereon regardless of whether or not a charge is
made for such accommodations.
TRAILER COACH AND MOBILE HOME SPACE: A plot of ground within a trailer coach
park.
VARIANCE: A modification of the regulations of this title where application of
the provisions of this title would cause undue and unnecessary hardship in view
of certain facts and conditions applying to a specific parcel of property. A
variance is not to be considered a right and is not to conflict with the public
interest. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 2
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
10-2-1: Permits Required
10-2-2: Contents Of Application
10-2-3: Approval Of Zoning Permit
10-2-4: Expiration Of Permit
10-2-5: Certificates Of Occupancy
10-2-6: Record Of Permits And Certificates
10-2-7: Failure To Obtain Permit Or Certificate
10-2-8: Schedule Of Fees, Charges And Expenses
10-2-9: Construction And Use, Compliance With Provisions
10-2-10: Complaints Regarding Violations
10-2-11: Penalties
10-2-1: PERMITS REQUIRED:
No building or other structure shall be erected, moved, added to or
structurally altered, nor shall any building, structure or land be established
or changed in use without a permit therefor issued by the city clerk-treasurer.
Permits shall be issued only in conformity with the provisions of this title.
(Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-2-2: CONTENTS OF APPLICATION:
Every application for a permit shall be filed in duplicate on a form provided
by the city clerk-treasurer. The application shall be signed by the owner or
applicant attesting to the truth and exactness of all information supplied on
the application. Each application shall clearly state that the permit shall
expire and may be revoked if work has not begun or is not substantially
completed within one year. At a minimum, the application shall contain the
following information: (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981; amd. 2010 Code)
   A.   Name, address and phone number of applicant;
   B.   Legal description of property;
   C.   Existing use;
   D.   Proposed use;
   E.   Zoning district;
   F.   Plan, drawn to scale, showing the actual dimensions and the shape of
the lot to be built upon; the exact size and location of existing buildings on
the lot, if any; and the location and dimensions of the proposed building(s) or
alteration;
   G.   Building heights;
   H.   Number of off street parking spaces or loading berths;
   I.   Number of dwelling units;
   J.   Proposed sewer and water facilities; and
   K.   Such other matters as may be necessary to determine conformance with,
and provide for, the enforcement of this title. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-2-3: APPROVAL OF ZONING PERMIT:
The city council shall act upon the application at its next regularly scheduled
meeting to deny or approve with or without conditions. Any conditions imposed
shall be transmitted to the applicant, in writing, within five (5) working days
of approval. All permits shall, however, be conditional upon the commencement
of work within one year. One copy of the plans shall be returned to the
applicant by the city clerk-treasurer after the building inspector shall have
marked such a copy either as approved or disapproved and attested to same by
his signature on such copy. One copy of plans, similarly marked, shall be
retained by the city clerk-treasurer. The city clerk-treasurer shall issue a
placard, to be posted in a conspicuous place on the property in question,
attesting to the fact that the use or alteration is in conformance with the
provisions of this title. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981; amd. 2010 Code)
10-2-4: EXPIRATION OF PERMIT:
   A.   Three Months: If the work for which a permit has been issued is not
commenced within three (3) months after the date of issuance, or such longer
period as the building inspector may authorize in writing, because of the
occurrence of conditions unforeseen at the time of the issuance, such permit
shall expire. A new permit shall be obtained before such work is commenced.
   B.   One Year: If the work for which a permit was issued is not completed
within one year from the date of issuance of the permit, or such longer period
as the building inspector shall authorize in writing, said permit shall expire.
No further work shall be undertaken until a new building permit has been
obtained. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-2-5: CERTIFICATES OF OCCUPANCY:
See section
9-1-2 of this code for requirements regarding certificates of occupancy. (Ord.
297A, 5-5-1981; amd. 2010 Code)
10-2-6: RECORD OF PERMITS AND CERTIFICATES:
The city clerk-treasurer shall maintain a record of all permits and
certificates of occupancy, and copies shall be furnished upon request to any
person. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-2-7: FAILURE TO OBTAIN PERMIT OR CERTIFICATE:
Failure to obtain a permit or certificate of occupancy shall be a violation of
this title. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-2-8: SCHEDULE OF FEES, CHARGES AND EXPENSES:
The city council shall establish a schedule of fees, charges and expenses and a
collection procedure for permits, amendments, appeals, variances, special use
permits, plan approvals and other matters pertaining to the administration and
enforcement of this title requiring investigations, inspections, legal
advertising, postage and other expenses. The schedule of fees shall be posted
in the office of the city clerk-treasurer and may be altered or amended only by
the city council. Until all applicable fees, charges and expenses have been
paid in full, no action shall be taken on any application or appeal. (Ord.
297A, 5-5-1981)
10-2-9: CONSTRUCTION AND USE, COMPLIANCE WITH PROVISIONS:
Permits or certificates of occupancy issued on the basis of plans and
applications approved by the building inspector authorize only the use, and
arrangement, set forth in such approved plans and applications or amendments
thereto, and no other use, arrangement or construction. Use, arrangement or
construction contrary to that authorized shall be deemed a violation of this
title. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-2-10: COMPLAINTS REGARDING VIOLATIONS:
Whenever a violation of this title occurs, or is alleged to have occurred, any
person may file a written complaint. Such complaint stating fully the causes
and basis thereof shall be filed with the city clerk-treasurer. The city clerk-
treasurer and building inspector shall properly record such complaint,
immediately investigate, and take action thereon as provided by this title.
(Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-2-11: PENALTIES:
The city attorney shall, in addition to taking whatever criminal action deemed
necessary, take steps to civilly enjoin any violation of this title. Penalties
for failure to comply with, or violations of, the provisions of this title
shall be as follows:
   Violation of any of the provisions of this title or failure to comply with
any of its requirements shall constitute a misdemeanor. Each day such violation
continues shall be considered a separate offense. The landowner, tenant,
subdivider, builder, public official or any other person who commits,
participates in, assists in or maintains such violation may be found guilty of
a separate offense. Nothing herein contained shall prevent the city council or
any other public official or private citizen from taking such lawful action as
is necessary to restrain or prevent any violation of this title or of the Idaho
Code. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
CHAPTER 3
ZONING DISTRICTS AND MAP
SECTION:
10-3-1: Districts Established
10-3-2: Subdistricts
10-3-3: Boundaries Established On Zoning Map
10-3-1: DISTRICTS ESTABLISHED:
For the purpose of this title, lands within the incorporated area of the city
are hereby classified into categories termed "zoning districts", as follows:
 
R-1 Single- and two-family residential
R-2 Multiple-family residential
C   Commercial
I-C Light industrial-commercial
I   Industrial
T-A Transitional-agricultural
 
 
(Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-3-2: SUBDISTRICTS:
A subdistrict of any district may be created within planned unit development
boundaries, provided a planned unit development permit has been issued for said
development pursuant to chapter 9 of this title. The subdistrict shall be
designated by the suffix "PUD" added to the symbol of the parent district.
(Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-3-3: BOUNDARIES ESTABLISHED ON ZONING MAP:
   A.   Map Adopted: The boundaries of the districts and subdistricts shall be
shown on the "zoning map" as adopted by this title.
   B.   Changes; Notice And Hearing: Changes in boundaries of districts or
subdistricts shall be made by ordinance which amends the provisions of this
title and amends the "zoning map". Such changes shall come only upon public
notice and hearing as defined by Idaho Code section 67-6509. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-
1981)
CHAPTER 4
RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS
ARTICLE A. R-1 SINGLE- AND TWO-FAMILY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-4A-1: Description And Purpose
10-4A-2: Permitted Buildings And Uses
10-4A-3: Special Uses Permitted
10-4A-4: Density Standards
10-4A-1: DESCRIPTION AND PURPOSE:
The R-1 single- and two-family residential district is intended for low density
urban residential use. A stable, healthful environment combined with the full
range of urban services is the goal of this district. Central water and sewer
are required. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-4A-2: PERMITTED BUILDINGS AND USES:
In an R-1 district, the following buildings and uses are permitted, subject to
general provisions and exceptions set forth in this article, and regulations
set forth in
chapter 7 of this title:
   Accessory uses customarily incidental to a permitted use, such as private
garages or parking areas for noncommercial vehicles.
   Home occupations. Offices of professional persons and, customarily, home
occupants, if carried on in a part of the residence. The occupation must not
occupy over fifty percent (50%) of such residence building. Adequate off street
parking shall be provided. Signs for identification are limited to one, not to
exceed twelve (12) square feet. Signs may not be lighted.
   Mobile homes are to be converted to a permanent dwelling by being set on a
permanent type foundation adequate to permanently support the home, with
concrete footings the width of the mobile home at least every fifteen feet
(15') of the trailer's length. All wheels and other mechanisms necessary for
the mobility of the home shall be removed. When the foundation is not solidly
around the exterior walls of the mobile home, the area between the mobile home
and the ground must be skirted. The mobile home must have a minimum of five
hundred (500) square feet of floor space.
   One-family detached dwelling structures.
   Renting of rooms for lodging purposes; not more than two (2) rooms are to be
permitted per dwelling.
   Subsistence or hobby type gardening and horticultural activities. Also
related structures of less than eight hundred (800) square feet total area and
used solely for noncommercial purposes.
   Two-family attached dwellings (duplexes). (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-4A-3: SPECIAL USES PERMITTED:
The following uses may be authorized by the planning and zoning commission and/
or city council as special exceptions in residential areas:
   Churches and other religious or charitable organizations.
   Franchised and public utility and communication facilities.
   Hospitals, provided ambulance and delivery areas are obscured from area
residential view with a wall and/or comparable shrubbery six feet (6') in
height.
   Keeping of livestock and/or domestic poultry by a student as part of the
student’s membership or enrollment in 4-H, Future Farmers of America, or
similar nonprofit or school-sponsored agricultural education program subject to
all standards and conditions for such use established by the city.
   Nursery schools, daycare centers, private kindergartens, orphanages or
similar facilities, provided there is established and maintained in connection
therewith a fenced yard and screened playlot on or adjoining the premises with
a minimum of four hundred (400) square feet for each child.
   Parks and playgrounds.
   Private clubs or lodges and community assembly halls; provided, that any
building used for such purpose shall be at least fifty feet (50') from an
adjoining residentially used lot.
   Professional offices to the extent of one professional person per five
thousand (5,000) square feet of lot area.
   Public and governmental buildings serving as administrative offices.
   Public, private, and parochial schools, provided playfields (exclusive of
the building site) are provided at a minimum ratio of one acre per one hundred
(100) elementary school students.
   Railroad right of way, but not yards or other similar facilities.
   Rest, convalescent, or retirement homes.
   A.   Site development is to include adequate off street parking for
visitors, employees, loading and other services.
   B.   Open space is to be provided which creates a ratio of one thousand
(1,000) square feet for each bed in the facility.
   C.   No building shall be closer than forty feet (40') from any property
line. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981; amd. Ord. 448, 6-4-2024)
10-4A-4: DENSITY STANDARDS:
   A.   Building Height: Two (2) stories, but not over thirty five feet (35').
   B.   Lots:
      1.   Minimum Lot Area: Ten thousand five hundred (10,500) square feet for
a single detached dwelling, plus three hundred (300) square feet for each
additional dwelling unit.
      2.   Minimum Lot Depth: One hundred forty feet (140').
      3.   Minimum Lot Width: Seventy five feet (75').
      4.   Maximum Percent Of Lot Coverage: Forty percent (40%).
   C.   Yards:
      1.   Minimum Front Yard Depth: Twenty feet (20').
      2.   Minimum Side Yard Width:
         a.   Minimum side yard width shall be five feet (5') for a single-
family detached dwelling or six feet (6') in the case of a two- family attached
unit.
         b.   Minimum side yard width along the street side of a corner lot
shall be ten feet (10').
      3.   Minimum Rear Yard: Twenty feet (20'). (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
ARTICLE B. R-2 MULTIPLE-FAMILY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-4B-1: Description And Purpose
10-4B-2: Permitted Buildings And Uses
10-4B-3: Special Uses
10-4B-4: Density Standards
10-4B-1: DESCRIPTION AND PURPOSE:
The R-2 multiple-family residential districts are designed to provide sites for
multiple-family dwelling structures, and related uses, which will generally
serve as zones of transition between the nonresidential districts and the lower
density district. The R-2 district is provided to serve the limited need for
higher density residential buildings in an otherwise low density, single-family
community. Central water and sewer is required. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-4B-2: PERMITTED BUILDINGS AND USES:
In the R-2 district, the following uses are permitted, subject to the general
provisions set forth in this article and the regulations set forth in
chapter 7 of this title:
   Accessory uses permitted in an R-1 district.
   Multiple dwelling structures or groups of structures including triplex and
fourplex family dwelling structures and multiple unit apartments in which units
are rented on a permanent basis. Exception: Not including motels or other
facilities offered on a transient tenancy basis.
   Principal uses permitted in an R-1 district. See section
10-4A-2 of this title. (Ord. 297A, 5-5-1981)
10-4B-3: SPECIAL USES:
The following uses may be authorized by the planning and zoning commission and/
or city council as special exceptions:
   Any special use permitted in an R-1 district.
   Keeping of livestock and/or domestic poultry by a student as part of the
student’s membership or enrollment in 4-H, Future Farmers of America, or
similar nonprofit or school-sponsored agricultural education program subject to
all standards and conditions for such use established by the city.
   Mobile homes or trailer courts may be permitted. Each unit is considered a
separate dwelling under the laws of the city. All single mobile homes on lots
are to meet yard requirements of section
10-4A-4 of this title. Placement and use of trailers occupied by any person in
other than an approved trailer court must be so arranged as not to interfere
with the rights and privileges of adjacent property owners. Mobile homes in
this district must be of at least five hundred (500) square feet, set in
accordance with the international building code, as adopted by the city, or
placed on a permanent foundation and declared real estate; and a statement of
intent to declare the same real estate, recorded in the public records,
pursuant to Idaho Code.
